Title: Aphids in Sesame
Authors: G.   Sudhakar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    These are a major pest on sesame and pulses,
and are commonly known as aphids (Asuvini in Tamil). Aphids can cause 10-15%
yield loss in sesame, also known as gingelly. The nymphs and yellow-coloured adults
suck the plant sap. As a result of this, the crop growth is stunted and the
flowering and pod setting are affected. Typical symptoms of the damage caused
by this insect are yellowish discoloration and crinkling of leaves. The damage is
more severe in young shoots and buds.
    Aphids are found in groups on the under
surface of the leaves, tender shoots and growing tips. Ants are attracted to the
honey dew secretion that aphids release and can help in carrying the aphids
from one plant to another plant.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Apply the recommended dose of
    fertilizer</li>
    <li>Practice thinning of sesame and maintain an optimum population of 11 plants per square meter</li>
    <li>Follow the check basin method of
    irrigation by avoiding excess irrigation</li>
    <li>Prophylactic spray of neem oil @ 3 ml
    per litre of water</li>
    <li>Spray <em>Metarhizium&nbsp;anisopliae</em> and&nbsp;<em>Beauveria&nbsp;bassiana</em> @ 100
    ml / per acre</li>
    <li>Release 15,000 <em>Chrysopa</em> adults per acre</li>
    <li>Seed treatment with imidacloprid 21.4% FC @ 5 g per
    kg of seeds</li>
    <li>Spray imidacloprid 17.8% SL @ 1 ml per
    litre of water</li>
</ul>
SL &ndash; Soluble Liquid
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Aphis gossypii</em>
Images: a0cfb367-9807-4201-a956-946fac86cbe0.jpg, feb1cb66-c3a2-45b6-9dda-7275bd641b69.jpg

Title: Brown Planthopper
Authors: S.   Malarvannan
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The brown planthopper is a major
problem on rice, particularly in low land. In Tamil Nadu, it is known as
&ldquo;Pugaiyan&rdquo;. The adult has a brown body and chestnut brown eyes. Two forms of
panthopper, namely long winged and short winged, are seen. As a result of
feeding by both nymphs and adults at the base of the tillers, plants turn
yellow and dry up rapidly. This condition is called 'hopper burn', in which
circular patches of drying and lodging of matured plants is seen. If timely
control measures are not adopted it may cause up to 60% crop loss.
    The insect infests the rice crop at
all stages of plant growth. Nymphs and adults congregate at the base of the
plant above the water level. They damage rice directly through feeding and also
by transmitting two viruses, rice ragged stunt virus and rice grassy stunt
virus. Excessive use of&nbsp;urea&nbsp;and
certain chemicals can lead to outbreak by increasing the&nbsp;egg laying of the brown plant hopper
and by reducing populations of natural enemies.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Grow resistant/
    tolerant varieties like ADT 36, Co 46, Co 42, IR 36, Aruna</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Provide 30 cm
    rogue spacing at every 2.5 m to reduce the pest incidence. Avoid the use of
    excessive nitrogenous fertilizers. Control irrigation by intermittent draining.
    Grow Azolla to increase wolf spider population, which will control BPH.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Set up light
    traps @ 5 / acre between 7-9 pm. Install 20 yellow pan traps during the day
    time</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Conserve
    natural enemies like wolf spider, mirid bugs etc.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Avoid chemicals
    like fenthion and quinalphos which can cause resurgence of the pest</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>If the pest
    persists after adopting the above management practices then chemical control
    may be necessary. Drain water from the field then spray any one of the
    following chemicals: buprofezin 25% EC @ 625 ml/ha, imidacloprid 17.8 SL @ 100
    ml/ha, thiamethoxam 20 % WDG @ 100 g/ha, neem oil 3% @ 15 lit/ha or 25 kg of neem
    seed kernel powder in 600 litres of water for 1 ha.</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Nilaparvata lugens</em>
Images: 14b8ba1a-6f2d-4797-8a5d-d6c1179c3e9b.jpg, f25593f6-4f0b-4e2c-b532-2469fafcf0c0.jpg

Title: Chickpea Pod Borer
Authors: K. P Singh, S. A Pachkawade
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Female moths of the pod borer each lay about 300-350
eggs on the tender leaves and flower bracts of the plant. The eggs are creamy
white in colour. The incubation period is
4-5 days and the larval period is 22-27 days. Newly hatched
larvae feed on green leaves and later feed on flower buds and pods. Fully
grown larvae feed on the pods by making small circular holes. Half of the larvae body always remains outside
the pods. A single larva can damage up to 50-60 pods during its larval period.
    The chickpea pod borer causes serious
damage to chickpea crops with yield losses of up
to 50%. The infestation usually starts
on chickpea a fortnight after germination and becomes serious just after the
initiation of flower buds, especially when
coupled
with cloudy and humid weather.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Sowing
    early, especially short-duration varieties, helps to avoid pod borer damage in
    Northern India</li>
    <li>Intercropping
    coriander with chickpea provides nectar sources for adult parasitoids and
    improves the natural control of the pod borer</li>
    <li>After
    30 days of sowing, install pheromone traps @ 12 per hectare</li>
    <li>Erect
    bird perches @ 10-15/ha at flowering stage. Remove the perches before pod
    maturity.</li>
    <li>Spray
    5% NSKE at flowering stage</li>
    <li>Spray
    3 times with NPV250 LE @ 2.5 ml /litre of water at weekly intervals</li>
    <li>If
    chemicals are required, spray emamectin benzoate 5% SG @ 4 gm/10 litres of
    water</li>
</ul>
NSKE- Neem Seed Kernal Extract; NPV-
Nuclear Polyhedrosis Virus;
LE- Larval Equivalent; SG- Soluble
Granule; EC &ndash; Emulsifiable Concentrate
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Helicoverpa armigera</em>
Images: e23464e2-2e41-40a2-aa24-420bdb2e5569.jpg, 3c77929e-6dbb-4ca7-a57b-29b631fb9c48.jpg

Title: Button Shedding in Coconut
Authors: S.   Malarvannan
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Premature
button shedding is a very common problem observed on coconut. Buttons can be
shed after fertilization and some nuts are shed after setting. This is not
due to a single cause but may be due to combination of one or more factors.
The economic loss ranges from 10 to 20%.
    Shedding
of buttons and premature nuts may be due to one or more of the following:
excess acidity or alkalinity, poor drainage facilities, severe and prolonged
drought, genetic disorders, insufficient nutrients, improper pollination,
hormone deficiency, insect pests or poor management practices.
    The
following remedial measures can be followed to effectively manage this
problem:-
<ul>
    <li><strong>Rectification
    of soil pH</strong>-Excess acidity or alkalinity of soil may
    cause button shedding. If the soil pH is less than 5.5, the soil is too
    acidic. This could be overcome by adding lime. High alkalinity is indicated
    by soil pH higher than 8.0. This situation could be managed by adding gypsum.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li><strong>Lack of nutrition</strong>-Button
    shedding can occur as a result of inadequate manuring. The recommended dose
    of manurial schedules and proper time of application are important to
    minimise the button shedding. Soil application of 1.3 Kg urea, 2 Kg of Single
    Super Phosphate and 2 Kg of potash, mixed with 50 Kg of farmyard manure per
    palm. This can be followed by root feeding of Coconut tonic @ 40 ml in 160 ml
    of water per palm once in 6 months which will control the button shedding and
    enhance the yield.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li><strong>Irrigation management</strong>- Button
    shedding will be severe during March-April. Severe drought and / or
    insufficient irrigation aggravate the problem. Soil mulching with green
    fronds reduces evapo-transpiration and conserves soil moisture. Ensuring
    sufficient irrigation during summer and drainage during winter will lead to a
    sustainable yield.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li><strong>Hormone deficiency</strong>- Apply 0.5 ml
    of NAA (Planofix) mixed in 1 litre of water on the inflorescence. This
    prevents button shedding.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li><strong>Pests and Diseases</strong>- When young
    buttons are formed sucking pests start infesting which in turn attracts secondary
    fungal infections. Apply the recommended plant protection measures to ward
    off the problem.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li><strong>Boron deficiency or crown chokes disorder:</strong> Apply 200g of
    borax/palm/year in two splits.</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: 
Images: e003883b-35f0-4753-bba1-345d49e72a9d.jpg

Title: Citrus Canker
Authors: Bhavana   Kolhe
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Citrus
canker affects all above ground parts of the citrus tree. Rusty-brown spots called
cankers form on the leaves, twigs and shoots. The cankers on leaves develop a
distinctive bright yellow halo around them. Scabby cankers also appear on the
fruit. When conditions are highly favourable for infection, the disease can
cause shoot dieback, leaf drop and premature fruit drop. Growth of young trees
is severely affected because of the damage to new shoots.
    The
disease is caused by bacteria which attack the fruit, leaves and twigs of citrus.
Windbreaks help to reduce the wind speed and so lower the probability of
bacteria directly penetrating the stomata of the leaves. They also help to
reduce entry of bacteria via wind-induced injuries on foliage and fruit.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Deploy
    windbreaks on the perimeter of the orchard or between the rows</li>
    <li>
    Remove
    and burn the affected plant parts and clean the field</li>
    <li>
    Spray
    copper oxychloride, 25g per 10 litres of water
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Xanthomonas citri</em>
Images: 551730b7-ac7d-44e1-921c-9ffaad2d1553.jpg, 5a26f3b6-c9b0-4219-b90e-590b721edc53.jpg
Content:

Title: Citrus Psyllid
Authors: Charudatta D Thipse
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Psyllids are a serious
sucking pest of citrus. Psyllids extract large quantities of sap from the
plants, especially from new flush and flower buds. This causes curling of the leaves, distortion of shoots and
even stops growth. While sucking the sap, nymphs inject a
toxin that causes the plant tips to
dieback. A sugary substance coats the leaves. This may also be
found on the ground below the affected plant parts,
indicating heavy incidence of the pest. Brownish
adult citrus psyllids can be seen sitting in a row on the tender leaves. Heavy
infestation causes bud and fruit drop. Quality and quantity of fruit is
affected.
Psyllids are a serious
sucking pest of citrus. Psyllids extract large quantities of sap from the
plants, especially from new flush and flower buds. This causes curling of the leaves, distortion of shoots and
even stops growth. While sucking the sap, nymphs inject a
toxin that causes the plant tips to
dieback. A sugary substance coats the leaves. This may also be
found on the ground below the affected plant parts,
indicating heavy incidence of the pest. Brownish
adult citrus psyllids can be seen sitting in a row on the tender leaves. Heavy
infestation causes bud and fruit drop. Quality and quantity of fruit is
affected.
    Mriga
bahar variety (June-July) and Ambia bahar variety (January-February) flush is
more affected. Psyllids transmit the serious citrus greening disease which
causes devastating losses of citrus orchards.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Maintain good field sanitation by clipping, collecting and burning the
    previous year affected twigs</li>
    <li>Remove collateral host i.e. curry leaf plant. Avoid planting curry leaf
    plants near the citrus orchard.</li>
    <li>Avoid excessive application of nitrogenous fertilizers</li>
    <li>Avoid too much irrigation</li>
    <li>Observe and encourage the activity of ladybird beetles and aphid lions
    (Chrysopids)</li>
    <li>Release 10,000 Mallada eggs in the month of July for Mriga bahar and in
    March for Ambia bahar</li>
    <li>Spray 5% Neem Seed Kernal Extract (NSKE) or Azadirachtin 10,000 ppm @ 1ml
    / lit of water</li>
    <li>Spray Imidacloprid 17.8% SL @ 0. 4 ml or Acephate 75 % SP @ 2 g/ lit or
    Dimethoate 30 EC @2 ml / lit of water</li>
    <li>Time of spraying for Mriga bahar crop is mid-July to mid-August and for
    Ambia bahar crop is mid-March to mid-April depending on pest incidence.</li>
</ul>
<p>
SL &ndash; Soluble
Liquid; SP- Soluble Powder; EC- Emulsifiable Concentrate.</p>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Diaphorina citri</em>
Images: 18f57452-a553-4df7-af28-ae181ef416db.jpg, 974a62dd-0a09-44bc-a0ba-225aaead3ee1.jpg

Title: Coconut Basal Stem End Rot
Authors: R.   Rajkumar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    This chronic problem was first noticed in
Tanjore in Tamil Nadu and hence is sometimes known as Tanjore wilt disease. It
later spread to all coconut growing tracts of India. In the initial stages of
the disease, profuse bearing of nuts is noticed. The characteristic symptoms of
the disease are the exudation of reddish brown liquid through cracks, stem
discolouration and internal rotting up to the height of bleeding. In later
stages of the infestation, the decaying of tissues at the bleeding point and
the basal portion of the stem is observed and a reduction in nut size and nut
yield is seen. In rare cases, the bark of the stem peels off and causes
complete collapse of tree.
    This disease is caused by a fungus and can
cause an economic loss of up to 80%. It spreads mainly through root contact and
irrigation between diseased and healthy palms. Repeated ploughing and
uncontrolled flood irrigation also favours infection.
    <ul>
    <li>Remove and burn infected trees</li>
    <li>Avoid flood irrigation and repeated ploughing</li>
    <li>Intercrop with banana</li>
    <li>Apply 2 kg of lime and 3.5 kg Potash/palm</li>
    <li>Apply <em>Pseudomonas flourescens</em> (PF1) @ 100gms/palm/year + <em>Trichoderma viride</em> @100 g/palm/ year in
    soil</li>
    <li>Apply 200 g of Phosphobacteria and 200 g of Azotobacter mixed with 50 kg
    FYM/palm/year</li>
    <li>Apply 5 kg of Neem cake per palm per year. This bioagent is available in
    local agro input dealers and also in Depot of Agricultural Extension Centres.</li>
    <li>If chemical control is required, use root feeding: select an active
    absorbing root of pencil thickness and make a slanting cut in it. Dip this cut
    end into a polythene bag containing one of the following solutions:
    <ul>
        <li>Tridemorph 20% EC @ 10ml + 15 ml of water/tree</li>
        <li>Aureofunginsol&nbsp; 21% WP @ 1 g + 1 g
        of Copper Sulphate in 100 ml of water/tree</li>
    </ul>
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Ganoderma lucidum</em>
Images: 0878f364-ff9c-47b5-ad24-a2ed806c0165.jpg, b2c7afdb-b205-4015-8c54-9b2146114aa9.jpg
Content:
This chronic problem was first noticed in
Tanjore in Tamil Nadu and hence is sometimes known as Tanjore wilt disease. It
later spread to all coconut growing tracts of India. In the initial stages of
the disease, profuse bearing of nuts is noticed. The characteristic symptoms of
the disease are the exudation of reddish brown liquid through cracks, stem
discolouration and internal rotting up to the height of bleeding. In later
stages of the infestation, the decaying of tissues at the bleeding point and
the basal portion of the stem is observed and a reduction in nut size and nut
yield is seen. In rare cases, the bark of the stem peels off and causes
complete collapse of tree. This disease is caused by a fungus and can
cause an economic loss of up to 80%. It spreads mainly through root contact and
irrigation between diseased and healthy palms. Repeated ploughing and
uncontrolled flood irrigation also favours infection. <ul>
    <li>Remove and burn infected trees</li>
    <li>Avoid flood irrigation and repeated ploughing</li>
    <li>Intercrop with banana</li>
    <li>Apply 2 kg of lime and 3.5 kg Potash/palm</li>
    <li>Apply <em>Pseudomonas flourescens</em> (PF1) @ 100gms/palm/year + <em>Trichoderma viride</em> @100 g/palm/ year in
    soil</li>
    <li>Apply 200 g of Phosphobacteria and 200 g of Azotobacter mixed with 50 kg
    FYM/palm/year</li>
    <li>Apply 5 kg of Neem cake per palm per year. This bioagent is available in
    local agro input dealers and also in Depot of Agricultural Extension Centres.</li>
    <li>If chemical control is required, use root feeding: select an active
    absorbing root of pencil thickness and make a slanting cut in it. Dip this cut
    end into a polythene bag containing one of the following solutions:
    <ul>
        <li>Tridemorph 20% EC @ 10ml + 15 ml of water/tree</li>
        <li>Aureofunginsol&nbsp; 21% WP @ 1 g + 1 g
        of Copper Sulphate in 100 ml of water/tree</li>
    </ul>
    </li>
</ul> When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

Title: Cotton Whitefly
Authors: Charudatta D Thipse
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Whiteflies
suck sap from the cotton leaves, causing leaves to curl upwards. The leaves
turn pale yellow and have reduced vigour. The upper surface of the lower leaves
becomes shiny with a sugary secretion from the insect. Growth of black sooty
mould can be seen on these leaves. Lint from open bolls also gets contaminated
with these secretions.
    The
incidence of whiteflies is at its peak from September to November. We can see
the tiny whiteflies with milky white colour wings and yellow bodies sitting on
the under surface of tender leaves. High temperatures with scanty rainfall
situations increase the problem. Whiteflies can transmit cotton leaf curl virus
disease.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Maintain
    good field sanitation by destroying crop residues and weeds</li>
    <li>Avoid
    excessive use of nitrogenous fertilizers</li>
    <li>Avoid
    using synthetic pyrethroids</li>
    <li>Set
    up yellow pans or sticky traps for monitoring whitefly @ 15 yellow pans or
    sticky traps per hectare. Locally available empty yellow palmolein tins coated
    with grease/vaseline/castor oil on the outer surface may also be used.</li>
    <li>Scout
    the field to initiate pest management practices on the basis of the economic
    threshold level (ETL) of 5 &ndash; 10 flies per leaf before 9 AM</li>
    <li>Use
    Neem oil @ 750ml/ha or 5% Neem seed extract as an organic pest management
    measure</li>
    <li>Spray
    acetamiprid 20 SP 4 grams
    or diafenthiuron 50% SC at 12
    grams per 10 litres of water. Ensure proper coverage of
    the underside of the leaves during insecticidal spray to effectively reduce the
    whitefly population.</li>
</ul>
<p>
SP-
Soluble Powder, SC- Suspension concentrate</p>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Bemisia
tabaci</em>
Images: 148e0de7-786b-4031-acb8-02ec525a4b02.jpg, c8a52dc2-58e4-4e90-a255-e05bcc51053c.jpg

Title: Deficiency of Magnesium in Cotton Plant
Authors: Vaishali   Londase
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Magnesium is an
essential secondary nutrient&nbsp;making up&nbsp;0.2-0.4% of dry matter of cotton plants. It
is necessary for normal plant growth and is a core element in the chlorophyll molecules. In cotton
plants, magnesium deficiency appears first on the lower leaves in which green
leaves turns purple in colour. The middle and the older leaves turn red in
colour. The plant becomes stunted in appearance and its yield is reduced.
    Magnesium
(Mg) deficiency&nbsp;is a detrimental plant disorder that occurs most often in
strongly acidic, light and sandy soils where magnesium gets easily leached
away.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Due to the deficiency of magnesium, plants begin to degrade the
    chlorophyll in older leaves. To reduce this, use organic
    manure and compost manure.</li>
    <li>Apply homemade compost as mulch
    to prevent leaching during excessive rainfall</li>
    <li>Spray 100g magnesium sulphate with 20g lime in 10
    litres of water</li>
    <li>Spray 20g
    magnesium sulphate with 10g urea per litre of water with an interval of 15 days</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

    <li>Spray 20g
    magnesium sulphate with 10g urea per litre of water with an interval of 15 days</li>
</ul> When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

Title: False smut Disease of Paddy
Authors: G.   Sudhakar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    False smut is caused by a fungus and is also known as Lakshmi disease or
Oothupathi disease of rice.
The typical symptom of the disease is black fungal mycelium growth in paddy
grains which become covered with yellow fungal growth in the field. Mature
spores are orange and turn yellowish green or greenish black in colour. Only a few
grains in a panicle are usually infected and the rest are normal.
    This disease is more typical when the
farmer plants paddy crops.&nbsp; The affected
grain colour and low quality of grain and leads to a low market price of the
grain. The disease starts in scattered places and spreads quickly.&nbsp; It starts from shady areas and areas near bunds.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Avoid
    growing susceptible varieties like Co-43</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Early
    planting of paddy seedlings avoids disease incidence</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Collect
    the affected parts and burn them outside the field</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Apply hexaconazole 5% SC at 1ml/litres or chlorothalonil
    72% SC at 2gm/ litres</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Use
    a seed treatment of carbendazim at 2 grams per kg of paddy seeds</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Avoid
    spraying at the time of grain formation stage
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Ustilaginoidea virens</em>
Images: 6a9450eb-c7fc-4401-9925-174abb9646cb.jpg

Title: Fruit Rot and Dieback in Chillies
Authors: S.   Malarvannan
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Chilli fruit rot and dieback is a fungal
problem witnessed globally. This disease is observed at the flowering stage of
chilli growth. Flowers dry up resulting in
profuse shedding. The flower stalk shrivels. This drying up spreads from the flower stalks to the stem, resulting in dieback
of the branches and stem. The fungus causes necrosis of tender twigs
from the tip backwards, hence the name dieback. The branches wither. Partially affected plants bear a few fruits
which are of low quality.
    This is a fungal disease
which occurs on many vegetable crops but is most severe on chillies. If action is
not taken, the farmer will end up with poor and marginal crops. Seed treatments
are effective in
eliminating the seed-borne inoculum. Chemicals like zineb, copper oxychloride
and wettable sulphur not only reduce the disease incidence but also increase the
yield of fruits.
    <ul>
    <li>Use disease
    free seeds</li>
    <li>Use a seed
    treatment with <em>Trichoderma viride</em>
    @10g/kg to manage the disease in a biological way</li>
    <li>Alternatively,
    use a chemical seed treatment of thiram or captan 4g/kg</li>
    <li>Good control of
    the disease has been reported by spraying ziram 0.25%, captan 0.2% or a
    combination of zineb and copper oxychloride (e.g. Miltox 0.2%) three times</li>
    <li>The first
    spraying should be given just before flowering and the second at the time of
    fruit formation. The third spraying may be given a fortnight after second
    spraying</li>
</ul>
<p>
The chemical
control options above should be used&nbsp;as an alternative to biological seed treatment, not
as well as, to avoid killing the biocontrol agent <em>Trichoderma</em>.</p>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Colletotrichum capsici</em>
Images: aad07c33-a797-40f6-8a67-cdeab3f167f6.jpg
Content:

Title: Green Semilooper in Soybean
Authors: S. A Pachkawade
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The semilooper larva is green in colour with several
thin light lines running the length of the body. When crawling, it forms a
characteristic loop or hump so is known as the semilooper. The full grown larva
feeds on foliage, flowers and pods. In severe infestation, it defoliates the
plant leaving behind only midribs. The female moth lays tiny white creamy eggs
on the underside of the leaves or young stems. The eggs hatch 3-4 days later.
The newly emerged caterpillars feed on the lower surface of the upper canopy of
soybean leaves in a characteristic manner, leaving the top epidermis intact.
    The
semilooper feeds on soybean crops and causes yield losses up to 30-40%. It
affects the crop at the vegetative stage and if the infestation is at the
podding or flowering stage, it can cause considerable yield losses. Usually the
infestation occurs before late August and early September.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Practise
    deep summer ploughing</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Install
    bird perches at 20/ ha in the field</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Spray
    <em>Beauveria bassiana</em> 4 ml/litre of
    water during high humidity</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Spray
    5 % Neem Seed Kernel Extract (NSKE) at flowering stage as a preventive measure</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Spray
    quinalphos 25% EC at 30 ml or chlorpyriphos 20% EC @ 30 ml in 10 litres of
    water</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Chrysodeixis acuta</em>
Images: 9f3b2136-6568-4d89-a533-3877049f79a9.jpg, 38549298-b6d9-4d8c-ab5b-a8b2b61ab238.jpg

Title: Groundnut stem rot
Authors: T.   Aruna
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Germinating
seeds infected by groundnut stem rot are covered with masses of black spongy
fungi. This causes rapid wilting of the entire plant or its branches. The
development of white fungal threads can be seen on affected plant tissue,
particularly on the stem. The base of the plant turns yellow and
then&nbsp;wilts down. Mature plants may also be attacked. Lesions develop on
the stem below the soil and spread upwards along the branches. The whole collar
region becomes shredded and dark brown. Dried, dead branches can be easily
detached from the disintegrated collar region.
    Groundnut stem rot
is caused by a fungus.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Apply
    a deep covering of organic matter before planting</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Carry
    out non-dirting cultivation by avoiding movement of soil up around the
    base of plants</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Preventing
    accumulation of organic debris</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Rotate
    the groundnut crop with wheat, corn and soyabean</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Use
    a seed treatment of&nbsp;<em>Trichoderma viride</em>&nbsp;@
    4 g/kg seed and soil application of&nbsp;<em>Trichoderma viride</em>&nbsp;@2.5
    kg/ha, mixed with 50 kg farmyard manure or with organic amendments such as castor cake
    or neem cake or mustard cake @ 500 kg/ ha</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Alternatively,
    use a dry seed treatment of carbendazim or captan @ 2-3 g/kg of seed is
    effective.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>A
    mixture of fungicides viz., quintozene (e.g.&nbsp;Terraclor) plus etridiazole (e.g. Terrazole) @ 20 kg/ha plus 40
    kg/ha at pegging is also effective in controlling stem-rot diseases</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Sclerotium rolfsii</em>
Images: 2774f8c3-6b82-4966-abfc-ac8633a72fed.jpg, fb17c0b6-1a6f-4f5a-9ef5-dfecc8317bd3.jpg

Title: Maize Stem Borer
Authors: R.   Rajkumar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The young maize stem
borer larvae are yellow brown in colour with a brown head. The larva feeds on
the leaves by making a few &ldquo;shot holes&rdquo; and then boring its way downwards
through the central whorl. It may also cause internal tunnels by entering into
the midribs and feeding on the internal tissues. The characteristic symptoms
are &ldquo;shot holes&rdquo; during early stage and &ldquo;dead heart&rdquo; during severe attack.
Severe damage will result in breaking of the stem, and stunted growth is widely reported.
Larvae pupate inside the stem. The adult moth is medium sized and straw
coloured.
    This is one of the most serious
pests of maize and requires immediate control measures if noticed. The insect
damage occurs mostly during the months of April to October.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Destroy the crop residues after harvest</li>
    <li>Clip lower leaves (up to the 4th leaf)</li>
    <li>Earth up the crop to bury the lower leaves and apply a basal application
    of neem cake @ 80 kg/acre</li>
    <li>Install light traps @ 5/acre between 7 - 9 pm to trap and kill the
    adults</li>
    <li>On confirmation of the pest incidence based on the light trap catches,
    release<em> Trichogramma chilonis</em> @ 6 to
    7 cc/acre during the insect&rsquo;s egg laying period 3 times at weekly intervals.
    These egg parasitoid cards are available from biocontrol labs of the Department
    of Agriculture and Research laboratories of local sugar factories</li>
    <li>Mix cartap hydrochloride 4% G @ 4 kg/acre with sand to make a total
    quantity of 50 kg and apply onto the leaf whorl on the 20th day
    after sowing</li>
    <li>Spray carbaryl 50 WP @ 400 g/ acre on the&nbsp;20th day after
    sowing</li>
</ul>
<p>
Note: These plant protection inputs are
available in local agro input dealers and also in Depot of Agricultural
Extension Centres.</p>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Chilo
partellus</em>
Images: 8eb46d11-6003-4d95-900b-ca3308d17c92.jpg, 550afe53-7384-4a90-b617-1562227f2ad1.jpg
Content:
The young maize stem
borer larvae are yellow brown in colour with a brown head. The larva feeds on
the leaves by making a few &ldquo;shot holes&rdquo; and then boring its way downwards
through the central whorl. It may also cause internal tunnels by entering into
the midribs and feeding on the internal tissues. The characteristic symptoms
are &ldquo;shot holes&rdquo; during early stage and &ldquo;dead heart&rdquo; during severe attack.
Severe damage will result in breaking of the stem, and stunted growth is widely reported.
Larvae pupate inside the stem. The adult moth is medium sized and straw
coloured. This is one of the most serious
pests of maize and requires immediate control measures if noticed. The insect
damage occurs mostly during the months of April to October. <ul>
    <li>
    Destroy the crop residues after harvest</li>
    <li>Clip lower leaves (up to the 4th leaf)</li>
    <li>Earth up the crop to bury the lower leaves and apply a basal application
    of neem cake @ 80 kg/acre</li>
    <li>Install light traps @ 5/acre between 7 - 9 pm to trap and kill the
    adults</li>
    <li>On confirmation of the pest incidence based on the light trap catches,
    release<em> Trichogramma chilonis</em> @ 6 to
    7 cc/acre during the insect&rsquo;s egg laying period 3 times at weekly intervals.
    These egg parasitoid cards are available from biocontrol labs of the Department
    of Agriculture and Research laboratories of local sugar factories</li>
    <li>Mix cartap hydrochloride 4% G @ 4 kg/acre with sand to make a total
    quantity of 50 kg and apply onto the leaf whorl on the 20th day
    after sowing</li>
    <li>Spray carbaryl 50 WP @ 400 g/ acre on the&nbsp;20th day after
    sowing</li>
</ul>
<p>
Note: These plant protection inputs are
available in local agro input dealers and also in Depot of Agricultural
Extension Centres.</p> When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

Title: Management of Uniformity in Size of Bulbs in Onion
Authors: Gulbir    Singh
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Non-uniformity in bulb size of onion is a very big problem
which leads to economic loss to the farmers. Non-uniform bulbs are difficult to
store for marketing. The difference in size does not attract a good value for
the crop in the market. Hence, the uniformity in size of onion bulbs is very
important.
    Uniformity
in maturity plays a very important role in bulb size and storage quality. Onion
is a moderate weather crop and should be planted early to attain the largest
bulb size. Selecting the correct
variety and understanding the climatic and other environmental factors that
affect its performance is extremely important.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Adequate light and frequent irrigation should be
    used when onions are small to minimize leaching of nitrogen from the root zone</li>
    <li>Application of optimum fertilizer is essential
    for top quality and yields</li>
    <li>Proper moisture management is important in
    alleviating pink root problems, general root health, and therefore bulb growth vigour</li>
    <li>Maintaining an even soil moisture is important in
    reducing incidence of double-centre bulbs</li>
    <li>Spray Chlormequat chloride, e.g. Lihocin 50% / CCC
    at 0.5 ml per litre of water 60 and 75 days after transplanting seedlings to
    help maintain the size of the bulbs</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

Title: Nutrient Deficiency
Authors: S. G Matale
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Stresses such as soil salinity, pathogens and air pollution induce their
own characteristic set of visual symptoms. These symptoms closely resemble
those of nutrient deficiency. Pathological symptoms can often be separated from
nutritional symptoms by their distribution in a population of affected plants.
If the plants are under a nutrient stress, all plants of a given type and age
in the same environment tend to develop similar symptoms at the same time. To
study the exact cause of the disease, plant parts are to be examined for the
following:<br>
</br>
1)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Specific
nutritional problem for deficiency
<br>
</br>
2)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Nutrient
requirement of the crop
<br>
</br>
3)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Concentration
of nutrients for the recommendations
    Visible nutrient
deficiency symptoms can be a very powerful diagnostic tool for evaluating the
nutrient status of plants. Many of the classic deficiency symptoms such as tip
burn, chlorosis and necrosis are characteristically associated with more than
one mineral deficiency and also with other stresses that by themselves are not diagnostic
for any specific nutrient stress. Their detection is extremely useful in making
an evaluation of nutrient status. The nutrients used by and available to crops
must be balanced.
    <ul>
    <li>Proper
    nutrients should be provided to the plant</li>
    <li>To
    advise the recommendation, the mature plant parts should be sent for analysis</li>
    <li>Correct
    growth stage and time are the most crucial things in plant analysis. Plant parts
    that correlate with the yield should be selected.</li>
    <li>Different
    methods are adopted to prepare plant samples for analysis. These are total leaf
    analysis, pot culture and tissue testing.</li>
    <li>The
    plant samples should be well processed through standard method to avoid any
    contamination.</li>
</ul>
Scientific Names:

<br>
</br>

    <li>Correct
    growth stage and time are the most crucial things in plant analysis. Plant parts
    that correlate with the yield should be selected.</li>
    <li>Different
    methods are adopted to prepare plant samples for analysis. These are total leaf
    analysis, pot culture and tissue testing.</li>
    <li>The
    plant samples should be well processed through standard method to avoid any
    contamination.</li>
</ul>

Title: Paddy Blast
Authors: G.   Sudhakar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Rice blast is one of the most important diseases of rice
and is caused by a fungus. A typical blast wound on a rice leaf is grey at the
centre, has a dark border, and is spindle-shaped, i.e. large in the middle and smaller
towards the ends.
    This disease is also known as &lsquo;rice fever&rsquo;. The pathogen
may infect all the aboveground parts of a rice plant at different growth
stages: leaf, collar, node, internode, base, or neck and other parts of the
panicle, and sometimes the leaf sheath. Among them, leaves and neck infections
are more severe. The infection will be more during rainy season.The disease
will cause severe yield loss (up to 70-80%) to the paddy crop.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Avoid excessive application of
    Nitrogenous fertilizers and apply nitrogen in three split doses</li>
    <li>Remove weeds from bunds</li>
    <li>Grow tolerant varieties (Co 47, IR -
    64, IR - 36, Jaya)</li>
    <li>Burn straw and stubbles after harvest</li>
    <li>Treat the dry seeds with&nbsp;<em>Pseudomonas
    fluorescens</em>&nbsp;talc formulation @10g/Kg of seed</li>
    <li>Maintain water to a depth of 2.5 cm
    over an area of 25 m2 in the nursery and sprinkle 2.5 kg of&nbsp;<em>P.
    fluorescens</em>&nbsp;(talc) and mix in stagnated water. Soak the roots of
    seedlings for 30 minutes before transplanting.</li>
    <li>Spray&nbsp;<em>P. fluorescens</em>&nbsp;talc
    formulation @ 0.5% from 45 days after transplanting at 10 day intervals thrice.</li>
    <li>Alternatively, treat the seeds @ 2 g/Kg
    seed with captan 50% WP, carbendazim 50% WP or tricyclazole 75% WP</li>
    <li>Spray tricyclazole 95% WP @ 1g/lit of
    water or carbendazim 50% WP @ 1 g/lit of water</li>
    <li>Spraying 3 to 4 times each at nursery,
    tillering and panicle emergence stage may be required for complete control</li>
    <li>Spray potassium silicate @ 200 ml/ 100
    lit of water.</li>
</ul>
<p>Do not use
chemical control when making use of <em>Pseudomonas fluorescens</em>&nbsp;as
chemicals will kill this bacterium.<br>
</br>
<br>
</br>
EC- Emulsifiable Concentrate; WP: Wettable Powder</p>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Magnaporthe grisea</em>
Images: 7bbede6d-ead4-4220-b02f-4fc70e587202.jpg, f64bc7f0-a14c-449d-8727-73e62a4bb15a.jpg

Title: Papaya Mealybug
Authors: K.   Soundary
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Papaya mealybug infestations are typically
observed as clusters of cotton-like masses on the above-ground portion of
plants. The adult female is yellow and covered with a white waxy coating. The
papaya mealybug feeds on the sap of plants by inserting its mouthparts, called
stylets, into the leaf epidermis, fruit and stem. This results in chlorosis,
plant stunting, leaf deformation, early leaf and fruit drop, a heavy build up
of honeydew, and the death of the plant. Heavy infestations are capable of
rendering fruit inedible due to the build up of thick white wax.
    Mealybugs have piercing-sucking mouthparts
and feed by inserting these mouthparts into plant tissue and sucking the plant
sap. The papaya mealybug is polyphagous and has been recorded on 55 host plants
in more than 25 genera. Economically important host plants of the papaya mealy
bug include papaya, hibiscus, avocado, citrus, cotton, tomato, eggplant,
peppers, beans, peas, sweet potato, mango, cherry and pomegranate. Papaya mealybugs
have only been recorded feeding on areas of the host plant that are above
ground, such as leaves and fruits.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Spray
    neem oil @ 5 ml per litre at intervals of 15 days</li>
    <li>The
    ants that spread the mealybugs can be controlled through application of kerosene
    spray 3 ml per tree along with 2g turmeric powder</li>
    <li>Spray <em>Verticillium
    lecanii</em> at 5g
    per litre of water</li>
    <li>Spray imidacloprid 17.5% SL at 1 ml per litre
    of water and add 60g soap mixture</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Paracoccus marginatus</em>
Images: 0cfc2159-13d5-4b46-8566-4cf2c092e74b.jpg, 649e527d-a2d9-4d5f-8c5d-0631be7aeff1.jpg

Title: Phytophthora in Tomato
Authors: Gulbir    Singh
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The
roots, crown, stems and fruit of tomato are susceptible to Phytophthora. Symptoms
of Phytophthora infection include wilted plants, discoloured plant roots and cankers
on fruit crowns and lower stems. The fruits also develop brown grey water-soaked
lesions on their surface.
    Tomato
seedlings that are raised in nurseries before being transplanted into the field
can be attacked by Phytophthora. The pathogen lives in the soil and can persist
for more than 10 years. If this disease is not controlled in the nursery, it could
cause huge yield loss. The seedlings should be planted in very well drained
sites because Phytophthora can move in water.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Use
    Phytophthora free or resistant variety</li>
    <li>Sow
    seeds in lines to allow more sunlight and air to reach the plants</li>
    <li>Affected
    plants should be uprooted and burnt</li>
    <li>Seedlings
    should be dipped in 1% carbendazim solution before transplanting</li>
    <li>Treat
    seeds with the fungicide thiram 1-2gm per/kg</li>
    <li>Spray
    fungicide copper oxychloride at 2gm/ 1 litres of water, 15 to 25 days after
    transplanting</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Phytophthora infestans</em>
Images: 2af7a741-61c6-4a41-9684-b4e7ad8f9740.jpg, ade693de-637e-489a-9932-fb6e21e976cf.jpg
Content:

Title: Pigeon Pea Pod Borer
Authors: Vijay S Thokre
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The pod borer is a major pest of pigeon pea. Its
population directly affects the yield. Infestation starts from 90 days after
sowing. The females lay eggs in all parts of the plant. The eggs are yellowish
and shiny. It feeds on leaves at the initial stage and then later on the pods. The
larva thrusts its head inside the pods and leaves the rest of its body hanging
out. Round holes appear on the pods. Larval colour changes accordingly to their
feeding habitat.
    It is a polyphagous pest observed on various crops. The economic
threshold level (ETL) of the pest is 1 larva per plant. 1 larva of this pest
causes about 138 kg yield loss.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Install
    pheromone traps @ 12/ hectare. Use Hexalure for pod borers. Change the lure
    every 21 days.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Install
    as many bird perches as possible so the birds can feed on harmful larvae. Install
    the perches 1 to 2 feet above the plant height.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Spray
    Neem Seed Kernal Extract (NSKE) 5% after 50% flowering to prevent the insects
    from laying eggs</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Release
    the egg parasite, <em>Trichogramma chilonis</em> @ 1cc per acre</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>If
    infestation is above the ETL, then spray any one of following chemicals:</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <ul>
        <li>Chlorpyrifos
        20% EC @ 25 ml per 10 litres water</li>
    </ul>
</ul>
<ul>
    <ul>
        <li>Quinalphos
        25% EC @ 16 ml per 10 litres water</li>
    </ul>
</ul>
<ul>
    <ul>
        <li>Profenophos
        40% EC @ 25ml per 10 litres water</li>
    </ul>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Helicoverpa armigera</em>
Images: c61eb461-3dc6-4703-9c60-b7bb108b4504.jpg, d86493ef-d1ee-4a64-a2f1-643df136b3d1.jpg, b7888455-41ff-49a1-82e7-24543d6f7b31.jpg

Title: Rat control in Paddy
Authors: Mr   Murugan
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Rats
pose a real problem and challenge to Indian agriculture. The outbreaks that
occurred periodically in the past have brought limitless miseries in terms of
food shortages and loss of livelihood among farmers. Rats inflict extensive
damage to rice in all stages of growth. Yearly yield loss may range from 5% -60%.
    Generally, rat damage is higher in the wet
season than in the dry&nbsp;season.
Rat damage occurs at all stages of rice growth but reaches its peak&nbsp;while grain is maturing. Increased
damage is due to greater numbers of rats when there is increased&nbsp;cover (rice plants, weeds, etc.) and
available food (rice). Field rats survive by eating frogs, snails, etc. during
non-rice periods, making them difficult to manage.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Maintain narrow bunds
    (45 x 30 cm)</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Identify the bund holes
    and plaster them with heavy clay. Burn straw near the bund holes and cover with clay.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Log the field with water at times of heavy rat incidence</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Trap using Thanjavur bow traps
    (100 traps/ha)</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Keep owl perches
    in different places in the paddy field</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Use bait traps for killing the rats like rodent
    paste, aluminium phosphide and rodent cakes along with paddy
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Bandicota
bengalensis</em>
Images: 031ba7a6-129b-4a23-b7ca-ff9bda42b77a.jpg, 6e8f54d9-149c-4fd1-8fdf-861a5dd1eca4.jpg
Content:

<ul>
    <li>Use bait traps for killing the rats like rodent
    paste, aluminium phosphide and rodent cakes along with paddy
    </li>
</ul> When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

Title: Rhinoceros Beetle in Coconut
Authors: Ms.    Girija
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The Rhinoceros
beetle is a black-coloured
horned beetle which is active at night and hides in feeding
or breeding sites during the day. The beetle attacks the young leaf fronds which,
when fully opened, show characteristic
diamond shaped cuts. Repeated attack can destroy the top portion resulting in
the death of the palm.
    The adult beetles from the manure pits
or the nearby trees bore into the opened fronds of the young palms and cause
damage. The rhinoceros beetle feeds on young growing tissue and eats the exuded sap. The grubs of the beetle are
usually found in manure pits.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Wipe out the grubs in the manure pits by pouring 250 ml green muscardine fungus (<em>Metarhizium anisopliae</em>) culture mixed
    with 750 ml of water into manure pits</li>
    <li>Keep the coconut farm clean by chopping and burning the decayed
    and affected logs</li>
    <li>Hook out the beetle from the attacked palm using the beetle hook</li>
    <li>Place three naphthalene balls in the leaf axil at the top of the
    crown to repel the beetles</li>
    <li>Set up light traps following the first
    rains in summer and monsoon period to attract and kill the adult beetles</li>
    <li>Use pheromone traps with
    Rhinolure @ 12 /ha for trapping the adults, then destroy them</li>
    <li>Soak castor cake @ 1 kg/ 5 litres of
    water in small mud pots and keep them in the coconut gardens to attract and
    kill the adults</li>
    <li>Treat the longitudinally split tender
    coconut stem and green petioles of fronds with fresh toddy and keep them in the
    garden to attract and trap the beetles</li>
    <li>Apply a mixture of Neem Seed
    Kernel Powder + sand (1:2) @150g/ palm at the base of the 3 inner most leaves
    in the crown</li>
    <li>For nut bearing
    coconut, root feed with TNAU coconut tonic at 200ml/palm, once in six months.
    Apply 200 g of borax/ palm /year in two splits.
    </li>
</ul>
Scientific Names: <em>Oryctes
rhinoceros</em>
Images: f11110ca-dfb2-4165-9b13-df8bc33a221f.jpg, 50e8c4cf-fb15-4d38-8c4e-96169ed982bf.jpg

Title: Rice Leaf Folder
Authors: R.   Rajkumar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Chlorotic
symptoms are a characteristic feature of this problem. The damage is caused by
an insect, locally known as leaf folder or leaf roller. Oval shaped eggs are
laid in rows on the leaf tissue. Young larvae feed on the unopened leaves,
while the older larvae remain inside the leaf fold and scrape the leaf tissue. The
presence of faecal matter and leaf tips fastened to the leaf base, which
represent a papery structure even at a distance, will help the farmer to be
prepared to manage the pest. Adult moths are&nbsp;yellow with wavy stripes.
    Rice leaf folders
are a common problem in rice growing countries. Economic losses of 10%
leaf&nbsp;damage&nbsp;at vegetative phase and 5% at flag leaf&nbsp;stage and
flowering&nbsp;are possible if the pest is unnoticed.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Remove and destroy the stubbles after
    harvest. Keep the field free from weeds, trim field bunds and provide effective
    drainage.</li>
    <li>Avoid excessive use of nitrogenous
    fertilizers</li>
    <li>Avoid&nbsp;close&nbsp;planting; leave
    30 cm space every 2.5 m</li>
    <li>Use light traps in paddy fields from 6pm
    to 9pm to monitor pest incidence</li>
    <li>Dislodge the hidden larvae using a ber
    twig</li>
    <li>Release <em>Trichogramma chilonis</em> three times at 3cc per acre</li>
    <li>Spread neem leaves randomly in the
    field to deter the adults from laying eggs</li>
    <li>Spray neem oil 300 ml + kerosene 250 ml
    + 50 g khadi soap, which will be very effective</li>
    <li>Spray 300 ml neem oil + 300 ml pongamia
    oil + 50 gram khadi soap which will afford protection</li>
    <li>Spray Chlorpyrifos 20% EC @ 250 ml/acre
    to protect against the pest</li>
    <li>Apply Cartap Hydrochloride 50 SP @ 250
    g/acre
    </li>
</ul>
<p>
EC-
Emulsifiable concentrate, SP-
Soluble powder
</p>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Cnaphalocrocis medinalis</em>
Images: 70946d01-f448-47e8-9809-1fd4d9681fe2.jpg, 0136ae51-110f-46d8-a14b-5f3c2d3c0ebe.jpg

Title: Rice Stem Borer
Authors: S.   Malarvannan
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    This problem is caused by an insect. It is commonly known
as rice stem borer or yellow rice borer. Typical bore holes will be seen on the
stem. Usually one larva is seen inside the stem. It remains inside the stem and
feeds on the internal contents. The shoot of the affected plant can be pulled
off easily, a symptom known as dead heart. At maturity, the grains become chaffy,
which is known as white ear. The whole plant finally dies.
<br>
</br>
The yellow adult moth has a black spot on its wings so
is easy to identify. It lays eggs in masses on the leaf tips.
    Rice stem borer is a major problem on rice.
If timely control measures are not adapted it may cause a crop loss of 30%. This
is a major pest that is noticed both in the nursery as well as in the main
field. During the off season, it survives on weed hosts. It does not transmit
plant diseases.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Grow
    resistant varieties such as TKM 6, IR 20 and IR 36</li>
    <li>Practice
    crop rotation and maintain proper crop spacing</li>
    <li>While
    transplanting, clip the tips of the leaves to remove and destroy egg masses</li>
    <li>Avoid
    excess use of nitrogenous fertilizers</li>
    <li>Apply
    a basal application of neem cake at 42-50 kg/acre</li>
    <li>Avoid
    continuous water stagnation in the field</li>
    <li>Remove
    and destroy weeds, dead hearts and white ears</li>
    <li>Use
    pheromone traps @ 3 per acre</li>
    <li>Use
    light traps @ 12 per acre between 7-9 pm
    &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </li>
    <li>Spray
    neem-based biopesticides like Nimbecidine @ 300 ml per acre</li>
    <li>Spray<em>
    Bacillus thuringiensis</em> (kurstaki
    strain) @ 100 ml per acre</li>
    <li>If
    the damage is above the economic threshold level of 10% dead heart in
    vegetative stage and the presence of 1 moth or 1 egg mass/sq.m. in the ear-head
    bearing stage, then spray any one of the following chemicals: fenthion,
    fenitrothion, phosalone, cartap hydrochloride, chlorpyriphos or phenthoate at
    0.5 kg a.i./ha or fipronil 5% SC at 1 litre/ha</li>
    <li>Harvest
    the crop down to the ground level to prevent the spread of the pest to the next
    season</li>
    <li>After
    the harvest, burn the crop residues and plough the field&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
a.i.
&ndash; active ingredient SC- Suspension concentrate
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Scirpophaga incertulas</em>
Images: b33d6b2e-ad77-4cae-a6a9-b9cb49eb6e7e.jpg, 7dd65446-7c07-4425-8643-0512a366e05d.jpg

Title: Sesame Phyllody
Authors: T.   Aruna
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    A
plant affected by sesame
phyllody bears clusters of leaves and a malformed
flower at the tip. Plants looks like a witches broom. In severe infection, the
entire flower shoot is replaced by short twisted leaves closely arranged on a
stem with abnormal branches bending
downwards.
    This
disease is
caused by Phytoplasma which is transmitted by leaf hoppers. It converts the flowering
parts into green leafy structures
then causes severe vein clearing. Though the capsules are
formed on the lower portion,
the plant does not yield quality seeds. This is the major yield-reducing problem
affecting
sesame.
    <ul>
    <li>Intercrop
    sesame with pigeon pea (6:1)</li>
    <li>Remove
    and burn infected plants</li>
    <li>Seed
    treatment with imidacloprid or carbosulfan protects the crop from all sucking
    pests including leaf hoppers for about a month</li>
    <li>Spray
    dimethoate 30 EC @ 500 ml/ ha at 30, 40 and 60 days after sowing to control the
    leaf hopper
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: Phytoplasma
Images: 9d9ee927-5f74-43d6-a3d1-916f7d84a678.jpg, de9e5990-43f2-4362-b107-dfaed918c9b4.jpg

Title: Soil Sample Collection
Authors: R.   Rajkumar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Soil
testing is important in estimating the physical, chemical and biological
properties of soil. It will help to decide the exact nutrient requirement for
the crop. It also provides information on the existing nutrient status after
harvest.
    Soil testing helps
to record the available nutrients in the soil. Based on the soil testing
results, precise requirement for each crop can be calculated.<br>
</br>
<br>
</br>
The results can also
give the farmer an idea about what crops are most suitable for the field according
to the availability of nutrients. This scientific method saves the cost of
fertilizer application as the soil will supply nutrients in an available form
during the critical stages of the crop growth. This prevents unnecessary
accumulation of unutilized fertilisers and thereby prevents harmful effects to
the environment.
    <ul>
    <li>Walk in a
    zig-zag manner in the field. Remove the surface litter in 10 randomly selected locations.
    Using an auger or spade, make a &lsquo;V&rsquo; shaped cut to a depth of 15 cm or according
    to the crop cultivation. Collect 0.5 to 1.0 kg of representative soil samples
    and put them in poly bags. Label the bag giving the details of the field, crop,
    farmer name survey number, sample number and date of collection.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Do not
    collect sample around fences, bunds, trees etc.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Do
    not collect sample during heavy rainfall, water stagnation or in fields where
    organic manure has been applied</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Use
    of bio fertilizers could supplement 25% of the total requirement of the
    nutrients and also promote soil fertility in an eco-friendly manner</li>
</ul>
Scientific Names: 
Images: e1500ca7-9f65-44a2-9278-e44dd987e436.jpg, 4fabd820-2f23-4cc1-8c0e-ab517ba37255.jpg
Content:

</ul>

</ul>

Title: Soybean Girdle Beetle
Authors: Charudatta D Thipse
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The
incidence of girdle beetles is observed at the seedling stage. The presence of 2
circular cuts on the branch or stem is a characteristic symptom. Larvae bore
into the stem of soybean. The inside of the stem is eaten by the larvae,
forming tunnels within the stem. The infected portion above the circular cut is
unable to get any nutrition so it dries up. In the later stages of infestation,
the plant is severed at about 15 to 25 cm above the ground.
    The
main damage is caused by the larvae of the insect. The attack of the insect
initially begins in the last week of July to the first fortnight of August. The
insect remains active from July to October, damaging the crop most severely
during August and September. Heavy incidence may reduce the yield by up to 40%.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Practice deep summer ploughing</li>
    <li>Sow the crop at the proper time i.e. at the onset of
    monsoon, with the recommended seed rate of 75 kg/ha. The crop should not be
    overcrowded</li>
    <li>Sow tolerant varieties such as NRC-12 or NRC-7</li>
    <li>Avoid excess nitrogenous fertilizers</li>
    <li>Destroy crop residues</li>
    <li>Collect and destroy infested plant parts at least once
    every 10 days</li>
    <li>Apply pesticides if pest population crosses the
    Economic Threshold Level (5 per cent damaged plants)</li>
    <li>Spray NSKE 5% or azadirachtin 10,000 ppm @1 ml per 1
    litre of water to avoid the pest laying eggs</li>
    <li>Apply Cartap hydrochloride 4 G @ 4 kg/acre at the time
    of sowing</li>
    <li>Spray lambda cyhalothrin 5% EC @ 10 ml or dimethoate
    25% EC @ 2 ml per liter of water 30-35 days after sowing and repeat 15-20 days
    after the first spraying if infestation is observed</li>
    <li>Always use a hollow cone spray nozzle for spraying</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Obereopsis
brevis</em>
Images: 3f804654-dae4-4ceb-a470-2728e878dabc.jpg, 41c79d75-a4d7-4b36-b693-212d1c699c4f.jpg
Content:

Title: Spodoptera in Soybean
Authors: K. P Singh
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Spodoptera
larvae feed on the soybean crop and can cause considerable yield losses. Two
black spots are present on the second segment of the larva. The female lays
eggs in masses on the surface of the leaves and covers them with whitish hair
scales. The egg stage lasts for 3 days. The newly emerged caterpillars feed on
the lower surface of soybean leaves, skeletonising the lower surface of leaves,
so that only the top epidermis is left intact. Spodoptera larvae undergo
several colour changes from green to almost black in the mature stages. Large
larvae can feed on the whole plant.
    Spodoptera
larvae affect the crop at the vegetative stage and if the infestation is at
flowering or podding stage, they can cause yield losses of up to 60%. The
infestation mainly occurs before late August and early September.
    <ul>
    <li>Deep
    summer ploughing</li>
    <li>Install
    bird perches in the field @ 20/ha</li>
    <li>Install
    pheromone traps @ 10/ha</li>
    <li>Spray
    5% Neem Seed Kernel Extract (NSKE) at flowering stage as a preventive measure</li>
    <li>Spray
    quinalphos 25% EC at 30 ml or chlorpyripfos 20% EC @ 30 ml in 10 litres of
    water</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Spodoptera</em>
sp.
Images: 2a2b5011-7d8e-456f-a543-00bb7abee43c.jpg, 619fa542-94b9-4dbe-8632-9a1b5207c388.jpg
Content:

    bird perches in the field @ 20/ha</li>
    <li>Install
    pheromone traps @ 10/ha</li>
    <li>Spray
    5% Neem Seed Kernel Extract (NSKE) at flowering stage as a preventive measure</li>
    <li>Spray
    quinalphos 25% EC at 30 ml or chlorpyripfos 20% EC @ 30 ml in 10 litres of
    water</li>
</ul> When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.

Title: Weed Control in Black Gram
Authors: G.   Sudhakar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    Grassy
weeds are a common problem in black gram fields. The weeds lead to stunted
growth of the main crop. Weed management is critical in the early stages of the
crop.
    In
black gram, among the grassy and dicot weeds, grassy weed is the main problem,
resulting in yield losses.&nbsp; This weed
cannot be controlled by manual weeding practice.
    Identify
the predominant weed flora in the field.&nbsp;
The control measures are adapted according to the weed flora present.<br>
</br>
<ul>
    <li>Adapt
    the row planting method with a spacing of 35 cm between the rows and 15 cm between
    the plants</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Apply post-emergent weedicide, e.g. quizalofop ethyl
    5% EC @ of 350 ml per acre in 180 litres of water.&nbsp; This should be done 25 days after sowing.</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names:

Title: Banana Stem Weevil
Authors: Manju   Thakur
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The banana stem weevil
attacks the plant during flowering and bunch formation stages and causes severe
yield loss by preventing bunch development. The early symptom which indicates
weevil and grub activity is the presence of jelly exudation on the banana
stem. Due to feeding by grubs, the pseudostem becomes hollow and can even
break at the apical region after a gush of wind. The grubs cause more damage
by making long tunnels in the pseudostem. This results in yellowing and
withering of leaves, exudation of sap from leaf sheaths, decaying of
peduncles and immature ripening of fruits.
    The pest
incidence is at its peak during summer and monsoon seasons. The attack
usually starts about four months after planting, which coincides with the
initiation of the peduncle in the growing plants.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Follow clean cultivation practices
    and in severe infestations, uproot and burn the plants</li>
    <li>Stem
    trapping- Cut old pseudostems into
    lengths of 20 to 60 cm and split each of these lengthways. Then, place on the
    ground near the corn bases with the cut surface downwards. Swab
    the cut surface of these traps with biocontrol agents like <em>Beauveria
    bassiana</em> (20 g rice chaffy grains formulation/ 3 ml in 100 ml of liquid
    formulation) or 15 ml of entomopathogenic nematode,&nbsp;<em>Heterorhabditis indica</em>&nbsp;at 1 billion infective
    juveniles (IJs) per ml. The volatiles from these stem traps attract weevils
    that will be killed while walking on the trap surface within or after 24 hrs</li>
    <li>Spray
    chlorpyriphos 20 EC 2.5 ml/litre + 1 ml wetting agent or azadirachtin (5 ml/litre)
    2 or 3 times at 3 week intervals.</li>
    <li>If
    infestation is noticed after 7 months of planting, stem injection with
    systemic insecticide such as imidacloprid (0.2 ml in 500 ml water) is the
    only way to control the pest. Do not inject insecticide after flowering.</li>
    <li>Matocking should be avoided i.e. the plant should not be left after bunch harvest for
    recycling of nutrients in weevil endemic area.</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Odoiporus longicollis</em>

Title: Citrus Bark Eating Caterpillar
Authors: Vijay S Thokre
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The full grown larva is cylindrical, dirty brown in colour and measures
about 40 mm in length. The larvae tunnel
into the branches and stem of citrus, especially near joints in branches. They
feed mostly during the night under the protective covering of webbing
consisting partly of frays, feacal pellets and silken threads secreted by the
larvae, and remain hidden during the day time. As a result of their feeding on
the bark, the sap conducting tissues are damaged. The vigor of the plant is reduced and the yield and quality of fruits are
adversely affected.
    This is often a serious
pest on citrus, particularly in South India. The eggs are laid in the months of May and June in groups of 15, which
are glued to the bark. A single female lays as many as 624 eggs with an average
of about 350. The eggs hatch after 8 to 11 days. On hatching, the larvae live
under the bark until September when they tunnel in to the wood.<br>
</br>
<br>
</br>
The pest is active throughout the year. The pest is very common in old
and neglected orchards of any age. However, the pest incidence has been observed
in more than 65% of orchards, where more than 60% of trees were found attacked.
    Cut and burn affected twigs wherever possible<br>
</br>
<br>
</br>
Insert a hooked iron wire inside the holes in the bark and pull out the
larvae, then kill them by dipping in kerosinized water<br>
</br>
<br>
</br>
Apply spot
application of 10 ml fenthion in 1 litre of water
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Indarbela tetraonis</em>
Images: 4b62fb3b-cfcb-4146-add3-bb4b921fc5c7.jpg

Title: Citrus Leaf Miner
Authors: Sachin    Matale
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The problem is caused by an insect called a leaf
miner. As the name implies, the larvae mine into the tender leaves and sometimes
under the outer skin (epidermis) of the tender branches. The larvae leave the
outer skin intact and thus give rise to transparent white shiny zigzag
galleries. As a result of the attack a
large number of leaves turn pale, curl up and eventually dry up. This kind of
damage to nursery plants results in the complete loss of root stock.<br>
</br>
<br>
</br>
The adult moths are very
small in size, silvery white in colour with prominent black eyes. The wing
expanse is 5 mm. The forewings are brown and striped with a prominent black
spot near the apical margin. The hind pair or wings are white. Both the pairs
of wings are fringed with minute hairs.
    The citrus leaf miner (CLM) is native to Asia and is
found throughout the continent and beyond. The full grown caterpillar remains in the galleries tunneled below the
epidermis of the leaf tissue.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Prune heavily the infested leaves in winter and burn
    them</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>Clip the first attacked leaves and crush the larvae in
    their galleries</li>
</ul>
<ul>
    <li>The pest is difficult to
    control, particularly after infestation has taken place, since the larvae are
    internal feeders. However, pesticide application may be used immediately after
    the attack is noticed.&nbsp; Please note that
    chemicals will also kill the natural enemies so consider their use carefully. Any
    one of the following insecticides at the concentration mentioned may be
    selected and sprayed for the control of this pest: Formothion 25 EC 0.04% or
    Dimethoate 30 EC 0.05% or Chlorpyriphos 20 EC 0.05% or Quinalphos 25EC 0.05%
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Phyllocnistis
citrella</em>
Images: cd7949cb-8ea8-4f77-87df-a7cd196ff30c.jpg, 344cf1e6-021d-43ab-bff4-9c50325dce51.jpg, 060aa611-8f3f-464f-9f42-1f4d884ba9eb.jpg

Title: Groundnut Caterpillar
Authors: R.   Rajkumar
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The groundnut caterpillar, <em>Spodoptera litura</em>, appears on groundnut
both in vegetative phase and at the time of pod formation. It feeds initially
by skeletonizing, leaving only the outline of the leaves and veins on the
plant. As growth continues, caterpillars eat the entire leaves. After December,
particularly after heavy rains, the infestation increases.
    The adult female moth lays eggs in masses of
200-300 on the underside of the groundnut leaves. The egg masses are
approximately 4-7 mm in diameter, brown in colour and are covered with body
hair. Eggs usually hatch after 3- 4 days. Fully grown caterpillars measure
about 3-5 cm in length. They feed gregariously by scrapping the chlorophyll.
Sometimes the feeding is so heavy that only the petiole (the stalk that
attaches the leaf to the stem) and branches are left behind. The old larvae are
nocturnal and can be found on the soil around the base of the plant during the
day time. When the population is high, the larvae migrate from one field to another
in search of food.
    <ul>
    <li>
    Deep
    summer ploughing will expose the hidden pupae to direct sunlight which can kill
    them</li>
    <li>Irrigating
    the field will avoid prolonged mid-season drought</li>
    <li>Plant
    castor or sunflower as trap crop</li>
    <li>Install
    pheromone traps @ 12 per acre</li>
    <li>Install
    5 bird perches per acre</li>
    <li>Spread
    a blue cloth in the filed during the evening to attract the larvae and then
    destroy them</li>
    <li>Spray
    NPV (Nuclear Polyhedrosis Virus) at 250 LE per hectare</li>
    <li>Place
    poison baits in the field to attract and be eaten by the caterpillars. The bait
    can be made with 12 kg rice bran, 2.5 kg jaggery, carbaryl 10% dust and
    sufficient water per ha to make as a small round ball.</li>
    <li>Spray
    Profenophos 50 EC @ 2 ml per litre of water.
    </li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Spodoptera litura</em>
Images: b9514ed2-7178-4992-8f65-13fd6712a026.jpg, bb77a455-4de4-4baf-a9f3-7195228edb79.jpg

Title: Groundnut Leaf Miner
Authors: Manju   Thakur
Editors: CABI
Sections:
    The groundnut leaf miner is a key pest of
groundnut. The damage to groundnut is caused by both larval and adult stages.
The adult is a tiny moth measuring about 6 mm in length with brownish grey
coloured wings. The larvae mine the leaves and feed inside the leaflet.
Initially, short blister-like mines can be seen on the upper side of the
leaflets. The larvae come out of the mine after 5-6 days and migrate together
to nearby leaves to feed and pupate in the webbed leaves. The mined areas in
the leaf become dry. In severe infestation, the entire foliage dries and gives
a burnt appearance.
    The groundnut leaf miner attacks both rainy
season and post-rainy season crops. Its incidence is severe July-August and
February-March and the losses can vary from 25 to 75%. Soybean is also one of
its important hosts.
    This pest can be managed using cultural
control measures, resistant varieties, biological control agents and by
spraying chemicals only when the
pest population is above the economic threshold level (ETL).<br>
</br>
<ul>
    <li>Intercrop
    groundnut with trap crops such as pearl millet and cowpea</li>
    <li>Practice crop
    rotation with non-leguminous crops such as maize, cotton and sorghum. Cotton-sorghum-groundnut
    is the best crop rotation combination to give better yields and reduce the
    incidence of leaf miner</li>
    <li>Use resistant
    varieties viz., ICGV 87160 (ICG (FDRS)) and NCAC 17090 which give better yields
    in the areas of high leaf miner incidence</li>
    <li>Set up light
    traps to attract the moths during night hours and to monitor the pest
    populations</li>
    <li>Remove the
    alternative hosts and weeds viz., lucerne, amaranthus, berseem and <em>Indigofera hirsuta</em> to control the growth
    of the leaf miner population</li>
    <li>Release&nbsp;<em>Trichogramma
    chilonis</em>&nbsp;@ 50000/ha twice (7-10 day interval)</li>
    <li>The chemical
    spray is only recommended when you have found 5 larvae per plant at the
    seedling stage i.e. 30 days after emergence (DAE), 10 larvae per plant per
    plant at the flowering stage (50 DAE), and 15 larvae per plant at the pod
    filling stage (70 DAE)</li>
    <li>If the
    populations are above ETL use a chemical spray with dimethoate at 200-250 ml
    a.i./ha or profenofos 20EC @ 2ml/ litre, 30-45 days after sowing</li>
</ul>
    When using a pesticide, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, and pre-harvest interval.
Scientific Names: <em>Aproaerema modicella</em>
Images: ee114cfd-51ed-4b4d-ac0d-d10569c62b43.jpg, c7238db1-0d78-4a04-898e-1761a24ac057.jpg
