Title: Banana Panama Wilt
Authors:   T. Aruna, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Grow wilt resistant cultivars in endemic areas and avoid susceptible varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Use pathogen free suckers.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Visual observations show yellowing of lower leaves, longitudinal splitting of pseudostem and wilting of plants.<br/>-&nbsp;A small portion of soil is removed to expose the upper portion of the corm to reveal symptoms.<br/>-&nbsp;Advanced stages of disease shows plants with a spiky appearance due to prominent upright apical leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;The xylem (water conducting) vessels turn reddish brown as the fungus grows through the tissues.<br/>-&nbsp;It is a soil borne disease and the fungus enters the roots through the fine laterals.<br/>-&nbsp;Infected rhizomes or suckers, farm implements, and irrigation water are responsible for the spread of the fungus.<br/>
    -&nbsp;An oblique hole at 45 angle is made to a depth of 10 cm. Immediately apply a gelatine capsule containing 60 mg of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i>. The capsule is injected into the hole with the help of a corm injector on the 2nd, 4th and 6th month after planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Provide good drainage especially during rainy season and use organic soil amendments.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply neem cake at 250 kg/ha.<br/>-&nbsp;Application of bio-agents <i>Trichoderma viride</i> at 1 kg and <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> along 1 kg with 100 kg farmyard manure per acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Dip pathogen free suckers in 1% Carbendazim before planting.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use). Very toxic to the aquatic organisms. Therefore cultivation besides water reservoirs should not be soil drenched. Systemic with curative and protectant activity<br/>-&nbsp;Panama wilt can be prevented by corm injection methods.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;As above<br/>-&nbsp;Drenching of Carbendazim 0.2% solution at 2-3 litre/ plant in the soil around the plants at monthly intervals starting from 1st month of planting.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;As above<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Fusarium oxysporum</i> f. sp. <i>cubense</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_90103.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_90105.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Grow wilt resistant cultivars in endemic areas and avoid susceptible varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Use pathogen free suckers.<br/> -&nbsp;Visual observations show yellowing of lower leaves, longitudinal splitting of pseudostem and wilting of plants.<br/>-&nbsp;A small portion of soil is removed to expose the upper portion of the corm to reveal symptoms.<br/>-&nbsp;Advanced stages of disease shows plants with a spiky appearance due to prominent upright apical leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;The xylem (water conducting) vessels turn reddish brown as the fungus grows through the tissues.<br/>-&nbsp;It is a soil borne disease and the fungus enters the roots through the fine laterals.<br/>-&nbsp;Infected rhizomes or suckers, farm implements, and irrigation water are responsible for the spread of the fungus.<br/> -&nbsp;An oblique hole at 45 angle is made to a depth of 10 cm. Immediately apply a gelatine capsule containing 60 mg of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i>. The capsule is injected into the hole with the help of a corm injector on the 2nd, 4th and 6th month after planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Provide good drainage especially during rainy season and use organic soil amendments.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply neem cake at 250 kg/ha.<br/>-&nbsp;Application of bio-agents <i>Trichoderma viride</i> at 1 kg and <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> along 1 kg with 100 kg farmyard manure per acre.<br/> -&nbsp;Dip pathogen free suckers in 1% Carbendazim before planting.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use). Title: Soybean Girdle Beetle
Authors:   Mr. Vijay S. Thokre
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Used broad base furrow technology for sowing. <br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant varieties e.g. JS 71-05, JS 97-52, MAUS 32.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove alternate host plants from the field e.g. <i>Xanthium strumarium</i>.<br/>-&nbsp;Larger plant populations result in increased infestation.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Infestation starts from 18-21 days after sowing. <br/>-&nbsp;Stem tissues are eaten by larvae, which results in tunnelling.<br/>-&nbsp;Girdling of stems causes drying of shoots and branches<br/>
    -&nbsp;Manual collection and destruction of infested plant parts. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of neem seed kernel extract 5% as a repellent for egg laying. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray fenvalerate 20 EC @ 10 ml per litre water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray profenofos 50EC @ 15ml per litre water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Acephate 75 WP @ 3 grams per litre water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>

-&nbsp;Used broad base furrow technology for sowing. <br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant varieties e.g. JS 71-05, JS 97-52, MAUS 32.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove alternate host plants from the field e.g. <i>Xanthium strumarium</i>.<br/>-&nbsp;Larger plant populations result in increased infestation.<br/> -&nbsp;Infestation starts from 18-21 days after sowing. <br/>-&nbsp;Stem tissues are eaten by larvae, which results in tunnelling.<br/>-&nbsp;Girdling of stems causes drying of shoots and branches<br/> -&nbsp;Manual collection and destruction of infested plant parts. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of neem seed kernel extract 5% as a repellent for egg laying. <br/> -&nbsp;Spray fenvalerate 20 EC @ 10 ml per litre water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray profenofos 50EC @ 15ml per litre water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Acephate 75 WP @ 3 grams per litre water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>

Title: Soybean Tobacco Leaf Eating Caterpillar
Authors:   Mr. Vijay S. Thokre
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep ploughing in summer season <br/>-&nbsp;Use castor (<i>Ricinus communis</i>) as trap crop <br/>-&nbsp;In Rabi season dont grow sunflower (<i>Helianthus annuus</i>), groundnut (<i>Arachys hypogaea</i>) or Sesamum crop<br/>-&nbsp;Adopt the plant protection measures on a community basis to get maximum benefits<br/>
    -&nbsp;Collect and destroy eggs and larvae of the pest<br/>-&nbsp;Higher infestation of pest observed in August month<br/>-&nbsp;Install pheromone traps 10 per ha (use Spodo lure) <br/>-&nbsp;Install light traps in field from 07 to 09 PM<br/>
    -&nbsp;Application of neem seed kernel extract 5%  <br/>-&nbsp;Application of <i>Beauveria bassiana</i> or <i>Nomuraea rileyi</i> or <i>Metarhizium anisopliae</i>  40gm/10litre water<br/>-&nbsp;Install of bird perches at 10-12/ha. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray SL NPV (nuclear polyhedrosis virus of <i>Spodoptera litura</i>) 5 ml  (500LE/ha)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray biocides at proper humidity level (more than 80%), spray in morning or evening time <br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray chlorpyriphos 20EC at 20 ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), organophosphate<br/>-&nbsp;Spray emamectin benzoate 5 SG at 5 g.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), macrocyclic lactone, systemic with contact and stomach action<br/>-&nbsp;Spray profenofos 50 EC at 25 ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), organophosphate, non-systemic with stomach and contact action.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray rynaxpyr 20 SC at 2ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by WHO<br/>-&nbsp;Spray spinosad 5 SG at 4 g.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (Slightly hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray indoxacarb 14.5 SC at 10 ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), oxadiazine insecticide with contact and stomach action<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Spodoptera litura</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_90302.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_90304.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_90305.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Deep ploughing in summer season <br/>-&nbsp;Use castor (<i>Ricinus communis</i>) as trap crop <br/>-&nbsp;In Rabi season dont grow sunflower (<i>Helianthus annuus</i>), groundnut (<i>Arachys hypogaea</i>) or Sesamum crop<br/>-&nbsp;Adopt the plant protection measures on a community basis to get maximum benefits<br/> -&nbsp;Collect and destroy eggs and larvae of the pest<br/>-&nbsp;Higher infestation of pest observed in August month<br/>-&nbsp;Install pheromone traps 10 per ha (use Spodo lure) <br/>-&nbsp;Install light traps in field from 07 to 09 PM<br/> -&nbsp;Application of neem seed kernel extract 5%  <br/>-&nbsp;Application of <i>Beauveria bassiana</i> or <i>Nomuraea rileyi</i> or <i>Metarhizium anisopliae</i>  40gm/10litre water<br/>-&nbsp;Install of bird perches at 10-12/ha. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray SL NPV (nuclear polyhedrosis virus of <i>Spodoptera litura</i>) 5 ml  (500LE/ha)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray biocides at proper humidity level (more than 80%), spray in morning or evening time <br/> -&nbsp;Spray chlorpyriphos 20EC at 20 ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), organophosphate<br/>-&nbsp;Spray emamectin benzoate 5 SG at 5 g.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), macrocyclic lactone, systemic with contact and stomach action<br/>-&nbsp;Spray profenofos 50 EC at 25 ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), organophosphate, non-systemic with stomach and contact action.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray rynaxpyr 20 SC at 2ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by WHO<br/>-&nbsp;Spray spinosad 5 SG at 4 g.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (Slightly hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray indoxacarb 14.5 SC at 10 ml.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), oxadiazine insecticide with contact and stomach action<br/>

Title: Cashew Stem and Root Borer
Authors:   Dr.V.R.Saminathan (TNAU), Mr.G.Sudakar ( MSSRF), Dr. K.Chozhan (TNAU), Ms.D.S.Girija (MSSRF)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Swabbing the trunk with neem oil 5% for three times in a year. (Jan- Feb, May - June, Sep-Oct)<br/>-&nbsp;Swabbing the trunk with coaltar once in a year <br/>-&nbsp;Uproot and destory the completely damaged trees.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitoring the gummosis (oozing of gumlike substance) at the base of the tree.<br/>-&nbsp;Presence of chewed up material or excreta at the base of the tree.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for the presence of eggs (resembling rice grains) on and underneath the bark<br/>
    -&nbsp;Application of <i>Metarhizium anisopliae</i> suspension on the excreta protruding outside the bore hole. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Drenching the ground around the affected plant with chlorpyriphos 0.2% (2ml per litre of water).&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Repeated drenching shall be avoided to reduce residue accumulation in the soil.<br/>-&nbsp;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (moderately hazardous ), organophosphate, non systemic insecticide with contact, stomach and respiratory action.<br/>
Scientific Names: Thandu matrum ver thulaipan
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_91125.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Swabbing the trunk with neem oil 5% for three times in a year. (Jan- Feb, May - June, Sep-Oct)<br/>-&nbsp;Swabbing the trunk with coaltar once in a year <br/>-&nbsp;Uproot and destory the completely damaged trees.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitoring the gummosis (oozing of gumlike substance) at the base of the tree.<br/>-&nbsp;Presence of chewed up material or excreta at the base of the tree.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for the presence of eggs (resembling rice grains) on and underneath the bark<br/> -&nbsp;Application of <i>Metarhizium anisopliae</i> suspension on the excreta protruding outside the bore hole. <br/> -&nbsp;Drenching the ground around the affected plant with chlorpyriphos 0.2% (2ml per litre of water).&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Repeated drenching shall be avoided to reduce residue accumulation in the soil.<br/>-&nbsp;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (moderately hazardous ), organophosphate, non systemic insecticide with contact, stomach and respiratory action.<br/>

Title: Maize aphid
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Sow early (before the onset of rains) so that ears appear before the peak period of aphid populations<br/>-&nbsp;Provide adequate nutrients to soil with manure to grow healthy plants<br/>-&nbsp;Provide adequate irrigation during the silk stage to reduce or eliminate aphid damage<br/>-&nbsp;Eliminate weeds and host plants, such as Johnson grass, from around the farm <br/>-&nbsp;Practise crop rotation with non-cereal crops e.g. beans, cowpeas, etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Encourage natural enemies such as parasitic wasps, lady beetles, syrphid fly larvae and lacewings by reducing the amount of chemicals used in the field<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor protected locations on the plant (i.e. within the whorl, in the curl of the leaves, upper part of the cornstalk) during whorl stage for dark green to bluish-green nymphs and adults<br/>-&nbsp;Infestation usually starts on the leaf whorls, unemerged heads and tassels. The most severe damage occurs between late-whorl and pollination stages<br/>-&nbsp;In heavy infestation, feeding may cause leaf curling, wilting and yellow mottling, and stunting of the whole plant<br/>-&nbsp;Abundant production of honeydew by aphids results in sooty mould growth, and tassels and upper leaves may become completely covered preventing pollen release<br/>-&nbsp;Ants are attracted by honeydew secretions; monitor ant activity at the base of the plants<br/>-&nbsp;<i>R. maidis</i> is not of major importance and often doesn't need control, unless transmitting viruses (it is a vector of maize dwarf mosaic virus and maize leaf-fleck virus)<br/>-&nbsp;Act only if 50 % of the plants monitored have more than 100 aphids/plant, and plants are under drought stress<br/>
    -&nbsp;If available, release biological control agents such as <i>Aphelinus varipes</i>, <i>Lysiphlebus testaceipes</i> and <i>L. mirzai</i><br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Rhopalosiphum maidis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96512.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96513.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96514.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Sow early (before the onset of rains) so that ears appear before the peak period of aphid populations<br/>-&nbsp;Provide adequate nutrients to soil with manure to grow healthy plants<br/>-&nbsp;Provide adequate irrigation during the silk stage to reduce or eliminate aphid damage<br/>-&nbsp;Eliminate weeds and host plants, such as Johnson grass, from around the farm <br/>-&nbsp;Practise crop rotation with non-cereal crops e.g. beans, cowpeas, etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Encourage natural enemies such as parasitic wasps, lady beetles, syrphid fly larvae and lacewings by reducing the amount of chemicals used in the field<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor protected locations on the plant (i.e. within the whorl, in the curl of the leaves, upper part of the cornstalk) during whorl stage for dark green to bluish-green nymphs and adults<br/>-&nbsp;Infestation usually starts on the leaf whorls, unemerged heads and tassels. The most severe damage occurs between late-whorl and pollination stages<br/>-&nbsp;In heavy infestation, feeding may cause leaf curling, wilting and yellow mottling, and stunting of the whole plant<br/>-&nbsp;Abundant production of honeydew by aphids results in sooty mould growth, and tassels and upper leaves may become completely covered preventing pollen release<br/>-&nbsp;Ants are attracted by honeydew secretions; monitor ant activity at the base of the plants<br/>-&nbsp;<i>R. maidis</i> is not of major importance and often doesn't need control, unless transmitting viruses (it is a vector of maize dwarf mosaic virus and maize leaf-fleck virus)<br/>-&nbsp;Act only if 50 % of the plants monitored have more than 100 aphids/plant, and plants are under drought stress<br/> -&nbsp;If available, release biological control agents such as <i>Aphelinus varipes</i>, <i>Lysiphlebus testaceipes</i> and <i>L. mirzai</i><br/> Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.

Title: Paddy  Bacterial Leaf Blight
Authors:   Dr. K. Rajappan, Dr. Malarvannan, Mr. Vijay S. Thokre, Ms. Rajeshwari (MSSRF)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Grow Tolerant varieties (IR 20, IR 72, TKM 6)<br/>-&nbsp;Secure disease free seed and from disease free source<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with Pseudomonas fluorescens at 10 gm per kg seed in 1 lit of water overnight<br/>-&nbsp;Establish nurseries preferably away from the main field and in upland conditions<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid injuries of seedlings during transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply Nitrogen (N) fertilizer based on Leaf Colour Chart. Skip N application at booting stage (if disease is moderate).<br/>-&nbsp;Drain the field (except at flowering stage of the crop)<br/>-&nbsp;Destruction of weeds and collateral hosts (e.g. Watergrass, Barnyard grass)<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid flow of water from affected fields<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain proper plant spacing 20X15 cm <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor Irrigation channels to avoid water from affected fields. <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for disease free tools for intercultural operations<br/>
    -&nbsp;Regular observation after 45 DAT for temperature (25-30 C), humidity (> 90%), splash rains and deep water (>2.5 cm height for a week).<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor after 45 DAT for leaf tip drying with yellow margins and follow the oozing test by cutting the cross section of the leaf in a pure water. (Also check for the development of streaks on the leaves for the possible cause of Bacterial Leaf Streak disease).<br/>-&nbsp;Disease score exceeds 3 (5-25% leaf area infected) then follow curative measures. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid continuous deep water, water from affected fields and use of infected tools  <br/>-&nbsp;Spray Pseudomonas fluorescens at 1kg per acre with 200 lit. of water <br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil 30 ml per lit of water or neem seed kernel powder 50 gm of 1 lit of water<br/>-&nbsp;Application of bleaching powder @ 2 kg/acre in the irrigation water at Kresek stage (>60 DAT)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Bacterial leaf blight is air borne so apply recommended chemicals on entire crop<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Plantomycin 7 SP @ 100 gm per acre in 200 lit of water when the disease attains grade 3.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Plantomycin is not classified by WHO but should be used with care<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Streptomycin sulphate + Tetracycline combination 120g + Copper oxychloride 500g per acre (200 Lit water).&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Streptomycin sulphate and Tetracycline not classified by WHO but should be used with care. Copper oxychloride: WHO class II (Moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Xanthomonas oryzae pv. oryzae (Oryza sativa)</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96709.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96711.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96712.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Grow Tolerant varieties (IR 20, IR 72, TKM 6)<br/>-&nbsp;Secure disease free seed and from disease free source<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with Pseudomonas fluorescens at 10 gm per kg seed in 1 lit of water overnight<br/>-&nbsp;Establish nurseries preferably away from the main field and in upland conditions<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid injuries of seedlings during transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply Nitrogen (N) fertilizer based on Leaf Colour Chart. Skip N application at booting stage (if disease is moderate).<br/>-&nbsp;Drain the field (except at flowering stage of the crop)<br/>-&nbsp;Destruction of weeds and collateral hosts (e.g. Watergrass, Barnyard grass)<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid flow of water from affected fields<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain proper plant spacing 20X15 cm <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor Irrigation channels to avoid water from affected fields. <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for disease free tools for intercultural operations<br/> -&nbsp;Regular observation after 45 DAT for temperature (25-30 C), humidity (> 90%), splash rains and deep water (>2.5 cm height for a week).<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor after 45 DAT for leaf tip drying with yellow margins and follow the oozing test by cutting the cross section of the leaf in a pure water. (Also check for the development of streaks on the leaves for the possible cause of Bacterial Leaf Streak disease).<br/>-&nbsp;Disease score exceeds 3 (5-25% leaf area infected) then follow curative measures. <br/> -&nbsp;Avoid continuous deep water, water from affected fields and use of infected tools  <br/>-&nbsp;Spray Pseudomonas fluorescens at 1kg per acre with 200 lit. of water <br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil 30 ml per lit of water or neem seed kernel powder 50 gm of 1 lit of water<br/>-&nbsp;Application of bleaching powder @ 2 kg/acre in the irrigation water at Kresek stage (>60 DAT)<br/> -&nbsp;Bacterial leaf blight is air borne so apply recommended chemicals on entire crop<br/> -&nbsp;Spray Plantomycin 7 SP @ 100 gm per acre in 200 lit of water when the disease attains grade 3.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Plantomycin is not classified by WHO but should be used with care<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Streptomycin sulphate + Tetracycline combination 120g + Copper oxychloride 500g per acre (200 Lit water).&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Streptomycin sulphate and Tetracycline not classified by WHO but should be used with care. Copper oxychloride: WHO class II (Moderately hazardous).<br/>

Title: Yellow Sigatoka Leaf Spot in Banana 
Authors:   Dr. K. Rajappan, Dr. Malarvannan, Mr. Vijay S. Thokre, Ms. Rajeshwari (MSSRF) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Secure suckers from disease free source <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid injuries of rhizomes during planting.g.<br/>-&nbsp;Choose well drained field for planting. <br/>-&nbsp;Destruction of weeds and collateral hosts (e.g. Canna indica) <br/>-&nbsp;Field sanitation & restriction of water flowing from affected field <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain proper spacing according to varieties  <br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for appearance of yellow colour spots on leaves after 2 months of planting.  Later these spots turn to spherical in shape with grey centre & brown margin <br/>-&nbsp;Observe the temperature because lower temperature (<210 C) favours the disease  <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor disease free tools used for intercultural operations<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for water logging in the field<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water logging in the fields  <br/>
    -&nbsp;Removal and destruction of affected leaves. <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water flowing from affected fields<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Bordeaux mixture 10 ml + linseed oil 20 ml / lit  of water at initial occurrence of the disease   <br/>
    -&nbsp;Sigatoka Leaf Spot in Banana is air borne, apply one of the recommended chemicals on entire crop<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Carbendazim  @ 0.5  gm / lit of water;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Carbendazim: WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Mancozeb 2.25 gm / lit of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole: WHO Class II, (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Propiconazole @   0.5ml / lit of water .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Mancozeb: WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Tridemorph @ 0.5 ml / lit of water .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Tridemorph: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Add Teepol (sticking agent)  0.5  ml / lit of water in each spraying<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Mycosphaerella musicola</i>

Later these spots turn to spherical in shape with grey centre & brown margin <br/>-&nbsp;Observe the temperature because lower temperature (<210 C) favours the disease  <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor disease free tools used for intercultural operations<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for water logging in the field<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water logging in the fields  <br/> -&nbsp;Removal and destruction of affected leaves. <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water flowing from affected fields<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Bordeaux mixture 10 ml + linseed oil 20 ml / lit  of water at initial occurrence of the disease   <br/> -&nbsp;Sigatoka Leaf Spot in Banana is air borne, apply one of the recommended chemicals on entire crop<br/> -&nbsp;Spray Carbendazim  @ 0.5  gm / lit of water;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Carbendazim: WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Mancozeb 2.25 gm / lit of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole: WHO Class II, (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Propiconazole @   0.5ml / lit of water .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Mancozeb: WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Tridemorph @ 0.5 ml / lit of water .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Tridemorph: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Add Teepol (sticking agent)  0.5  ml / lit of water in each spraying<br/>

Title: Blackgram Pod Borer 
Authors:   Dr. Raja. Ramesh (TNAU), Ms. D.S. Girija (MSSRF), Dr. Rajeswari (MSSRF) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep summer ploughing (30 cm) to expose pupae present in the soil.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with non host crops like paddy and Brinjal<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve the natural enemies like Lady bird beetle, Ground beetle, Praying mantis, Pentatomid bug, etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Installation of light traps 1/acre of land.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for the defoliation of leaves from 20 to 35 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for green coloured larva with black band laterally on leaves. Later the larvae move on to flowers and fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for bored fruits with round holes. Notice the larvae thrust their head inside the pod leaving the body outside.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the economic threshold level up to 10% of affected pods.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for warm weather condition followed by light rains and dry spells which is favourable for pest.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Collection and destruction of larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Place bird perches @ 20 nos/acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem Seed Kernel powder @ 50g/ litre of water or Neem Oil @ 30 ml/litre twice at the time of flowering and early pod formation stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of <i>Helicoverpa armigera</i> Pheromone trap @ 5 nos/acre<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray <i>Chlorotraniliprole</i> 18.5% SC @ 40 ml/acre during flowering stage.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class U/IV (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray <i>Indoxacarb</i> 14.5 SC @ 0.75ml/litre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Emmamectin benzoate 5% SC @ 50 gm/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Emmamectin benzoate is not classified by WHO but is considered highly toxic and should be used with care<br/>-&nbsp;Thiodicarb 75%WP @ 250 gm/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Flubendamide 480 SC @

40 ml/acre.

.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Flubendamide is not classified by WHO<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Helicoverpa armigera</i>

Content:
-&nbsp;Deep summer ploughing (30 cm) to expose pupae present in the soil.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with non host crops like paddy and Brinjal<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve the natural enemies like Lady bird beetle, Ground beetle, Praying mantis, Pentatomid bug, etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Installation of light traps 1/acre of land.<br/> -&nbsp;Observe for the defoliation of leaves from 20 to 35 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for green coloured larva with black band laterally on leaves. Later the larvae move on to flowers and fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for bored fruits with round holes. Notice the larvae thrust their head inside the pod leaving the body outside.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the economic threshold level up to 10% of affected pods.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for warm weather condition followed by light rains and dry spells which is favourable for pest.<br/> -&nbsp;Collection and destruction of larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Place bird perches @ 20 nos/acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem Seed Kernel powder @ 50g/ litre of water or Neem Oil @ 30 ml/litre twice at the time of flowering and early pod formation stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of <i>Helicoverpa armigera</i> Pheromone trap @ 5 nos/acre<br/> -&nbsp;Spray <i>Chlorotraniliprole</i> 18.5% SC @ 40 ml/acre during flowering stage.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class U/IV (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray <i>Indoxacarb</i> 14.5 SC @ 0.75ml/litre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Emmamectin benzoate 5% SC @ 50 gm/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Emmamectin benzoate is not classified by WHO but is considered highly toxic and should be used with care<br/>-&nbsp;Thiodicarb 75%WP @ 250 gm/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Flubendamide 480 SC @

Title: Brinjal Fruit and Shoot Borer
Authors:   Dr. Raja. Ramesh (TNAU), Ms. D.S. Girija (MSSRF), Dr. Rajeswari (MSSRF) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Grow less susceptible varieties like Pusa Purple Round, Brinjal Long green, Pusa purple cluster, Brinjal round white and Annamalai.  In general, short and cylindrical varieties are more susceptible when compared to long and elongated varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding mono-cropping of Brinjal.<br/>-&nbsp;Adjust the time of transplanting at fourth week of June.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe burrows in the petiole and tender shoots. Later drooping of leaves and shedding of flower buds.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for bore holes in the fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe the ETL @ 5% fruit damage.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Carry out shoot clipping at weekly interval <br/>-&nbsp;Collect and destroy the affected terminal shoots showing bore holes and fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Release the larval parasitoid <i>Pristomers testaceus</i> or <i>Cremastus flavoorbitalis</i><br/>-&nbsp;Install pheromone traps @ 4 per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of Neem cake @ 25 gms per plant 45 days after transplanting. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray Azadirachtin 0.03% @ 3ml/litre, from one month after transplanting at 15 days interval<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid using synthetic pyrethroids<br/>
    -&nbsp;Dip the roots of seedlings for three hours in Imidacloprid @ 1ml/litre before transplanting.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;On severe infestation, foliar application of Chlorantraniliprole 18.5% SC @ 0.75 ml/ litre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Carbaryl 50 WP @ 2g/ litre from one month after transplanting at 15 days interval.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Carbosulfon 25% EC @ 3.5 ml/litre (or) Cartap hydrochoride 50% SP @ 3 gm / litre (or) Emamectin Benzoate 5% WG @ 1 gm/ litre twice at the interval of 15 days. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Carbosulfan and Cartap- WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)

Emmamectin Benzoate- not classified by WHO but considered toxic and should be used with care.

<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Leucinodes orbonalis</i> 
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96818.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96821.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Grow less susceptible varieties like Pusa Purple Round, Brinjal Long green, Pusa purple cluster, Brinjal round white and Annamalai.  In general, short and cylindrical varieties are more susceptible when compared to long and elongated varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding mono-cropping of Brinjal.<br/>-&nbsp;Adjust the time of transplanting at fourth week of June.<br/> -&nbsp;Observe burrows in the petiole and tender shoots. Later drooping of leaves and shedding of flower buds.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for bore holes in the fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe the ETL @ 5% fruit damage.<br/> -&nbsp;Carry out shoot clipping at weekly interval <br/>-&nbsp;Collect and destroy the affected terminal shoots showing bore holes and fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Release the larval parasitoid <i>Pristomers testaceus</i> or <i>Cremastus flavoorbitalis</i><br/>-&nbsp;Install pheromone traps @ 4 per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of Neem cake @ 25 gms per plant 45 days after transplanting. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray Azadirachtin 0.03% @ 3ml/litre, from one month after transplanting at 15 days interval<br/> -&nbsp;Avoid using synthetic pyrethroids<br/> -&nbsp;Dip the roots of seedlings for three hours in Imidacloprid @ 1ml/litre before transplanting.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;On severe infestation, foliar application of Chlorantraniliprole 18.5% SC @ 0.75 ml/ litre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Carbaryl 50 WP @ 2g/ litre from one month after transplanting at 15 days interval.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Carbosulfon 25% EC @ 3.5 ml/litre (or) Cartap hydrochoride 50% SP @ 3 gm / litre (or) Emamectin Benzoate 5% WG @ 1 gm/ litre twice at the interval of 15 days. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Carbosulfan and Cartap- WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)

Emmamectin Benzoate- not classified by WHO but considered toxic and should be used with care.

Title: Paddy Gallmidge
Authors:   Dr. Raja. Ramesh (TNAU), Ms. D.S. Girija (MSSRF), Dr. Rajeswari (MSSRF) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Grow resistant varieties. For Short duration, use varieties like ADT 45, 48 and IR 36. For Medium and Long duration varieties  MDU 3, ADT 39.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid late sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove alternate weed hosts such as sedges and grasses<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid close spacing.<br/>-&nbsp;Flood irrigation reduces the incidence of gall midge.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with pulses.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies like spider, Praying Mantis, Dragon fly, Water strider etc.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for formation of tube like galls from nursery to active tillering stage <br/>-&nbsp;Observe regularly for tube galls (silver shoot) during 35 to 45 DAT. <br/>-&nbsp;Observe for relative humidity 83 to 87% with intermittent rain from September to November which is favourable for pest.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for mosquito like yellow or brown coloured insects with long legs during early hours.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the economic threshold level up to 10% of silver shoot.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Follow spacing of 22.5 x 22.5 cm while transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Set up light traps 1/5 acre <br/>-&nbsp;Release of <i>Platygaster oryzae</i> 1/10m2 on 10 DAT<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Thiomethoxam 25 WG @ 40gm/acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Thiomethoxam not classified by WHO<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Carbosulfan 25 EC@ 400ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Fipronil 5 SC @ 500gm/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Chlorpyriphos 50EC @ 400 to 500ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Orseolia oryzae</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96822.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96825.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96826.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Powdery Mildew of Black gram
Authors:   Dr.Raja, Dr.Rajeswari (MSSRF), Ms.D.S.Girija (MSSRF), Vijay Thokre
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use seeds from disease free source<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment for one hour with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> or <i>Trichoderma viride</i> @ 4g/kg of seed.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy the collateral hosts of the soybean, lentil, clover, wild bean near bunds<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe weekly for white patches on the upper surface of the leaves and other green parts from 35 to 40 days of sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;If the relative humidity increase more than 90% monitor for white patches on upper surface every alternative day from 30 days of sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for premature defoliation of plants at pod setting stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the distorted and shrivelled pods for severe infection.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove and destroy the infected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem Seed Kernel extract 50ml/ litre of water or Neem Oil 30ml/litre twice at ten days interval from initial disease appearance.

or<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Eucalyptus Leaf extract 10% at the initiation of disease and repeat after ten days.<br/>-&nbsp;After harvest debris should be collected and buried for composting with FYM.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Wettable sulphur 80% WDG 600g or Propiconazole 25% EC or Flusilazole 40% EC@ 200ml / acre in 200 litre of water twice at initiation of disease and ten days later.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole, Flusilazole -WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous). Wettable Sulphur - WHO class III (Slightly hazardous). Flusilazole- WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Or spray Carbendazim @ 200g/acre in 200 litre of water at initiation of disease and repeat after ten days.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Carbendazim - WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Erysiphe polygoni</i> 
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_96827.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Use seeds from disease free source<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment for one hour with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> or <i>Trichoderma viride</i> @ 4g/kg of seed.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy the collateral hosts of the soybean, lentil, clover, wild bean near bunds<br/> -&nbsp;Observe weekly for white patches on the upper surface of the leaves and other green parts from 35 to 40 days of sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;If the relative humidity increase more than 90% monitor for white patches on upper surface every alternative day from 30 days of sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for premature defoliation of plants at pod setting stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the distorted and shrivelled pods for severe infection.<br/> -&nbsp;Remove and destroy the infected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem Seed Kernel extract 50ml/ litre of water or Neem Oil 30ml/litre twice at ten days interval from initial disease appearance.

Title: Potato moth
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;<b>Use of certified seeds</b><br/>-&nbsp;Good soil preparation: remove and destroy the field residues of the previous crop, volunteer potatoes and weeds, and deep plough<br/>-&nbsp;Deep planting (10 cm) and high hilling of 25 cm prevent moths to lay their eggs on exposed tubers<br/>-&nbsp;Intercrop potatoes with onions to reduce infestation<br/>-&nbsp;Use repellent plants (use neem leaves as soil cover during the last 4 weeks before harvesting)<br/>-&nbsp;Irrigate the ground often to prevent soil cracks from forming. Moths will otherwise lie in the cracks and be protected<br/>-&nbsp;Timely harvest (do not wait to harvest). Cut foliage when plants show the typical yellowing of physiological maturity to limit shelter for adult moths<br/>-&nbsp;Good selection of tubers before storing<br/>-&nbsp;Move the harvest immediately to store to avoid the moth infesting the tubers in the field<br/>-&nbsp;Storage: disinfect the storage area before storing the tubers; protect the door and windows with mesh; store in cool, dry places; diffused light<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation (avoid rotation with susceptible hosts such as tomato, tabaco, eggplant and sweet peppers)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor every week for symptoms on leaves, stems and tubers, or for the moths, from planting to harvest<br/>-&nbsp;Mines in the leaves, petioles and stems<br/>-&nbsp;Weakened or broken stems<br/>-&nbsp;Irregular galleries within tubers caused by the larvae (twice a week, cut and check 10 stored tubers)<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor during late afternoon for adults flying around plants. The adult is a brown moth of 1 cm. The eggs are deposited individually or in groups on leaves or exposed tubers<br/>-&nbsp;Use pheromone traps in the field to detect adults (10-20 traps/ha). Take control measures when there are over 20 moths per trap<br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove and destroy infected tubers outside the field<br/>-&nbsp;Cut the potato plants 10 to 15 days before harvest to kill adults remaining in the plants<br/>-&nbsp;Release parasitoids available in your country (i.e. <i>Bracon gelechiae</i> or <i>Copidosoma koehleri</i>) or spray with entomopathogenic nematodes such as <i>Steinernema carpocapsae</i><br/>-&nbsp;Cover the tubers in storage with neem leaves. Put a blanket under and over the tuber piles<br/>-&nbsp;In storage, apply on the tubers a powder preparation of <i>Baculovirus phthorimaea</i>, if locally available<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Phthorimaea operculella</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_98106.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_98107.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_98108.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;<b>Use of certified seeds</b><br/>-&nbsp;Good soil preparation: remove and destroy the field residues of the previous crop, volunteer potatoes and weeds, and deep plough<br/>-&nbsp;Deep planting (10 cm) and high hilling of 25 cm prevent moths to lay their eggs on exposed tubers<br/>-&nbsp;Intercrop potatoes with onions to reduce infestation<br/>-&nbsp;Use repellent plants (use neem leaves as soil cover during the last 4 weeks before harvesting)<br/>-&nbsp;Irrigate the ground often to prevent soil cracks from forming. Title: Citrus leafminer
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Avoid using susceptible varieties like grapefruit and pomelos<br/>-&nbsp;Restrict the application of fertilizers during sprouting season, especially those containing nitrogen. Apply fertilizers when the pest population is low or absent to promote sprouting and prevent optimal conditions for the pest<br/>-&nbsp;Prune once a year to reduce sprouting and induce a uniform and short cycle<br/>-&nbsp;Remove vigorous shoots below and above the graft union on the trunk of mature trees as they produce new leaves for a long period of time<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid using insecticides to conserve natural enemies (parasitoids and predators)<br/>-&nbsp;Collect and burn fallen leaves<br/>
    -&nbsp;Adult: A small moth (3 mm long) yellowish grey with black spots at the bottom of the wings. The edge of the hind wings are covered of hair. This leafminer is different than the carob bean moth which attack the fruits and branches<br/>-&nbsp;Larvae: Feed on the undersides of the leaves under the epidermis causing serpentine mines initiating near the vein. The damages cause deformation and leafrolling<br/>-&nbsp;Pupa: Brown coloured and found in mines and rolled onto the edges of the leaves<br/>-&nbsp;This pest causes more damage in nurseries slowing the growth of young plants<br/>-&nbsp;In plantations of less than 5 years: sample 2 shoots/tree on leaves less than 20 mm long (total of 50 trees). Start monitoring when 25% of plants begin to sprout and repeat at 50% of sprounting<br/>-&nbsp;Place one pheromone trap per 5 acres in a citrus tree to determine the date when adults are active. Review the traps each week <br/>-&nbsp;Apply control measures when adults are active and several are found in traps or when 10% of samples show leafminer damage<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply mineral oil (0.5%) being careful not to cause phytotoxicity<br/>-&nbsp;In older plantations (over 4 years): although new shoots in mature trees can be damaged heavily, yields and growth of the tree are not affected. In addition, parasitoids normally control this pest, and applying insecticides can kill them<br/>-&nbsp;In new plantations: do not prune damaged twigs/branches<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Phyllocnistis citrella</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99306.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99307.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99308.img?width=800&height=640

Title: Bitter Gourd Downy Mildew
Authors:   Dr. A. Eswaran, Dr. P. Balabaskar, (Annamalai University), Dr. S. Mathiyazhagan (Tamil Nadu Agricultural University), G. Sudhakar
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use resistant cultivars<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain isolation distance from susceptible cucurbit species <br/>-&nbsp;Train (panthal) the vine in such a way to provide adequate aeration and exposure to sunlight<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water logging<br/>-&nbsp;Thin out dense canopy of the vines <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid over head irrigation in disease prone areas<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for white powdery growth on lower surface and yellow discoloration on corresponding upper leaf surface during high moisture condition <br/>-&nbsp;In advance stages entire leaf dries<br/>
    -&nbsp;Rogue out diseased plants and remove affected plant debris from field   <br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Metalaxyl @ 0.1% or Bordeaux mixture @ 1.0%, or Azoxystrobin @ 0.1% at disease initiation stage and repeat at weekly interval.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Metalaxyl - WHO class II, Azoxystrobin - WHO class U<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Pseudoperonospora cubensis</i>

Title: Brinjal Bacterial wilt
Authors:   Dr.  A. Eswaran, Dr. P. Balabaskar (Annamalai University), Dr. S. Mathiyazhagan (Tamil Nadu Agricultural University), G. Sudhakar
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Summer Ploughing<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with  cereals or cruciferous vegetables <br/>-&nbsp;Apply neem cake @ 100 kg /acre to reduce bacterial pathogen<br/>-&nbsp;Solarisation of nursery beds <br/>-&nbsp;Field sanitation by ensuring weed free field.<br/>-&nbsp;Keep land fallow for a season to destroy harmful pathogens<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water logging and provide drainage facility. <br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant variety namely Pant Samrat<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for dropping of lower leaves at mid sunny days<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for vascular browning<br/>-&nbsp;Discharge of milky streaks of bacteria from the ends of cut stems when placed in a glass of water<br/>
    -&nbsp;Rouging of diseased plants and burn<br/>-&nbsp;Rouging of diseased plants and then drench in and around diseased area with copper hydroxide 77%WP @ 3 gms per litre.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply basally talc based 2.5 kg  <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i>/ha precolonized in farm yard manure <br/>-&nbsp;Periodically remove  infected plants <br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply copper hydroxide.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Copper hydroxide: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Ralstonia solanacearum<i>

Title: Brinjal Shoot and Fruit Borer
Authors:   Mr.Nilesh Ganesh Patkar, Dr.Raja.Ramesh (Assistant Professor, ICAR-KVK, TNAU) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Avoid continuous cropping of brinjal crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Grow the varieties, pusa purple round, pusa purple long with long and narrow fruits in endemic areas.<br/>-&nbsp;In general, short and cylindrical varieties are more susceptible when compared to long and elongated varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Adjust the time of transplanting at fourth week of June.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercropping with cowpea, coriander, black gram,  green gram and vegetable cowpea as border crops can enhance the  activity of Braconid parasitoid<br/>-&nbsp;Spray NSKE 50ml per 10 L water to avoid egg laying prior to flowering stage<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor drying of shoots (dead heart) 45-50 days after transplanting <br/>-&nbsp;Observe the egg on the tender shoots <br/>-&nbsp;Observe the fruit bore holes with plugged excreta  <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for economic threshold level of 10% damaged shoots & fruits. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove the affected terminal shoot showing boreholes.<br/>-&nbsp;Carry out shoot clipping at weekly intervals during vegetative phase<br/>-&nbsp;Install Lucin lure sex pheromone traps @ 5 traps/acre for early identification and destruction of the pest.<br/>-&nbsp;Encourage the activity of larval parasitoids:  <i>Pristomerus testaceus</i>, <i>Cremastus flavoorbitalis</i><br/>-&nbsp;Install one light trap (200W mercury vapour lamp) per hectare between 7-9 pm to catch the adults <br/>-&nbsp;Collect and destroy infested shoots and fruits with larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of Neem cake @ 25 gm per plant 45 days after transplanting. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray azadiractin 0.03% @ 3ml/litre, from one month after transplanting at 15 days interval<br/>-&nbsp;Trichogramma chilonis 2 cc/acre release after 45 days after transplanting<br/>-&nbsp;<i>Bt</i> can also used: 250     gm/acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply Phosalone  35% EC @ 300 ml/acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Phosalone: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;In case of severe infestation apply Emamectin benzoate 5% SG @ 50g / acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Emamectin benzoate  not classified by WHO<br/>-&nbsp;On severe infestation, foliar application of chlorantraniliprole 18.5% SC  @ 0.4 ml/ litre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorotraniliprole - WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Leucinodes orbonalis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99418.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99420.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99421.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Avoid continuous cropping of brinjal crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Grow the varieties, pusa purple round, pusa purple long with long and narrow fruits in endemic areas.<br/>-&nbsp;In general, short and cylindrical varieties are more susceptible when compared to long and elongated varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Adjust the time of transplanting at fourth week of June.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercropping with cowpea, coriander, black gram,  green gram and vegetable cowpea as border crops can enhance the  activity of Braconid parasitoid<br/>-&nbsp;Spray NSKE 50ml per 10 L water to avoid egg laying prior to flowering stage<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor drying of shoots (dead heart) 45-50 days after transplanting <br/>-&nbsp;Observe the egg on the tender shoots <br/>-&nbsp;Observe the fruit bore holes with plugged excreta  <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for economic threshold level of 10% damaged shoots & fruits. <br/> -&nbsp;Remove the affected terminal shoot showing boreholes.<br/>-&nbsp;Carry out shoot clipping at weekly intervals during vegetative phase<br/>-&nbsp;Install Lucin lure sex pheromone traps @ 5 traps/acre for early identification and destruction of the pest.<br/>-&nbsp;Encourage the activity of larval parasitoids:  <i>Pristomerus testaceus</i>, <i>Cremastus flavoorbitalis</i><br/>-&nbsp;Install one light trap (200W mercury vapour lamp) per hectare between 7-9 pm to catch the adults <br/>-&nbsp;Collect and destroy infested shoots and fruits with larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of Neem cake @ 25 gm per plant 45 days after transplanting. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray azadiractin 0.03% @ 3ml/litre, from one month after transplanting at 15 days interval<br/>-&nbsp;Trichogramma chilonis 2 cc/acre release after 45 days after transplanting<br/>-&nbsp;<i>Bt</i> can also used: 250     gm/acre.<br/> -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators<br/> -&nbsp;Apply Phosalone  35% EC @ 300 ml/acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Phosalone: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;In case of severe infestation apply Emamectin benzoate 5% SG @ 50g / acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Emamectin benzoate  not classified by WHO<br/>-&nbsp;On severe infestation, foliar application of chlorantraniliprole 18.5% SC  @ 0.4 ml/ litre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorotraniliprole - WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use)<br/>

Title: Chilli Fusarium wilt
Authors:   Dr. A .Eswaran, Dr. P. Balabaskar (Annamalai University), Dr. S. Mathiyazhagan (Tamil Nadu Agricultural University), G. Sudhakar
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep summer ploughing to eliminate soil borne pathogen<br/>-&nbsp;Apply farm yard manure @ 10 tonnes per acre <br/>-&nbsp;Apply neem cake @ 100 kg per acre <br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with non-solanaceous crops<br/>-&nbsp;Use certified and resistant disease-free seeds.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid growing in areas where root knot nematodes are prevalent<br/>
    -&nbsp;Regularly observe  for yellowing and wilting of plants   <br/>-&nbsp;Observe for vascular browning at the basal region of plants<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for root modification/ deformities of diseased plant (root knot nematode infestation)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Roguing of diseased plant<br/>-&nbsp;Apply 2.5 litres of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> or <i>Trichoderma viride</i> precolonized in farm yard manure<br/>-&nbsp;Apply basally <i>Paecilomyces lilacinous</i> @ 2.5 kg/hectare to control root knot nematodes <br/>-&nbsp;Raise seedlings in soil that has been solarised to kill off the pathogen and nematodes.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Treat the seed with Carbendazim @ 2g/kg or <i>Trichoderma viride</i> @ 4g/kg. Soil drenching with Carbendazim 0.1% .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class U<br/>

Title: Chilli Powdery Mildew

Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Avoid planting during November to February in endemic areas<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain proper plant spacing (45 x 30 cm)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for white powdery growth mostly on the lower surface of the leaves during dry humid climate<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for the yellow patches on the upper surface<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for  shedding (leaf fall) of severely infected leaves and fruits<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray disease initiation stage. <i>Ampelomyces quisqualis</i> @ 2% concentration<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Tridemorph @ 0.05% or Wettable sulphur @ 0.3%, at disease initiation stage and repeat once at weekly interval. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Tridemorph falls in WHO class II. Wettable sulphur falls in WHO class III<br/>

Title: Cotton white fly
Authors:   Mr. Nilesh Ganesh Patkar, Dr. Raja.Ramesh (Assistant Professor, ICAR-KVK, TNAU) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Avoid cultivation of alternate host crops like okra, brinjal etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Adopting crop rotation with non-preferred hosts such as sorghum, ragi, maize etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal and destruction of alternate weed hosts viz., <i>Abutilon indicum</i>, <i>Chrozophore rottlari</i>, <i>Solanum nigrum</i> and <i>Hibiscus ficulensus</i> from the fields and neighboring areas and maintaining field sanitation. <br/>-&nbsp;Timely sowing i.e. first week of June up to fourth week of June.<br/>-&nbsp;Late sowing may be avoided and the crop growth should not be extended beyond its normal duration. <br/>-&nbsp;Collection and removal of whitefly infested leaves.<br/>
    -&nbsp;More than 10 white fly observed on the middle portion of the plant on >50% of plants (two out of four plants). <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor blackening of leaves due to sooty mold development caused by honeydew secretions by white fly adults and immatures. <br/>-&nbsp;Blackening of leaves indicates higher level of infestation. <br/>-&nbsp;Flight of adult producing the sooty appearance when the plant is shaken.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitoring the activities of the adult white flies by setting up yellow sticky trap @ 5 /acre at a height of 1 ft above the plant canopy.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Application of any one of the following sprays:<br/>-&nbsp;Neem seed kernel extract 5% (50 ml/L of water) and neem oil @ 3% 30 ml/L of water).<br/>-&nbsp;Fish oil rosin soap 25 g/L of water.<br/>-&nbsp;5% Notchi leaves extract 5% <i>Catharanthus rosea</i> extract<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as Hand gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators. Care should be taken to avoid the repeated spraying of the same chemicals more than two times.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Acetamiprid 20% SP 100 g/hectare,  Azadirachtin 0.15% 500-1000 ml/hectare, Buprofezin 25% SC 1000 ml/hectare or Clothianidin 50% WDG 40- 50 g/ hectare. Diafenthiuron 50%WP 600g/ hectare. Fipronil 5%SC 250-340 ml/ hectare. Imidacloprid 17.8% SL 100 -125 ml/hectare. Thiacloprid 21.7% SC  500-600 ml/ hectare. Thiamethoxam 25%WG 100 g/ hectare.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Buprofezin, Fipronil, Imidacloprid, Thiacloprid, Acetamiprid WHO Class II Moderately Hazardous. Diafenthiuron, Thiamethoxam WHO Class III. Azadirachtin, not classified by WHO<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Bemisia tabaci</i>

Title:  Groundnut bud borer 
Authors:   Mr. Nilesh Ganesh Patkar, Dr. Raja Ramesh (Assistant Professor, ICAR-KVK, TNAU) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Dig or plough immediately after harvest to expose the pupae to predatory birds, other natural enemies and the heat of the sun.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of weeds and plants which serve as alternate hosts.<br/>
    -&nbsp;The larva bores into the terminal buds and shoots and tip of the stem<br/>-&nbsp;The tender leaflets emerging from central spindle will show shot-hole symptoms initially<br/>-&nbsp;In severe infestation emerging leaflets will have only the midribs or several oblong feeding holes<br/>
    -&nbsp;Application of any one of the following sprays.<br/>-&nbsp;Neem seed kernel extract 5% (50 ml/litre of water) and neem oil @ 3% 30 ml/litre of water).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray any one of the following chemicals. Indoxacarb 14.5% SC (0.5 ml/litre ) or Spinosad 45% SC (0.5 ml/litere) or Cypermethrin 25% EC (1 ml/litre) at fortnightly interval from flower bud imitation. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Cyperthethrin, Indoxacarb WHO classification Class II Moderately Hazardous. Spinosad WHO classification Class III Slightly Hazardous<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Anarsia ephippias</i>

Content:

Title: Groundnut tikka leaf spot
Authors:   Dr. A. Eswaran, Dr. P. Balabaskar (Annamalai University), Dr. S. Mathiyazhagan (Tamil Nadu Agricultural University), G. Sudhakar
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Removal of infected plant debris<br/>-&nbsp;Deep summer ploughing <br/>-&nbsp;Apply farm yard manure @ 10 tonnes per acre <br/>-&nbsp;Apply neem cake @ 100 kg /acre<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with pearl millet and sorghum<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of volunteer seedlings from surrounding fields and from rotation crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Leaf spots although initially chlorotic soon become oval dark brown with chlorotic margins<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for development of chlorotic spots on  leaflets, petioles and stem <br/>-&nbsp;Premature senescence (leaf fall) of leaves in advanced stages<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray 10% <i>Calotropis</i> leaf extract at disease initiation<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Two sprays with carbendazim 100 g + mancozeb 400g/acre, first at appearance of symptoms followed up with second spray at 15 days intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Carbendazim  and mancozeb are WHO class U<br/>-&nbsp;Alternatively, spray Chlorothalonil 400g / acre or Tebuconazole 0.1%. First spray at appearance of symptoms and second spray at 15 day intervals. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Tebuconazole  are WHO class II, Chlorothalonil  falls in WHO class U and Tebuconazole are WHO class II<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Mycosphaerella arachidis</i>, <i>Mycosphaerella berkeleyi</i>

Content:

Title: Maize Fusarium stalk rot 
Authors:   Dr. A. Eswaran, Dr. P. Balabaskar, (Annamalai University) Dr. S. Mathiyazhagan (Tamil Nadu Agricultural University), G. Sudhakar 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep summer ploughing to eliminate soil borne pathogen<br/>-&nbsp;Apply farm yard manure @ 10 tonnes per acre<br/>-&nbsp;Basal  application of neem cake @ 100 kg/acre <br/>-&nbsp;Use certified seeds of resistant  varieties viz., Ranjit, Ganga 5 and TNAU Maize hybrid Co 6<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain plant spacing 60 x 30 cm (ridges and furrow systems)<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water stress during flowering stage<br/>-&nbsp;Apply potash 30 kg/ac during flowering phase<br/>-&nbsp;Improve drainage facilities<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe  yellowing of young (new leaf) leaves and wilting (drooping) symptoms at flowering stage  <br/>-&nbsp;Observe reddish browning of infected  maize stalk at advanced stage<br/>
    -&nbsp;Rouging of diseased plant <br/>-&nbsp;Apply basally 2.5 kg talc based /hectare  or 2.5 litres of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> or talc based  2.5 kg of <i>Bacillus subtilis</i> precolonized in 100 kg of farm yard manure <br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Trichoderma viride</i> (4g/kg of seeds) or <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> (10g/kg of seed)<br/>-&nbsp;Trenching of 2% lime solution in affected soil to reduce secondary infestation.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Treat the seed with carbendazim 4g/kg.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class U<br/>

Title: Mango Leafhopper
Authors:   Mr. Nilesh Ganesh Patkar, Dr. Raja. Ramesh (Assistant Professor, ICAR-KVK, TNAU)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Avoid close planting, as the incidence is very severe in overcrowded orchards. (1010m)<br/>-&nbsp;Orchards must be kept clean by ploughing and removal of weeds.<br/>-&nbsp;Prune dried branches, shoot, twigs during July and burn it. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray Dimethoate 35 EC @ 2 ml per liter of water immediately after pruning  during  2nd week July followed with a second spray at 15 days interval <br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe the hoppers on inflorescences (flowers)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray neem oil 3%  or neem seed kernel powder extract 5 % @ 50 ml/litre of water at the initiation of inflorescence (December)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray <i>Beauveria brongniartii</i> @ 4 gm /litre of water in December.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray acephate 75 SP @ 1g/litres or phosalone 35 EC @ 1.5 ml/litres in December or January at the time emergence of inflorescence followed with second spray after 15 days interval.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Acephate, phosalone, Dimethoate : WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Idioscopus niveosparsus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99438.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99440.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Avoid close planting, as the incidence is very severe in overcrowded orchards. (1010m)<br/>-&nbsp;Orchards must be kept clean by ploughing and removal of weeds.<br/>-&nbsp;Prune dried branches, shoot, twigs during July and burn it. <br/>-&nbsp;Spray Dimethoate 35 EC @ 2 ml per liter of water immediately after pruning  during  2nd week July followed with a second spray at 15 days interval <br/> -&nbsp;Observe the hoppers on inflorescences (flowers)<br/> -&nbsp;Spray neem oil 3%  or neem seed kernel powder extract 5 % @ 50 ml/litre of water at the initiation of inflorescence (December)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray <i>Beauveria brongniartii</i> @ 4 gm /litre of water in December.<br/> -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/> -&nbsp;Spray acephate 75 SP @ 1g/litres or phosalone 35 EC @ 1.5 ml/litres in December or January at the time emergence of inflorescence followed with second spray after 15 days interval.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Acephate, phosalone, Dimethoate : WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>

Title: Mango mealy bug
Authors:   Dr. N. Vijiyakumar, Ms.Girija
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Prune the unwanted and undesirable branches and twigs during September once in two years.<br/>-&nbsp;Deep ploughing during December in between the plant rows.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove weeds and alternate hosts in the orchard using a mini tractor and burn the stubbles.<br/>-&nbsp;Banding of tree trunks with polythene sheet (400 gauge, 30 cm wide) at a height of about 30 cm from the ground level. Grease should be applied at the lower edge of band during December to prevent pink to brown coloured nymphs crawling up the tree.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Look for white coloured cottony cushion every 2-3 days from December to January.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the honeydew secretion by mealy bugs as well as the presence of ants. (Phoresis)<br/>-&nbsp;Inspect for the presence of sooty mould on leaves and twigs<br/>
    -&nbsp;Release 10-15 grubs of coccinellid predator, <i>Cryptolemus montrozieri</i> per tree. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of <i>Beauveria bassiana</i> @ 2 gms per litre of water  or 5% Neem Seed Kernel Extract (5 gms per 10 litres of water) around the tree trunk during December-January. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of <i>Lecanicillum lecanii</i> @ 4 gm per litre of water during dawn hours for effective mycosis.<br/>-&nbsp;If the number of mealy bug colonies are low, smear the colonies with kerosene using paint brush in young plants.<br/>
    -&nbsp; Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of Profenophos 50 EC 2ml/litre of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Profenophos  WHO class II.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Drosicha Mangiferae</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99441.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99443.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Prune the unwanted and undesirable branches and twigs during September once in two years.<br/>-&nbsp;Deep ploughing during December in between the plant rows.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove weeds and alternate hosts in the orchard using a mini tractor and burn the stubbles.<br/>-&nbsp;Banding of tree trunks with polythene sheet (400 gauge, 30 cm wide) at a height of about 30 cm from the ground level. Grease should be applied at the lower edge of band during December to prevent pink to brown coloured nymphs crawling up the tree.<br/> -&nbsp;Look for white coloured cottony cushion every 2-3 days from December to January.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the honeydew secretion by mealy bugs as well as the presence of ants. (Phoresis)<br/>-&nbsp;Inspect for the presence of sooty mould on leaves and twigs<br/> -&nbsp;Release 10-15 grubs of coccinellid predator, <i>Cryptolemus montrozieri</i> per tree. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of <i>Beauveria bassiana</i> @ 2 gms per litre of water  or 5% Neem Seed Kernel Extract (5 gms per 10 litres of water) around the tree trunk during December-January. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of <i>Lecanicillum lecanii</i> @ 4 gm per litre of water during dawn hours for effective mycosis.<br/>-&nbsp;If the number of mealy bug colonies are low, smear the colonies with kerosene using paint brush in young plants.<br/> -&nbsp; Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/> -&nbsp;Spraying of Profenophos 50 EC 2ml/litre of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Profenophos  WHO class II.<br/>

Title: Pomegranate fruit borer
Authors:   Mr. Nilesh Ganesh Patkar, Dr. Raja Ramesh, Mr. Ganeshmoorthy, R.
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Dig or plough around pomegranate tree immediately after harvest to expose the pupae to predatory birds, other natural enemies and the sun.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of weeds and plants which serve as alternate hosts.<br/>-&nbsp;Collection and destruction (by burying) of damaged fruits away from the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Covering the fruit with Polythene bag or butter paper when fruits attain lemon size (30-40 days after fruit set).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of light trap @ 1/acre to monitor the activity of adults.<br/>-&nbsp;ETL: Observe the eggs on fruit calyx (flower) @ 5 eggs/plant.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Release of <i>Trichogramma chilonis</i> @ one lakh (5 cc)/acre at the time of flowering.<br/>-&nbsp;At flowering stage, spray NSKE 5% or Azadirachtin 1500 ppm @ 3.0 ml/litre of water at 15 days intervals commencing from initiation of flowering up to the harvesting subjected to the presence of fruit borer<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray  any one of the following chemicals: Indoxacarb 14.5% SC (0.5 ml/litre) or Spinosad 45% SC (0.5 ml/litere) or Cypermethrin 25% EC (1 ml/litre) at fortnightly interval from flowering to fruit development. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Cyperthethrin, Indoxacarb WHO classification Class II Moderately Hazardous. Spinosad WHO classification Class III Slightly Hazardous<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Deudorix isocrates</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99450.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99452.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Dig or plough around pomegranate tree immediately after harvest to expose the pupae to predatory birds, other natural enemies and the sun.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of weeds and plants which serve as alternate hosts.<br/>-&nbsp;Collection and destruction (by burying) of damaged fruits away from the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Covering the fruit with Polythene bag or butter paper when fruits attain lemon size (30-40 days after fruit set).<br/> -&nbsp;Use of light trap @ 1/acre to monitor the activity of adults.<br/>-&nbsp;ETL: Observe the eggs on fruit calyx (flower) @ 5 eggs/plant.<br/> -&nbsp;Release of <i>Trichogramma chilonis</i> @ one lakh (5 cc)/acre at the time of flowering.<br/>-&nbsp;At flowering stage, spray NSKE 5% or Azadirachtin 1500 ppm @ 3.0 ml/litre of water at 15 days intervals commencing from initiation of flowering up to the harvesting subjected to the presence of fruit borer<br/> -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators<br/> -&nbsp;Spray  any one of the following chemicals: Indoxacarb 14.5% SC (0.5 ml/litre) or Spinosad 45% SC (0.5 ml/litere) or Cypermethrin 25% EC (1 ml/litre) at fortnightly interval from flowering to fruit development. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Cyperthethrin, Indoxacarb WHO classification Class II Moderately Hazardous. Title: Rice Gall Midge
Authors:   Mr.Nilesh Ganesh Patkar, Dr.Raja.Ramesh (Assistant Professor, ICAR-KVK, TNAU) 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Plough the field after harvest & keep land fallow during off season.

Remove the alternate hosts (<i>Oryza glaberrima</i>, <i>Oryza longistaminata</i>) and three grasses <i>viz.</i>, <i>Eleusine indica</i>, <i>Bothriochloa</i> sp. and <i>Paspalum</i> sp <br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant variety MDU3, PTB 21, PTB 18 <br/>-&nbsp;Root dipping of seedlings in chlorpyriphos 20 EC 2 ml per lit of water for 20 min  before transplanting in <i>Kharif</i> & <i>Rabi</i> crop season.<br/>-&nbsp;Transplanting  during early June.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid close planting (maintain 20x20cm spacing).<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid staggered planting. <br/>-&nbsp;Optimum recommendation of Nitrogen & potash fertilizer (150 kg N &50 kg P)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Setup a light trap per acre and monitor the adult flies<br/>-&nbsp;Observe economic threshold level 10 % silver shoot <br/>
    -&nbsp;Release Platygaster oryzae parasitised galls at 1/10 m2 on 10 days after transplanting (DAT)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray NSKE 5%  at  50 ml or Neem Oil 3% at 30 ml per liter  15 days after transplanting<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply Thiamethoxam 25% WG 100 g/ha or  Fipronil 5% SC at 400 ml/acre or Fipronil  0.3 G 10 kg per acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Fipronil, Chlorpyrifos: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous). Thiamethoxam: No WHO classification<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Orseolia oryzae</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99453.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99455.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Plough the field after harvest & keep land fallow during off season.

Remove the alternate hosts (<i>Oryza glaberrima</i>, <i>Oryza longistaminata</i>) and three grasses <i>viz.</i>, <i>Eleusine indica</i>, <i>Bothriochloa</i> sp. and <i>Paspalum</i> sp <br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant variety MDU3, PTB 21, PTB 18 <br/>-&nbsp;Root dipping of seedlings in chlorpyriphos 20 EC 2 ml per lit of water for 20 min  before transplanting in <i>Kharif</i> & <i>Rabi</i> crop season.<br/>-&nbsp;Transplanting  during early June.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid close planting (maintain 20x20cm spacing).<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid staggered planting. <br/>-&nbsp;Optimum recommendation of Nitrogen & potash fertilizer (150 kg N &50 kg P)<br/> -&nbsp;Setup a light trap per acre and monitor the adult flies<br/>-&nbsp;Observe economic threshold level 10 % silver shoot <br/> -&nbsp;Release Platygaster oryzae parasitised galls at 1/10 m2 on 10 days after transplanting (DAT)<br/>-&nbsp;Spray NSKE 5%  at  50 ml or Neem Oil 3% at 30 ml per liter  15 days after transplanting<br/> -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/> -&nbsp;Apply Thiamethoxam 25% WG 100 g/ha or  Fipronil 5% SC at 400 ml/acre or Fipronil  0.3 G 10 kg per acre  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Fipronil, Chlorpyrifos: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous). Title: Rice thrips
Authors:   Dr. N. Vijiyakumar, Ms.Girija
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Timely sowing of paddy seeds should be encouraged, e.g. sornavari  April; samba  August; late samba  end of September; navarai  February. <br/>-&nbsp;Optimum seed rate (30 kg/acre) should be used to avoid dense canopy.<br/>-&nbsp;Encourage direct sowing wherever possible @ 12 Kg/acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water stress conditions. Maintain the optimum level of water in the nursery as well as in the main field.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain black gram, green gram, vegetable cowpea and coriander throughout the year for conserving natural enemies like coccinellid beetles, anthocorid bugs, and staphylinid beetles that feed on both the nymph and adults.<br/>
    -&nbsp;At 10 days after sowing (DAS), or for SRI 7 DAS, observe for 5 thrips per pass of wet palm, run along the foliage at 12 random places.<br/>-&nbsp;After 15 DAT, monitor for  yellowing of leaf tips both in the nursery and main fields <br/>-&nbsp;Observe for laceration (puncturing/ tearing) of tender leaves and white streaks along with rolling of leaves from tip to base.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray water @ 1 litre / cent of nursery bed using power sprayer.<br/>-&nbsp;Flood the nursery with water and drain it after 15 minutes. <br/>-&nbsp;Apply of 3% neem oil @ 100ml for 8 cents nursery.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply NSKE 5% @ 50ml/litre of water.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;In severe cases, spraying of Profenophos 50EC @ 50ml for 8 cents nursery.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Avoid indiscriminate and repeated use of Profenophos to prevent pest resurgence. Profenophos - Moderately hazardous (toxicity class II)<br/>-&nbsp;In main field, spray 400 ml of Profenophos  50 EC/per acre. Apply Thiamethoxam 25% WG @ 40g/acre or spray Fipronil 5% SC @ 400 ml /acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Avoid indiscriminate and repeated use of Profenophos to prevent pest resurgence. Profenophos - Moderately hazardous (toxicity class II). Thiamethoxam   WHO classification class III. Fipronil - WHO classification class II<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Baliothrips biformis</i> 
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99456.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_99458.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Yellow Vein Mosaic of Soybean
Authors:   Mr. Vijay S. Thokre, Mrs. Prapti Patkar, Dr. M. Kandibane
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Avoid monocropping of soybean crop<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid sowing during summer season in endemic areas<br/>-&nbsp;Use disease free seeds <br/>-&nbsp;Grow resistant varieties i.e. Phule Kalyani <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid high density of planting  <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid cultivation of Pigeon pea, black gram, green gram. <br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with Imidacloprid 70 WS @ 7gm per kg seed  <br/>-&nbsp;application of recommended nitrogenous fertilizer.<br/>-&nbsp;Encourage the activity of Lady bird beetle, <i>Chyrosoperla carnea</i>, spiders etc. by planting  cowpea and maize crops<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor nymphs and adult whiteflies on lower surface of leaves.  <br/>-&nbsp;Observe mottling & yellowing symptoms on leaves   <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for economic threshold level of 5-10 nymphs and adults per leaf. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Rogue out and destroy infected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Install yellow sticky traps @ 5 traps/acre for early identification and minimize the pest population.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem seed kernel extract 50 ml per lit water to repel whiteflies at  before flowering stage <br/>-&nbsp;Spray <i>Lecanicillium lecanii</i> 40 gm per 10 lit of water<br/>-&nbsp;Spray <i>Paecilomyces fumosoreosis</i> 40 gm per 10 lit water <br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as gloves, mask, goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Dimethoate 35% EC @ 30ml .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Dimethoate: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Alternatively, use Acetamiprid20% SP 4 g per10 litre of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Acetamiprid: WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>
Scientific Names:
