Title: Diplodia cob rot of maize
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use a resistant variety if available<br/>-&nbsp;Ensure the recommended distance between plants is used, about 40 cm between plants and 80 cm between rows (depends on hybrid variety). Dense planting can spread the disease<br/>-&nbsp;Treat seeds with hot water at 50C (hot but bearable for the hand) for 10 minutes before sowing to help kill the pathogen<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid mechanical damage that may be caused by insects and birds because it helps entry of the pathogen into the cob<br/>-&nbsp;Make sure fertilization of soil is well balanced, using ammonium as a nitrogen source to reduce cob rot and maintaining potassium levels<br/>-&nbsp;Rotate maize with wheat, soyabean or groundnut for at least two years after a severe outbreak<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain optimal irrigation levels so that maize does not get stressed and become vulnerable to disease<br/>-&nbsp;Ensure that bins are cleaned before storage to prevent disease spreading from previously infected cobs<br/>
    -&nbsp;Crop should be visited twice a week from early silking stage to 2-3 weeks after silking. Monitor particularly closely when dry weather is followed by frequent rainfall after silking.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for whitish powdery like material on corn grains by removing the husks. This rots the ears during warm and dry weather<br/>-&nbsp;Look for very small, black specks scattered on husks or embedded in cob tissues and kernels<br/>-&nbsp;Leaves wilt suddenly and become greyish-green<br/>-&nbsp;The crop stand may suffer from lodging<br/>-&nbsp;Apply control measures when 10 out of 100 ears are damaged and a quarter of the cob is infected<br/>-&nbsp;Check for insect damage to ears which can cause the disease to develop<br/>-&nbsp;Check for the stalk rot phase of this disease which can occur before ears get diseased<br/>-&nbsp;If more than 5-15 % of plants have stalk and/or ear rots then consider harvesting early as crop losses could be high<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms are similar to <i>Stenocarpella macrospora</i> which is prevalent in warm, humid regions, as opposed to <i>S. maydis</i> which is prevalent in cool, humid temperature regions<br/>-&nbsp;Disease caused by <i>S. maydis</i> can be distinguished from other stalk rots by the formation of small dark-coloured spots (pycnidia) on stalk internodes late in the season. If unsure about pathogen identity then send to a lab for analysis<br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove infected cobs as soon as possible (do not feed to livestock) to remove disease from field<br/>-&nbsp;Harvest early to reduce losses due to lodging following crop maturity<br/>-&nbsp;If there has been a severe outbreak of Diplodia cob rot, destroy crop residues by grazing, burning, baling or ploughing in crop remains to a depth of 20 cm<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Stenocarpella maydis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109572.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109573.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109574.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Use a resistant variety if available<br/>-&nbsp;Ensure the recommended distance between plants is used, about 40 cm between plants and 80 cm between rows (depends on hybrid variety). Dense planting can spread the disease<br/>-&nbsp;Treat seeds with hot water at 50C (hot but bearable for the hand) for 10 minutes before sowing to help kill the pathogen<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid mechanical damage that may be caused by insects and birds because it helps entry of the pathogen into the cob<br/>-&nbsp;Make sure fertilization of soil is well balanced, using ammonium as a nitrogen source to reduce cob rot and maintaining potassium levels<br/>-&nbsp;Rotate maize with wheat, soyabean or groundnut for at least two years after a severe outbreak<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain optimal irrigation levels so that maize does not get stressed and become vulnerable to disease<br/>-&nbsp;Ensure that bins are cleaned before storage to prevent disease spreading from previously infected cobs<br/> -&nbsp;Crop should be visited twice a week from early silking stage to 2-3 weeks after silking. Monitor particularly closely when dry weather is followed by frequent rainfall after silking.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for whitish powdery like material on corn grains by removing the husks. This rots the ears during warm and dry weather<br/>-&nbsp;Look for very small, black specks scattered on husks or embedded in cob tissues and kernels<br/>-&nbsp;Leaves wilt suddenly and become greyish-green<br/>-&nbsp;The crop stand may suffer from lodging<br/>-&nbsp;Apply control measures when 10 out of 100 ears are damaged and a quarter of the cob is infected<br/>-&nbsp;Check for insect damage to ears which can cause the disease to develop<br/>-&nbsp;Check for the stalk rot phase of this disease which can occur before ears get diseased<br/>-&nbsp;If more than 5-15 % of plants have stalk and/or ear rots then consider harvesting early as crop losses could be high<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms are similar to <i>Stenocarpella macrospora</i> which is prevalent in warm, humid regions, as opposed to <i>S. maydis</i> which is prevalent in cool, humid temperature regions<br/>-&nbsp;Disease caused by <i>S. maydis</i> can be distinguished from other stalk rots by the formation of small dark-coloured spots (pycnidia) on stalk internodes late in the season. If unsure about pathogen identity then send to a lab for analysis<br/> -&nbsp;Remove infected cobs as soon as possible (do not feed to livestock) to remove disease from field<br/>-&nbsp;Harvest early to reduce losses due to lodging following crop maturity<br/>-&nbsp;If there has been a severe outbreak of Diplodia cob rot, destroy crop residues by grazing, burning, baling or ploughing in crop remains to a depth of 20 cm<br/> Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.

Title: Soft rot on vegetables
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Locate nurseries away from production fields and transplant to well drained soils<br/>-&nbsp;Control insect pests which can cause damage (e.g. thrips, leaf hoppers, cutworms), providing entry points for the bacteria. Practice tillage before planting to expose insect pupae to natural enemies to reduce populations<br/>-&nbsp;Ensure that plants are spaced wide enough so that water can easily evaporate off the leaves<br/>-&nbsp;Fields should not be worked while plants are wet to avoid spreading the disease<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain optimal levels of fertilization to grow strong crops which are resilient to bacterial soft rot<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid overhead irrigation, particularly in the evening when it's cooler, to prevent leaves being wet for a long period of time<br/>-&nbsp;Use ground irrigation if required, starting from non-infected parts of the field to prevent bacterial disease spread from infected areas<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid injuries to plants when working to prevent bacteria from being able to easily enter the plant<br/>-&nbsp;Clean farming tools and machinery with 10% bleach or 70% alchohol before working in different areas of the field to prevent disease spread<br/>-&nbsp;Rotate with less susceptible crops such as maize, sorghum, snap beans and beets for 2-3 years after harvest<br/>
    -&nbsp;Relevant crops: potato, carrot, tomato, cucumbers, melons, squash, pumpkins, cabbage, cauliflower, bok choy<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor field looking for small to large water-soaked lesions on the leaves<br/>-&nbsp;Affected leaf tissues turn brown,

becomes soft and mushy and has a foul smell. Leaves may yellow and wilt<br/>-&nbsp;Look for decaying leaves, stems and roots

<br/>-&nbsp;Consider taking action as soon as the symptoms are seen<br/>
    -&nbsp;Rogue and destroy infected plants in nurseries and fields by deep burying (at least 1 m) or burning (if allowed in your area)<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy plant residues and volunteer crops by deep burying or burning<br/>-&nbsp;Harvest during dry conditions to prevent spreading the disease to other crops<br/>-&nbsp;Do not store any plants displaying symptoms as the disease can spread to other plants during storage<br/>-&nbsp;Store crop in a cool, dry place which is well aerated to suppress bacterial growth<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Dickeya</i> spp., <i>Erwinia</i> spp., <i>Pseudomonas</i> spp., <Pectobacterium</i> spp., <i>Bacillus</i> spp., <i>Clostridium</i> spp.
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109595.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109596.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109597.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Crown rot of groundnut
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Plant high quality seeds<br/>-&nbsp;Use <i>Trichoderma viride</i>/<i>T. harizanum</i> to treat seeds at 4g/kg of seed and soil application at 25-62.5kg/ha<br/>-&nbsp;Use organic fertilizers, such as alfalfa, castor cake, neem cake or mustard cake, at 500 kg/ha. Neem cake also has anti-fungal properties<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain adequate and uniform soil moisture during seedling stage as fluctuations in soil moisture can aggravate the disease.<br/>-&nbsp;Control root and stem boring insects whose feeding damage can also aggravate the disease<br/>-&nbsp;Do not plant near vegetables which show symptoms of <i>Aspergillus</i> (e.g. tomatoes, grapes, onions, mangoes, garlic, maize, banana, cotton) - the host range is very large<br/>-&nbsp;Control numbers of root and stem boring insects (e.g. lesser corn stalk borer), since feeding damage caused can encourage the development of crown rot<br/>-&nbsp;Minimise damage caused to seedlings by minimising the use of pesticides and the amount of soil thrown against plants during cultivation<br/>
    -&nbsp;Crown rot is a fungus which is found in the soil and lives on dead and decaying vegetation and leaves, compost piles and stored grain. It is spread via air, soil and water.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor carefully for crown rot of germinating seedlings (damping off) at temperatures greater than 30C<br/>-&nbsp;Infected areas of seedlings become watersoaked then light brown, and eventually are covered with black sporulating structures (fungus). Seedlings rapidly collapse and die<br/>-&nbsp;In moist soils, seeds may die due to rotting and when removed from soil, they show a black sooty cover<br/>-&nbsp;Mature plants show permanent wilt of branches, and/or wilting of entire plant. If dead and dried branches are pulled they will easily detach from the collar region<br/>-&nbsp;Root curling and deformation of upper plant parts<br/>-&nbsp;Pods have patches of black sooty spores<br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove the previous season's infected crop residues from the field and destroy to reduce source of infection<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Aspergillus niger</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109636.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_109637.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Plant high quality seeds<br/>-&nbsp;Use <i>Trichoderma viride</i>/<i>T. harizanum</i> to treat seeds at 4g/kg of seed and soil application at 25-62.5kg/ha<br/>-&nbsp;Use organic fertilizers, such as alfalfa, castor cake, neem cake or mustard cake, at 500 kg/ha. Title: Cassava Root Rot
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Cassava root rot is a disease caused by various types of fungi<br/>-&nbsp;Select land that will not flood throughout the year and avoid water logged soil.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid using planting materials from farms with reported cases of root rot diseases.<br/>-&nbsp;Select healthy plants for the production of planting materials, avoid plants that have wilted leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy plant debris (rotting stems, roots etc.) soon after harvest by burning or deep burying.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid delaying the harvest of early maturing varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid continuous cropping on the same area of land/in infected zones, use crop rotations of at least 3 seasons with maize, millet or sorghum.<br/>-&nbsp;Clean farming tools after use with a 10% solution of household bleach.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid planting cassava as first crop after clearance of woodland/forests to avoid fungal attacks.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor fields regularly for develoment of yellow mushrooms in the soil or white fruiting bodies at base of crop stems - these fungi cause root rot.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include wilting leaves, defoliation, stem dieback and death of infected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;In disease endemic areas, monitor farms for single or few wilted plants growing amongst healthy plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Storage roots of infected plants are swollen with soft brown rot internally.<br/>-&nbsp;Uproot any infected plant when identified and examine roots to establish cause of wilt.<br/>-&nbsp;Carry out control measures at the first sign of the disease.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Carefully remove fruiting bodies of the fungus and destroy immediately by burning.<br/>-&nbsp;Isolate plants with wilt symptoms and burn, take care for disrupting any fungus. <br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Polyporus sulphureus</i>; <i>Botryodiplodia theobromae</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110509.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110510.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Cassava root rot is a disease caused by various types of fungi<br/>-&nbsp;Select land that will not flood throughout the year and avoid water logged soil.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid using planting materials from farms with reported cases of root rot diseases.<br/>-&nbsp;Select healthy plants for the production of planting materials, avoid plants that have wilted leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy plant debris (rotting stems, roots etc.) soon after harvest by burning or deep burying.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid delaying the harvest of early maturing varieties.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid continuous cropping on the same area of land/in infected zones, use crop rotations of at least 3 seasons with maize, millet or sorghum.<br/>-&nbsp;Clean farming tools after use with a 10% solution of household bleach.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid planting cassava as first crop after clearance of woodland/forests to avoid fungal attacks.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor fields regularly for develoment of yellow mushrooms in the soil or white fruiting bodies at base of crop stems - these fungi cause root rot.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include wilting leaves, defoliation, stem dieback and death of infected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;In disease endemic areas, monitor farms for single or few wilted plants growing amongst healthy plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Storage roots of infected plants are swollen with soft brown rot internally.<br/>-&nbsp;Uproot any infected plant when identified and examine roots to establish cause of wilt.<br/>-&nbsp;Carry out control measures at the first sign of the disease.<br/> -&nbsp;Carefully remove fruiting bodies of the fungus and destroy immediately by burning.<br/>-&nbsp;Isolate plants with wilt symptoms and burn, take care for disrupting any fungus. <br/> Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Title: Aphids on chilli and green pepper
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;<i>M. persicae</i>are small green aphids which feed on plant sap. These aphids can transmit plant viruses. <br/>-&nbsp;Use of repellant plants such as onion, garlic and marigold in alternate rows to crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of agro nets (size 400 m) to prevent pest accessing crop seedlings, and remove at flowering stage<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies (e.g. ladybird beetles, hoverflies and parasitoid wasps) by avoiding use of broad spectrum insecticides and providing suitable habitat.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid high levels of nitrogen in soil, as this causes plants to become succulent and attractive to aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove and burn crop residues immediately after harvest.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Start monitoring from seedling stage, look at lower leaves, stems or growing points for soft bodies insects, found in clusters.<br/>-&nbsp;Check underside of leaves, shoots and stems for immobile aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for yellowing leaves, stunted growth and honeydew on infested crops. Sooty mould may grown on the honeydew.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for curled, wrinkled or cupped leaves and mosaic patterns on the leaves (alternating dark and light patches) - these are symptoms of viruses that can be transmitted by the aphid<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor at least 3 times a week for aphids early in the morning/late in day during dry periods.<br/>-&nbsp;Start control measures when there is 10-20% infestation (i.e. 1-2 infested plants/10-20 plants in plots).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove and burn infested plants to help reduce population spread.<br/>-&nbsp;Use yellow traps (at 2 traps per 30 m2 to attract and kill aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray soap solution (potassium soaps e.g. Alata samina). Add 10-15 tablespoons of liquid soal in 16 L knapsack and spray foliage.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray with neem-based products and follow label instructions (e.g. Azatrol, 1.2% Azadiractin. 1 part Azatrol with 1 part water, spray at 7-10 day intervals).<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Myzus persicae</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110536.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110537.img?width=800&height=640

Title: Aphids on eggplant
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;<i>M. persicae</i>are small aphids which feed on plant sap. These aphids can transmit plant viruses. <br/>-&nbsp;Cover plants with agro nets (400 m mesh) to prevent pest access.<br/>-&nbsp;Grow aphid repellant plants (e.g. marigold and onions) as border/barrier of crop plots.<br/>-&nbsp;Burn dried cow dung and herb/shrub leaves to make smoke in early mornings or late evenings to prevent pest colonisation. <br/>-&nbsp;Apply poultry manure (850 kg/Ha) to ensure high plant vigour.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies by avoiding broad spectrum insecticides and providing suitable habitat.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Begin monitoring at seedling stage, observe for associated ants around crops.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe underside of leaves for grey-black or green aphid insects (normally found in colonies).<br/>-&nbsp;Look for yellowing leaves, stunted growth and honeydew on infested crops. Sooty mould may grown on the honeydew.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for curled, wrinkled or cupped leaves and mosaic patterns on the leaves (alternating dark and light patches) - these are symptoms of viruses that can be transmitted by the aphid<br/>-&nbsp;If 2-3 out of 20-30 plants have at least 2 aphid colonies, undertake control measures.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Wash infested areas of plants with a strong jet of water.<br/>-&nbsp;Use soapy water (1 ml/2 L water) on both sides of leaves, spray during early mornings/late evenings so spray does not dry quickly.<br/>-&nbsp;Release biocontrol agents (e.g. <i>Aphidius</i> spp., ladybirds, lacewings and parasitic wasps). Release roughly 5-25 per 100 square ft., weekly in areas of high infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray with neem-based products and follow label instructions (e.g. Azatrol, 1.2% Azadiractin. 1 part Azatrol with 1 part water, spray at 7-10 day intervals).<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Myzus persicae, Aphis gossypii</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110541.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110542.img?width=800&height=640

Title: Aphids on okro
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;<i>M. persicae</i>are small aphids which feed on plant sap. These aphids can transmit plant viruses. <br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies by avoiding use of broad spectrum insecticides and providing suitable habitat.<br/>-&nbsp;Use agro-nets (400 m mesh) from seedling to vegetative stage to prevent aphid access.<br/>-&nbsp;Use aphid repellant plants (e.g. marigold, onion and/or garlic) in alternate rows amongst okro.<br/>-&nbsp;Use dry cow dung and green herb/shrub leaves to make smoke during early morning or late evening to repel aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply poultry manure (after 1 week decomposition at 850 kg/Ha) to ensure high plant vigour.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Begin monitoring seedling stage twice a week during early mornings and/or late evenings (especially during dry periods).<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for slow moving grey-black or green aphids, these are normally found in colonies on the underside of leaves as well as on new shoot tips and buds.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for ants (linked with aphid presence) climbing up and down crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for yellowing leaves, stunted growth and honeydew on infested crops. Sooty mould may grown on the honeydew.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for curled, wrinkled or cupped leaves and mosaic patterns on the leaves (alternating dark and light patches) - these are symptoms of viruses that can be transmitted by the aphid<br/>-&nbsp;At random, examine 20-30 plants, if 2-3 have at least 2 aphid colonies then undertake direct control measures.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray infested crops with a strong jet of water to remove aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;Use soap solution (potassium soap) (add 10-15 tablespoons of liquid soap and 1 L of water in a knapsack) to spray on plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Release biocontrol agents (e.g. <i>Aphidius</i> spp., ladybirds, lacewings and parasitic wasps). Release roughly 5-25 per 100 square ft., weekly in areas of high infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray crops with botanical extracts (e.g. garlic, neem, red chilli pepper and soap). Take 50 g mixture of each in 2 L of water, boil for 15 minutes, cool then spray during evening.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Myzus persicae, Aphid gossypii</i>

Take 50 g mixture of each in 2 L of water, boil for 15 minutes, cool then spray during evening.<br/> Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.

Title: Whitefly on cassava
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Whiteflies are small white insects that transmit viruses to the plants when feeding from the sap.<br/>-&nbsp;Clear weeds in advance of planting amongst crop to reduce overwintering pest stages.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid use of broad spectrum insecticides to conserve natural enemies such as ladybirds, lacewings, hoverflies and parasitoids. Provide suitable habitat.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove and destroy ratoon cassava materials and other plant residues by burning or burying deep.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant repellent crops such as marigold around the boundary of the plot to repel whiteflies.<br/>-&nbsp;Provide suitable irrigation to crops, as stressed plants are more prone to whitefly damage.<br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant varieties against whitefly transmitted viruses (see information on Cassava mosaic virus and African cassava mosaic disease).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops for whiteflies every week throughout the plant growth period (especially during the sprouting season).<br/>-&nbsp;For early detection, observe for white-brown eggs and white-yellow adults on the underside of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for a cloud of white insects which re-settle soon after disturbance of the plant.<br/>-&nbsp;Check for yellowing symptoms on the underside of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;If 10-20 plants are observed with symptoms or at least 20 whiteflies on 10-20 plants/acre then follow direct control suggestions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of yellow sticky traps to catch and kill adults (4 traps/300 m2 placed 50 cm above the ground).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray crops with Azadirachtin 0.03% (e.g. Nimbedicine EC, Nematech WG) 50 ml/20 L water 20 days after planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Release parasitic wasps such as <i>Encarsia formosa</i> if available in your area commercially.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray with entomopathogenic fungi such as <i>Verticillium lecanii</i>, <i>Beauveria bassiana</i>or <i>Paecilmyces fumosoroseus</i> if commercially available.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Bemisia tabaci</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110563.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110564.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110565.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Fusarium wilt on watermelon
Authors:   Mr D. Ilayakumar, Mr Tamizharasan, Mr Prakash (National Agro Foundation), D. Adhikari. Phone no: 9047405544  Email: ilayaagri@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Long rotations of six years or more are necessary to keep inoculum from building up in the soil during the winter season.<br/>-&nbsp;Fusarium wilt may be seed borne. Inspect seedlings for symptoms of fusarium wilt. Use new transplant trays or sanitize trays well.<br/>-&nbsp;Do not save seed from fields where Fusarium wilt has been observed.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid flood irrigation to prevent spreading of the disease.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow drip irrigation to prevent the disease spreading.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Symptoms include damping off in seedling from infested fields.<br/>-&nbsp;Wilting and chlorosis symptoms visible in older leaves. <br/>-&nbsp;Wilt is most evident in the heat of the day (afternoon hours).<br/>-&nbsp;Stem cracks and brown streaks often appear near the crown of the plant.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply <i>Pseudomonas fluorescence</i> at 2.5 kg/Ha along with 50 kg FYM (sieved) and 100 kg neem cake before last ploughing.<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Foliar spray of Carbendazim at 2 g/l of water at 15 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard). PHI: 14 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Top drenching with Carbendazim at 1 g/l of water and 5-10 ml per plant.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Fusarium oxysporum</i> f. sp niveumattaks
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110706.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110708.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110709.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Smut on Ragi
Authors:   P. Prakash, Kanchana, T. Sunil Kumar (National Agro Foundation), D. Adhikari. Phone no. 9110550127, Email: Sunilkumarthanga@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Remove weed hosts from bunds and channels.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant resistant varieties Markazhi pattam (Dec to Jan), Co -9, Co 13, Co 14, (Sep  oct), Paiyur 1, Co 13 or Co 14.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid using excess nitrogenous fertilizers (split in 3 doses: 50% in basal application, 25% in tillering stage/phase and 25% in panicle initiation stage). Recommended dosage of nitrogenous fertilizer usage is 60 kg/Ha.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Disease symptoms appear during ear emergence when the ear appears dark grey due to masses of teliospores covered by a thin membrane of tissue. The membrane splits at maturity by releasing spores into the air. <br/>-&nbsp;Affected grain may emerge later than neighbouring plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Infected plants can be identified by their dark colour and swollen appearance.<br/>-&nbsp;Green sorus turn pink/green and finally turn black. Stem galling has also been seen.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Dip the seedling with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescence</i> at 2.5 kg/3 cents, make treatment sub plot and dip seedlings for 15 minutes.<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Two sprays of Carbendazim 50% SC. 2% at the 45th day and 65th day.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard). Pre-harvest Interval 14 days.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Melanopsichium eleusinis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110726.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110728.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Remove weed hosts from bunds and channels.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant resistant varieties Markazhi pattam (Dec to Jan), Co -9, Co 13, Co 14, (Sep  oct), Paiyur 1, Co 13 or Co 14.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid using excess nitrogenous fertilizers (split in 3 doses: 50% in basal application, 25% in tillering stage/phase and 25% in panicle initiation stage). Title: Gram Pod Borer on Groundnut
Authors:   Vinoth, B.Kanchana, M.Saranya, M.Priyadarshni (National Agro Foundation), D. Adhikari. Phone no. 8344577099, Email: ponvinoth408@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Trim the bunds before crop sowing to prevent egg laying by pest.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy the pupae by ploughing at least 10 cm deep during the summer.<br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant varieties like Co-6 and Co-7.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant border crop with red gram/cowpea/black gram to increase natural enemies.<br/>-&nbsp;Grow trap crop of castor or chrysanthemum around the field for attracting the pest towards the trap crop. <br/>-&nbsp;Install 10 bird perches per acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Set up light trap (1/acre from planting) and observe during 6 to 8 pm.<br/>-&nbsp;Install para-pheromone trap Heli lure at 5 per acre. <br/>-&nbsp;Adult moths have a 40 mm wing span and dull brown forewings.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe longitudinal cut holes on pods by pulling the entire infested plant.<br/>-&nbsp;See faecal matter inside pods from the 45th day in removed plants.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray a solution of 250 ml of HaNPV at 250 Larval Equivalents (LE) + 1 kg palm jaggery + 200 litre of water/ acre. Spray in the evening hours with a hand sprayer. Apply 2 applications with 10 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray  <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> at 2 g in 1 litre of water at 15 day intervals for a maximum of 3 times.<br/>-&nbsp;Immerse 50 kg powder form of NSKE in 500 litres of water for 8 hours. Filter and add 500 ml of teepol to spray 1 Ha at 15 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem oil at 30 ml in 1 litre of water at 15 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Release <i>Trichogramma chilonis</i> at 1 lakh/Ha at 40 and 50 days after sowing (DAS).<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Chlorpyrifos 3 ml per litre of water at 15 days interval.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorpyrifos - WHO Class II. (Moderately hazardous). Pre Harvest Interval (PHI) 14 days<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spray of Quinolphos 2 ml/l of water at 15 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Quinalphos- WHO Class II. (Moderately hazardous). PHI - 7 days.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Helicoverpa armigera</i>

Title: Red Hairy Caterpillar on Groundnut
Authors:   P. Latha  & K. Indhumathi (National Agro Foundation), D. Adhikari. Phone no:9750603060  email: latha.ens@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Destroy the pupae through summer ploughing.<br/>-&nbsp;Collect volunteer plants from harvested field and destroy by burning.<br/>-&nbsp;Dig a trench around the field at 30 cm depth and 25 cm width to arrest the movement of migrating larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Raise one row of cowpea (Thatta payir) for every 5 rows of groundnut wherever red hairy caterpillar is endemic (predominant at a particular place).<br/>-&nbsp;Install T-shaped bird perches (10 to 15/ac) to encourage predators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Setup 1 light trap/acre from planting and observe regularly between 6- 9 pm.<br/>-&nbsp;Install sex pheromone trap (Amsactin lure) at 5/ac from planting, when 2-3 eggs are found for every 10 plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for faecal matter and defoliation symptoms at 6-8 am twice a week.<br/>-&nbsp;This pest affects the vegetative stage. It causes defoliation, where all the leaves are eaten, leaving the main stem alone.<br/>-&nbsp;Larvae are reddish brown with black bands on both ends and long reddish brown hairs all over the body. <br/>-&nbsp;Adult moths have white forewings with brownish streaks all over and a yellowish streak along the anterior margin and head. Hind wings are white with black markings. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray 250 ml of Amsacta NPV at 250 Larval Equivalents (LE) + 1 kg palm Jaggery + 200 litres of water/ac. Spray in the evening hours with a hand sprayer.<br/>-&nbsp;Immerse 50 kg powder form of NSKE in 500 litres of water for 8 hours, filter and add 500 ml of teepol to spray 1 Ha at 15 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray of Neem oil at 30 ml in 1 litre of water at 15 day intervals.

<br/>-&nbsp;Use of poison bait, prepared by using 8 kg rice bran + 1 kg palm Jaggery + 1 litre carbaryl. Prepare small balls and broadcast in the field during evening hours. <br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Phosalone 35EC at 2ml/litre of water at 15-20 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous), 35 days PHI.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray of Chlorpyriphos at 2 ml/litre water at 15-20 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous), 10 days PHI.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Amsacta albistriga</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110736.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110738.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Destroy the pupae through summer ploughing.<br/>-&nbsp;Collect volunteer plants from harvested field and destroy by burning.<br/>-&nbsp;Dig a trench around the field at 30 cm depth and 25 cm width to arrest the movement of migrating larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Raise one row of cowpea (Thatta payir) for every 5 rows of groundnut wherever red hairy caterpillar is endemic (predominant at a particular place).<br/>-&nbsp;Install T-shaped bird perches (10 to 15/ac) to encourage predators.<br/> -&nbsp;Setup 1 light trap/acre from planting and observe regularly between 6- 9 pm.<br/>-&nbsp;Install sex pheromone trap (Amsactin lure) at 5/ac from planting, when 2-3 eggs are found for every 10 plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for faecal matter and defoliation symptoms at 6-8 am twice a week.<br/>-&nbsp;This pest affects the vegetative stage. Title: Root rot in Black gram
Authors:   P. Prakash, Sunil Kumar, Vinoth Kumar (National Agro Foundation), D. Adhikari. Phone no: 9952361679  Email: prakashmuthu2006@gmail.com


Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;The disease occurs commonly at the podding stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Trichoderma viride</i> 4 g/kg or <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> 10 g/kg<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe damage in the seeds as the disease shows its first symptom before sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for affected plant leaves. Standing crop (5-10 days) turn yellow in colour and brown irregular lesions appear on leaves. <br/>-&nbsp;The roots and basal portion of the stem become black in colour and the bark peels off easily.<br/>-&nbsp;After 10 days of standing crop, the affected plants will dry up gradually. When the tap root of the affected plant is split open, reddening of internal tissues is visible.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply zinc sulphate 25 kg/Ha as basal application.<br/>-&nbsp;Basal application of neem cake at 150 kg/Ha.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>T. viride</i> at 2.5 kg/Ha + 50 kg of farm yard manure at 30 days after sowing.<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spot drenching of Carbendazim at 1 gm/l.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Macrophomina phaseolina</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110739.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110741.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Rust in Pulses
Authors:   Kanchana, Rajasekar, T. Sunil Kumar, D. Adhikari. NAF Phone no. 9790707020, Email: sriramamills@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Plough the soil twice before sowing the crop to kill the inoculum.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove the stubble after harvesting and destroy by burning to reduce the primary and secondary inoculums.<br/>-&nbsp;Sow/plant the seeds with 60x60cm spacing.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid excess usage of nitrogenous fertilizers (recommended dosage of nitrogen fertilizer is 12.25 kg). <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain soil moisture with a proper irrigation schedule.    <br/>-&nbsp;Irrigate immediately after sowing and light irrigation on the third day. Irrigate at intervals of 7 to 10 days depending upon soil and climatic conditions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Disease infestation occurs at the vegetative stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe leaves for red/brown raised pustules under a microscope or hand lens.<br/>-&nbsp;Disease incidence is severe during Jan 15th to Feb 15th due to heavy wind.<br/>-&nbsp;Red gram and Blackgram: Dark brown rusty pustules (uredia) appear on the lower surface of the leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Bengal gram and Cowpea: Dark brown rusty pustules (uredia) appear on the upper surface of the leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;In severe conditions observe for desiccated leaves and leaf drop at seed setting stage or pod formation stage.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Treat the seeds with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescence</i> at 10 gm/kg of seeds and shade dry for 15 minutes before sowing.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray of wettable Sulphur at 1500 g/Ha at 10 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (Slightly Hazardous). REI: 24 hrs.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray the crop with 0.2% Mancozeb 75 WP followed by two more sprays at 10 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Uredo cajani</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110742.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110744.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Plough the soil twice before sowing the crop to kill the inoculum.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove the stubble after harvesting and destroy by burning to reduce the primary and secondary inoculums.<br/>-&nbsp;Sow/plant the seeds with 60x60cm spacing.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid excess usage of nitrogenous fertilizers (recommended dosage of nitrogen fertilizer is 12.25 kg). <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain soil moisture with a proper irrigation schedule.    <br/>-&nbsp;Irrigate immediately after sowing and light irrigation on the third day. Irrigate at intervals of 7 to 10 days depending upon soil and climatic conditions.<br/> -&nbsp;Disease infestation occurs at the vegetative stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe leaves for red/brown raised pustules under a microscope or hand lens.<br/>-&nbsp;Disease incidence is severe during Jan 15th to Feb 15th due to heavy wind.<br/>-&nbsp;Red gram and Blackgram: Dark brown rusty pustules (uredia) appear on the lower surface of the leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Bengal gram and Cowpea: Dark brown rusty pustules (uredia) appear on the upper surface of the leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;In severe conditions observe for desiccated leaves and leaf drop at seed setting stage or pod formation stage.<br/> -&nbsp;Treat the seeds with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescence</i> at 10 gm/kg of seeds and shade dry for 15 minutes before sowing.<br/> -&nbsp;Spray of wettable Sulphur at 1500 g/Ha at 10 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (Slightly Hazardous). REI: 24 hrs.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray the crop with 0.2% Mancozeb 75 WP followed by two more sprays at 10 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class U (Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>

Title: Stem borer on Rice
Authors:   P. Prakash, Narayanan, Vinoth Kumar (National Agro Foundation), D. Adhikari. Phone no. 9952361679 email: prakashmuthu2006@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use resistant rice varieties like TKM 6, IR 20 & IR 26.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid close planting and continuous water stagnation at early stages.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove and destroy weeds regularly.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies such as dragonflies (Oosi thattan), spiders (Silanthi), parasitic wasps (Kulavi) by reducing the amount of insecticides usage.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow crop rotation (e.g. legumes/vegetables for two to three years).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Look for egg masses on the leaf tips and on the underside of the leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Egg masses are brownish yellow coloured and present on the upper surface of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe during the vegetative stage, larvae bore at the base of the plants, killing growing points which result in dead heart (central tiller dries up and is easily pulled from the base).<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor weekly from seedling to harvest for the presence of the insect and damage symptoms.<br/>-&nbsp;During the reproductive stage, larvae bore through the upper nodes and feed towards the base, resulting in whiteheads (emerging panicles are whitish and empty). Larvae leave tiny holes on the stems and tillers, and inside the damaged stems.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Install pheromone traps at 5 per acre from planting and observe during 7-9pm.<br/>-&nbsp;Set up light traps at 1 per acre and observe from 7-9 pm to control adult moths in the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Release of <i>Trichogramma japonicum</i> 3 at 2 cc/acre at 30 and 37 DAT.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem based bio-pesticides like Nimbicidine at 300 ml per acre at 15 days interval twice a month.<br/>-&nbsp;Application of Neem cake at 40 kg/acre at 40 DAT.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply combination of <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> var kurstaki 1 ml/lit of water and Neem seed kernel extract in combination of 2.5 kg/l of water to reduce the oviposition by stem borer.<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply Cartap hydrochloride 0.5 kg/Ha.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately Hazardous). PHI: 21 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Phenthoate at 0.5 kg a.i./Ha.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (Moderately Hazardous). PHI: 14 days<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Scirpophaga incertulas</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110745.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110747.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110748.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Bud Borer on Tuberose
Authors:   K. Indhumathi, Dr.P.Latha  (National Agro Foundation),  D. Adhikari. phone no: 8220743855, email: Induento2009@gmail.com
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Trim the bunds before crop sowing to prevent egg laying by pest.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy the pupae by ploughing during the summer.<br/>-&nbsp;Collect and destroy (by burning) damaged buds to reduce the spread of the pest.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant border crop with red gram/cowpea/black gram to increase natural enemies.<br/>-&nbsp;Grow trap crop of castor or chrysanthemum around the field for attracting the pest towards the trap crop. <br/>-&nbsp;Install 10 bird perches per acre from planting to encourage natural bird predators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Set up light traps (1/acre from planting) and observe during 6 to 11 pm.<br/>-&nbsp;Set up sex pheromone traps (Heli lure) at 5/acre at the stage of 5-10 pod damage or 5 larvae per 10 plants. Observe between 6-11 pm.<br/>-&nbsp;Eggs are deposited individually on growing spikes. Larvae bore into buds and flowers and feed on them by making holes.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray a solution of 250 ml of HaNPV at 250 Larval Equivalents (LE) + 1 kg palm jaggery + 200 litre of water/ acre. Spray in the evening hours with a hand sprayer. Apply 2 applications with 10 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;3 sprays of <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> at 2 g/l at 15 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Immerse 50 kg powder form of NSKE in 500 litres of water for 8 hours. Filter and add 500 ml of teepol to spray 1 Ha at 15 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem oil at 30 ml in 1 litre of water at 15 day intervals.<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Foliar spray of Carbaryl 0.2%at 6 g/l at 15 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorpyrifos - WHO Class II. (Moderately hazardous). Pre Harvest Interval (PHI) 14 days<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spray of Quinolphos 2 ml/l of water at 15 day intervals.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Quinalphos- WHO Class II. (Moderately hazardous). PHI - 7 days.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Helicoverpa armigera</i>

Title: Aphids on rape
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Aphids are highly reproductive, small insects that can weaken plant structures and transmit virus to crops.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid planting near an infested crop or on land with a history of infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Active removal of weeds from plots to reduce aphid hosts.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of alternative host species such as <i>Amaranthus</i>. Destroy by uprooting and burning or burying deep.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercropping with pest repellent plants such as onion, garlic and parsley to reduce aphid populations close to rape.<br/>-&nbsp;Do not apply high levels of nitrogenous fertilizer as this will make the plants more attractive to aphids.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Regularly check for leaf curling on crop at leats once a week.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe underside of leaves for aphid presence. Aphids are small insects of 2 mm long, soft-bodied and green, brown or yellow in colour.<br/>-&nbsp;High levels of infestation may result in the presence of black sooty mould on leaves due to honeydew secretion from aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitoring should be undertaken soon after crop emergence until crop harvest.<br/>-&nbsp;If there is no presence of aphid-transmitted viruses in the area, small aphid populations are tolerable amongst crop. <br/>-&nbsp;If infestation grows (10-20% por 1-2 infested plants per 10-20 observed) then consider undertaking direct control measures.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Prune leaves showing symptoms (curling, aphid populations on underside).<br/>-&nbsp;Removal and burning of infested crops to prevent spread of the fungus.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil products once a week for 4 weeks (4.5 ml/10 m2). Contact your local agro-input supplier to organise access of such products.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of soap water solution spray on crops to wash off any aphids present (1 tablespoons of liquid soap per 10 litres of water)<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Aphis</i> spp.
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110754.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110755.img?width=800&height=640

Title: Webworm on cabbage
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Widespread pest species, commonly found in food plants boring into stems and leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of clean, pest-free seedlings from nurseries.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove plant material residues after harvest and destroy by burning or burying.<br/>-&nbsp;Till soil to remove cabbage stubbles and dispose of before planting new crops.<br/>-&nbsp;Practice crop rotation or intercropping with non-host plants (such as onion and carrot) to reduce webworm populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Use mustard or Chinese cabbage as trap crops in alternate rows.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid use of broad spectrum insecticides to conserve natural enemies (spiders, parasistic wasps, lacewings and ants).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Start monitoring after seedling emergence and check crops for larvae twice a week <br/>-&nbsp;Inspect plants for egg masses, these are usually found in plant buds. Once eggs hatch the larvae feed on the underside of leaves and cover their bodies in webs.<br/>-&nbsp;A characteristic feature to observe is the larval webs covered in dirt and excrement.<br/>-&nbsp;The larva has a creamy white body with pale longitudinal stripes and a dark brown/black head, reaching 12-15 mm when fully grown.<br/>-&nbsp;Direct control measures should be followed once there are more than 1 larva per 5 plants.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Hand pick and destroy caterpillars found on crops during lower infestation levels.<br/>-&nbsp;Plowing/removing weeds at least one month in advance prior to crop planting reduces potential webworm populations <br/>-&nbsp;Use botanical extracts (such as neem seed extract, lemongrass or ginger) 1:15 L of water.<br/>-&nbsp;Use <i>Bacillus thurigiensis</i> and apply before larvae are protected by webs or in the centre of cabbages (which are difficult to reach by biopesticides). Apply once a week.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Hellula undalis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110762.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110763.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Widespread pest species, commonly found in food plants boring into stems and leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of clean, pest-free seedlings from nurseries.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove plant material residues after harvest and destroy by burning or burying.<br/>-&nbsp;Till soil to remove cabbage stubbles and dispose of before planting new crops.<br/>-&nbsp;Practice crop rotation or intercropping with non-host plants (such as onion and carrot) to reduce webworm populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Use mustard or Chinese cabbage as trap crops in alternate rows.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid use of broad spectrum insecticides to conserve natural enemies (spiders, parasistic wasps, lacewings and ants).<br/> -&nbsp;Start monitoring after seedling emergence and check crops for larvae twice a week <br/>-&nbsp;Inspect plants for egg masses, these are usually found in plant buds. Title: Aphids on tomato
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Aphids are highly reproductive insects that can cause structural weakening of plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid planting near aphid infested land or on land with a history of aphid infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Active removal of weeds from plots to reduce aphid hosts.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of alternative host species such as <i>Amaranthus</i>. Destroy by uprooting and burning or burying deep.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercropping with resistant species such as onion, garlic and parsley to reduce aphid populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Grow maize as a border around tomato field to attract flying aphids away from tomato crop.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitoring should be undertaken soon after crop emergence until crop harvest.<br/>-&nbsp;Regularly check for leaf curling and sticky residue on crops at least once a week.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe underside of leaves for aphid presence.<br/>-&nbsp;High levels of aphid infestation may result in the presence of black sooty mould due to honeydew secretions from aphids.<br/>-&nbsp;When monitoring crops, sample the most recently expanded leaves (4th or 5th leaf from the growing point) to give an estimate action threshold.<br/>-&nbsp;If there is no presence of aphid-transmitted viruses in the area, small aphid populations are tolerable amongst crop. If infestation grows (5-10 plants per quarter acre of field) then undertake direct control measures.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Prune leaves showing symptoms (curling, aphid populations on underside).<br/>-&nbsp;Removal and burning of infested crops to prevent spread of aphids to uninfested crops.<br/>-&nbsp;10 tablespoons of liquid soap per 10 litres of water. Spray plants every week in the evening until aphid population has gone (this treatment is only effective during wet weather). Avoid overuse of soap sprays as this will burn the plant.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil products once a week for 4 weeks (4.5 ml/10 m2). Contact your local agro-input supplier to organise access of such products.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Aphis</i> spp. <i>Myzus</i> spp.
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110767.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110768.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Larger grain borer on cassava
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;If pest is known to be found in your area, then remove all plant residue from previous harvest and burn.<br/>-&nbsp;Use clean and well ventilated storage facilities.<br/>-&nbsp;Leave cassava roots in the ground for as long as possible to reduce storage period and losses due to pest.<br/>-&nbsp;After harvesting cassava, sun dry the crop and transfer to sealed containers immediately.<br/>-&nbsp;Use suitable containers for storing crops (appropriately sealed to prevent access from pests), the insect can easily attack crop stored in bags.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor stored cassava weekly for damage (e.g. entry/exit holes from insect) and adults or larva. Infestation at low levels is not obvious, so monitoring should be done carefully.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for small beetles (3 - 4.5 mm) with a uniform dark brown-black body.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for exit holes in cassava and dust on the ground.<br/>-&nbsp;Install male-released aggregation pheromone traps in susceptible areas to monitor pest populations (at least 100 m away from crop/storage areas). Check traps regularly and replace the lure following the product label instructions. <br/>-&nbsp;Note: Pheromone traps will not work within storage areas as <i>P. truncatus</i> will not respond when on its food.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as grain borers are identified.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of biocontrol agent such as the predatory beetle <i>Teretrius nigrescens</i>. Contact your local government office to inquire about release in your area. <br/>-&nbsp;Use metal silos or similar storage options for crop, rather than bags and other easily-accessible materials for the insect to infest.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Prostephanus truncatus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110843.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110844.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;If pest is known to be found in your area, then remove all plant residue from previous harvest and burn.<br/>-&nbsp;Use clean and well ventilated storage facilities.<br/>-&nbsp;Leave cassava roots in the ground for as long as possible to reduce storage period and losses due to pest.<br/>-&nbsp;After harvesting cassava, sun dry the crop and transfer to sealed containers immediately.<br/>-&nbsp;Use suitable containers for storing crops (appropriately sealed to prevent access from pests), the insect can easily attack crop stored in bags.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor stored cassava weekly for damage (e.g. entry/exit holes from insect) and adults or larva. Title: Longtailed mealybug on cashew
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use planting materials with certified planting material to reduce spread of infestation into new fields.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid the use of broad spectrum pesticides to encourage natural enemies (lacewings, pirate bugs, lady beetles) and parasitoids (<i>Tetracnemoidea sydneyensis</i> or <i>T.peregrina</i>).<br/>-&nbsp;Collect any fallen leaves and plant material below cashew trees and destroy by burning to prevent the spread of mealybug pests.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for small, oval shaped insects with long tails (roughly a quarter of their body length) and a defined stripe running down the back.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for mealybugs between clusters of berries, on soft stems, flower buds, twigs, near the main root where soil is loose and the upper side of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms of mealybug infestations include delayed ripening, abnormal shapes and premature dropping of fruit. Sooty mould on leaf surfaces which can cause leaves to turn yellow and drop.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of yellow sticky traps with a pheromone lure to monitor for adults, follow product label for guidance.<br/>-&nbsp;Inspect plants anytime of day, monitor more frequently during dry periods.<br/>-&nbsp;As soon as mealybugs are identified in your fields, undertake direct control actions.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are observed.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use a strong jet of water to dislodge insects from plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Burn or bury (50 cm deep) any infested plant parts.<br/>-&nbsp;Prune highly infested plant areas such as stems or leaves and then destroy.<br/>-&nbsp;Control ant populations as they reduce natural predator populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of soap spray (one bar of soap in 20 L of water) to remove insect infestation from plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply 1-2% vegetable oil (e.g. neem oil) as a spray on plants (10 ml of liquid soap to 1 litre of water, add 50 ml of neem oil).<br/>-&nbsp;Paste a grease band (5 cm wide) on the main stem of the plant to prevent pests from crawling up to the leaves and fruit.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Pseudococcus longispinus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110849.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110850.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Use planting materials with certified planting material to reduce spread of infestation into new fields.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid the use of broad spectrum pesticides to encourage natural enemies (lacewings, pirate bugs, lady beetles) and parasitoids (<i>Tetracnemoidea sydneyensis</i> or <i>T.peregrina</i>).<br/>-&nbsp;Collect any fallen leaves and plant material below cashew trees and destroy by burning to prevent the spread of mealybug pests.<br/> -&nbsp;Observe for small, oval shaped insects with long tails (roughly a quarter of their body length) and a defined stripe running down the back.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for mealybugs between clusters of berries, on soft stems, flower buds, twigs, near the main root where soil is loose and the upper side of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms of mealybug infestations include delayed ripening, abnormal shapes and premature dropping of fruit. Sooty mould on leaf surfaces which can cause leaves to turn yellow and drop.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of yellow sticky traps with a pheromone lure to monitor for adults, follow product label for guidance.<br/>-&nbsp;Inspect plants anytime of day, monitor more frequently during dry periods.<br/>-&nbsp;As soon as mealybugs are identified in your fields, undertake direct control actions.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are observed.<br/> -&nbsp;Use a strong jet of water to dislodge insects from plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Burn or bury (50 cm deep) any infested plant parts.<br/>-&nbsp;Prune highly infested plant areas such as stems or leaves and then destroy.<br/>-&nbsp;Control ant populations as they reduce natural predator populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of soap spray (one bar of soap in 20 L of water) to remove insect infestation from plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply 1-2% vegetable oil (e.g. neem oil) as a spray on plants (10 ml of liquid soap to 1 litre of water, add 50 ml of neem oil).<br/>-&nbsp;Paste a grease band (5 cm wide) on the main stem of the plant to prevent pests from crawling up to the leaves and fruit.<br/> Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.

Title: Red-banded thrips on cashew
Authors:   Plantwise
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Thrips are tiny insects that cause damage to crop plants by feeding on the surface of the leaves and fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Establish windbreaks before orchard planting. <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain good cultural practices to increase plant vigour and enhance plant tolerance to thrip damage (sufficient fertilizer application, pruning, plant spacing etc.).<br/>-&nbsp;Keep the soil well irrigated, avoid excessive application of nitrogen fertilizers which may promote thrip populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies of <i>S. rubrocinctus</i> such as spiders, predatory mites, lacewings and predatory bugs (e.g. minute pirate bug) by avoiding the use of broad spectrum insecticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Prune trees to allow lighter conditions within the orchard (unfavourable conditions for thrips).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Plant parts attacked first show chlorotic spots and later turn to a silvery coloration. <br/>-&nbsp;Weekly, shake foliage/flowers over a white tray and observe for presence of nymphs with red bands on abdomen and black, elongated bodied adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Take note of clustered fruit, as low infestation levels show thrip preference to feed between clustered fruit rather than single fruit.<br/>-&nbsp;Sticky blue traps can be used to monitor the presence of thrips.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe plants for sooty mould, a symptom of thrip infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Population numbers are higher during the dry season and severe attacks can result in premature leaf drop, the inflorescences drying and the pseudofruit can even crack.<br/>-&nbsp;Take direct control actions before silvery leaves turn brown/appear burnt or when 4-6 adults are found per flower.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use pheromone lures in mass trappings, add a contaminant to kill trapped thrips.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of neem based products e.g. neem seed oil extract and Buprofezin or neem oil soap spray (check product label for dosage or 3 tablespoons of liquid soap per litre of water).<br/>-&nbsp;Use of biological pesticides e.g. <i>Metarhizum anisopliae</i> or <i>Beauveria bassiana</i> and follow instructions and dosage on the labels.<br/>
    Pesticides may be available to control this pest. Please check with the Ministry of Agriculture in your country to find out which pesticides are registered in your country and the local restrictions for their use.
Scientific Names: <i>Selenothrips rubrocinctus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110866.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110867.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110868.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Thrips are tiny insects that cause damage to crop plants by feeding on the surface of the leaves and fruits.<br/>-&nbsp;Establish windbreaks before orchard planting. <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain good cultural practices to increase plant vigour and enhance plant tolerance to thrip damage (sufficient fertilizer application, pruning, plant spacing etc.).<br/>-&nbsp;Keep the soil well irrigated, avoid excessive application of nitrogen fertilizers which may promote thrip populations.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies of <i>S. rubrocinctus</i> such as spiders, predatory mites, lacewings and Title: Bakanae disease of paddy
Authors:   Dr.Vishal Gupta Asstt. Professor (Sher-e-Kashmir University of Agriculture Sciences-Jammu) Sushil Kumar and Arun Khajuria( Plant Health Clinic Department of Agriculture Jammu)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Undertake deep summer ploughing to expose soil along with the pathogen to sunlight in order to reduce disease inoculum before puddling.<br/>-&nbsp;Use clean and healthy seeds to minimize disease occurrence.<br/>-&nbsp;Use 2% salt water to separate light weight and infected seeds during soaking.<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment before sowing and transplanting (see direct controls).<br/>-&nbsp;Apply recommended dose of urea, DAP and MOP as per soil health crd report; avoid excessive use of urea.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy crop residues after harvest.<br/>-&nbsp;Store grains with 13.5-14% moisture content.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Visit the field at weekly intervals in nurseries and after transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Be especially vigilant during periods of high temperature and high humidity as this favours disease development.<br/>-&nbsp;Infected plants are abnormally tall with pale, thin leaves, and produce fewer tillers.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for white growth of the pathogen at the base or on the lower sheath of the infected plant.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for adventitious roots growing from above-ground nodes on the stem.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for unhealthy seedlings drying from the bottom to top at early tillering stage which eventually die after few days.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Rogue out and destroy (burn or bury) infected or dead plants both from nursery and field as soon as identified.<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Trichoderma</i> spp. at 5 g/kg seed.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment by dipping 8kg seed in 10L of water containing 20g Carbendazim 50WP + 1g Streptocycline for 12hours.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>-&nbsp;Before transplanting dip the seedling in 0.2% solution of  Carbendazim 50 WP (2g/L water) for 6 hours.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Propiconazole 25EC at 0.1 per cet (I ml/L water) at boot stage  for seed crop.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class ll (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Mancozeb + Carbendazim at 2g/L water on apperance of disease.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Fusarium moniliforme</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110869.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110870.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

avoid excessive use of urea.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy crop residues after harvest.<br/>-&nbsp;Store grains with 13.5-14% moisture content.<br/> -&nbsp;Visit the field at weekly intervals in nurseries and after transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Be especially vigilant during periods of high temperature and high humidity as this favours disease development.<br/>-&nbsp;Infected plants are abnormally tall with pale, thin leaves, and produce fewer tillers.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for white growth of the pathogen at the base or on the lower sheath of the infected plant.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for adventitious roots growing from above-ground nodes on the stem.<br/>-&nbsp;Look for unhealthy seedlings drying from the bottom to top at early tillering stage which eventually die after few days.<br/> -&nbsp;Rogue out and destroy (burn or bury) infected or dead plants both from nursery and field as soon as identified.<br/>-&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Trichoderma</i> spp. at 5 g/kg seed.<br/> -&nbsp;Seed treatment by dipping 8kg seed in 10L of water containing 20g Carbendazim 50WP + 1g Streptocycline for 12hours.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>-&nbsp;Before transplanting dip the seedling in 0.2% solution of  Carbendazim 50 WP (2g/L water) for 6 hours.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Propiconazole 25EC at 0.1 per cet (I ml/L water) at boot stage  for seed crop.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class ll (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Mancozeb + Carbendazim at 2g/L water on apperance of disease.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>

Title: Brinjal Fruit and Shoot Borer
Authors:   Arun Khajuria
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep Summer Ploughing in May-June.<br/>-&nbsp;Early plant seedlings to avoid pest attack (Adjust time of Planting to late Feb/early March). <br/>-&nbsp;Use less susceptible varieties viz., PPL, PPC, Punjab Neelam and Punjab Barsati.<br/>-&nbsp;Sowing of coriander on ridges will encourage natural enemies.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow crop rotation using okra, tomato, cucubits, cruciferous vegetables or summer pulses.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid Monocropping if possible.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid the use of broad spectrum insecticides to promote natural enemies (such as predatory ants, ladybirg beetles, praying mantis and spiders).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Regularly monitor the crop to observe holes on leaf petioles, growing points of shoots or on fruits; as well as drying-up of terminal shoots.<br/>-&nbsp;Other symptoms of infestation include wilting of leaves, yield loss, weakened plant stems and poor fruit development.<br/>-&nbsp;Larvae can grow up to 155 mm long and are reddish coloured. Adults have a wingspan of 18-24 mm and have characteristic white wing patterns with a brown patch and black spots.<br/>-&nbsp;Use pheromone traps to observe the presence of moths; use 1-2 traps per acre placed above plant canopy. Action threshold is 3 moths per trap.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Clip and destroy infested shoots and fruits along with larvae twice a week; buried deep in the soil.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply neem cake at a rate of 100 kg/acre after 30 days of transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Installation of pheromomone traps 4-6 traps/acre for mass trapping of male moths. Change the lure after 15 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Release egg parasitoid <i>Trichogramma chilonis</i> or <i>Trichogramma pretiosum</i> at 10 days intervals of 50000-60000 per acre, once trap catch threshold reached.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem based insecticides viz., NSKE 5% or Neem oil at 3 ml/litre of water.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray B.t.var. kurstaki at 1-1.5 kg/Ha (e.g. Dipel).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use Personal Protection Equipment (PPE) while using Insecticides. <br/>-&nbsp;Follow pesticide rotation to avoid pest resistance.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Dipping of seedling in Imidacloprid for 3-4 hours at a rate of 1 ml per litre of water before transplanting.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Malathion 50EC at 2 ml/litre of water, or spinosad 240 SC during flowering.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class III (Slightly Hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Flubendamide 48SC or Chlorantraniliprole 18.5% at 0.5 ml/litre of water; or Emamectin benzoate 5% SG at a rate of 1 gm/ litre of water; or cartap hydrochloride 50%SP 3 gm/litre of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately Hazardous) apart from Chlorantraniliprole WHO Class -U (Unlikely to present acute hazards  in normal use)<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Leucinodes orbonalis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110871.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110872.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Deep Summer Ploughing in May-June.<br/>-&nbsp;Early plant seedlings to avoid pest attack (Adjust time of Planting to late Feb/early March). <br/>-&nbsp;Use less susceptible varieties viz., PPL, PPC, Punjab Neelam and Punjab Barsati.<br/>-&nbsp;Sowing of coriander on ridges will encourage natural enemies.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow crop rotation using okra, tomato, cucubits, cruciferous vegetables or summer pulses.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid Monocropping if possible.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid the use of broad spectrum insecticides to promote natural enemies (such as predatory ants, ladybirg beetles, praying mantis and spiders).<br/> -&nbsp;Regularly monitor the crop to observe holes on leaf petioles, growing points of shoots or on fruits; as well as drying-up of terminal shoots.<br/>-&nbsp;Other symptoms of infestation include wilting of leaves, yield loss, weakened plant stems and poor fruit development.<br/>-&nbsp;Larvae can grow up to 155 mm long and are reddish coloured. Title: Downy mildew of cucurbits
Authors:   Dr.Vishal Gupta Asstt. Professor (Sher-e-Kashmir University of Agriculture Sciences-Jammu) Sushil Kumar and Arun Khajuria( Plant Health Clinic Department of Agriculture Jammu)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Proper drainage conditions in the field should be maintained by raised bed planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Select sites with good air movement and provide adequate spacing between plants to allow air movement.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant crops earlier in the spring (late April) before downy mildew develops.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding overhead irrigation  to prevent leaf wetness.<br/>-&nbsp;Control alternate weed hosts (wild cucumber ) in neighbouring fence rows and field edges.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply recommended dose of urea, DAP and MOP for better soil fertility and crop growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider rotation using non-cucurbits crops such as okra and brinjal.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor the field at weekly intervals starting from the vegetative to fruiting stages.<br/>-&nbsp;Fungal development is most noticable during humid conditions (early mornings and following rainfall) on the underside of leaves. Some symtoms are more visible when leaves are wet. <br/>-&nbsp;Yellow spots of downy mildew, on the upper surface of a leaf; they are often angular and restricted by the leaf veins.<br/>-&nbsp;Look to see the purple-grey, downy or felt-like growth on the underside of the leaves where the spores form.<br/>-&nbsp;Pathogen infects the crop from April to August  and is more serious during the mid and later parts of the rainy season.<br/>-&nbsp;Severe infections results in necrosis of leaves and wilting.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Removal and destruction of highly infected lower leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Restrict the movement of water from infested areas to healthy areas.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Follow fungicide rotation to avoid disease resistance<br/>-&nbsp;Frequency of spray depends upon the disease intensity<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray crop with Metalaxyl 8% + Mancozeb 64% WP at 350- 500 gm per acre or 35-40 gm per pump (15 litre capacity).&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class Il. Spray at weekly interval during heavy disease infestation or at 15 days interval for moderate infestation<br/>-&nbsp;Spray crop with Cymoxanil 8% + Mancozeb 64% WP at 300 gm per acre or 30 gm per pump (15 litre capacity).&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class Il Spray at weekly interval during heavy disease infestation or at 15 days interval for moderate infestation<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Azoxystrobin 23 SC at 200 ml per acre or 15 ml per pump.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III; High risk for resistant development; Spray alternatively with contact fungicides (such as mancozeb);

Spray not more than 2 times in a season<br/>-&nbsp;.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application etc.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Pseudoperonospora cubensis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110873.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110874.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_110875.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Proper drainage conditions in the field should be maintained by raised bed planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Select sites with good air movement and provide adequate spacing between plants to allow air movement.<br/>-&nbsp;Plant crops earlier in the spring (late April) before downy mildew develops.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding overhead irrigation  to prevent leaf wetness.<br/>-&nbsp;Control alternate weed hosts (wild cucumber ) in neighbouring fence rows and field edges.<br/>-&nbsp;Apply recommended dose of urea, DAP and MOP for better soil fertility and crop growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider rotation using non-cucurbits crops such as okra and brinjal.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor the field at weekly intervals starting from the vegetative to fruiting stages.<br/>-&nbsp;Fungal development is most noticable during humid conditions (early mornings and following rainfall) on the underside of leaves.
