Title: Red Spider Mite on Jasmine
Authors:   Kanchana (NAF), Tamizhalarasan, Rajasekar, T.SunilKumar (NAF), D. Adhikari. Phone no: 9110550127 email: sriramamills@gmail.com


Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Provide intermittent irrigation   preferably once a week during the summer months (March to June)<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of alternate host & weeds like  <i>Tridaz procumbens</i> (Tamil Name: ).<br/>-&nbsp;Grow resistant varieties of Jasmine, i.e. Co-4.<br/>-&nbsp;Removal of infested plants from the field.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe in the evening during vegetative stages for yellowing & reddish leaves caused by mites sucking sap from the lower surface of the leaves. This should be done on a weekly basis.<br/>-&nbsp;Also look for drying, withering and the formation of silken webs on the plant.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for reddish mites on leaves with a hand lens.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Apply Pungam Oil<br/>-&nbsp;(<i>Pongamia glabra</i>) at 2ml / litre of water along with 100 gm of kadhi soap over foliage. 4 sprays at 15 day intervals.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray bioacaricide  <i>Hirsutella thompsonii</i> at 4 gm/lit of water during dawn hours.<br/>
    -&nbsp;When using a pesticide or botanical, always wear protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label, such as dosage, timing of application, pre-harvest interval, max number of sprays, restricted re-entry interval. Do not empty into drains and water sources.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Wettable Sulphur 50 WP at 2 gm/l of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Sulphur falls under WHO Class III (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;If the infestation is severe, spray Propargite 57% EC at 2 ml/l of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propargite falls under WHO Class III (slightly Hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Tetranychus cinnabarinus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_111450.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_111452.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_111453.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Paddy mites
Authors:   Dr.N. Vijayakumar, Ms.Girija
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Sowing in the month of early April. <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain Blackgram (Variety ADT 5), and cowpea as border crops to encourage multiplication of natural enemies like predatory mites, coccinellid beetles, anthocorid bugs, and staphylinid beetles<br/>
    -&nbsp;Observe for the occurrence of eggs, nymphs and adults on the lower surface of the leaves using a hand lens during hot summer and humid climate (May  June), Take immediate action.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for the development of intermittent red and yellow patches on the leaves and whitening of leaves.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Flood the nursery with water for about 15 minutes and then drain. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of 3% Neem oil @ 100ml/ 8 cents of nursery.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as Hand gloves, mask, Goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/>
    -&nbsp;There is no known direct control of Paddy mites.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Oligonychus oryzae</i> 
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_111454.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_111456.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Sowing in the month of early April. <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain Blackgram (Variety ADT 5), and cowpea as border crops to encourage multiplication of natural enemies like predatory mites, coccinellid beetles, anthocorid bugs, and staphylinid beetles<br/> -&nbsp;Observe for the occurrence of eggs, nymphs and adults on the lower surface of the leaves using a hand lens during hot summer and humid climate (May  June), Take immediate action.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for the development of intermittent red and yellow patches on the leaves and whitening of leaves.<br/> -&nbsp;Flood the nursery with water for about 15 minutes and then drain. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of 3% Neem oil @ 100ml/ 8 cents of nursery.<br/> -&nbsp;Use of personal protective equipment (PPEs) such as Hand gloves, mask, Goggles and keeping antidotes are mandatory by the spray applicators.<br/> -&nbsp;There is no known direct control of Paddy mites.<br/>

Title: Groundnut Aphid
Authors:   K.Bharathidasan, Sobana  Dominic and P.Senthilkumar, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Grow strong smelling repelling plants like onion and garlic as border crops. <br/>-&nbsp;Grow resistant varities such as Gimar-2, Jawahar Groundnut-3, Prutha, Kadiri-7 and Kadiri-8. <br/>-&nbsp;Remove alterrnate hosts such Cowpea and keep the field weed-free.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserving of natural enemies such as ladybird beetle, syrphids larvae, lace wing etc.<br/>-&nbsp;Use reflective mulches to repel invading populations of aphids.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Look at the leaves/stem for presence of ants, black shooty mold. Monitor from germination up to maturity once per week.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms of infestation include crinkling and motteling of newly emerged leaf, the presence of a sticky stubstance on leaves and ant colonies.<br/>-&nbsp;If aphids are found on 2-3 plants per 20-30 then consider direct control actions. If 4-10 pests are found per 20-30 plants then this is considered a severe infestation and chemical control is recommended.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Removal of affected twigs along with aphid colony at the early stage of growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Andrographis kashayam</i> botanical products at a rate of 10 ml per litre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1% Azadiractin at a rate of 300 ml per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of water with high speed which will manage aphids in sticking with plants. <br/>-&nbsp;Destruction of ant colonies with flooding of water. <br/>
    -&nbsp;When spraying the pesticides, Always use protective clothing and follow the instructions on the product label such as dosage, time of application.<br/>-&nbsp;Large quantities of pesticides will reduce natural enemies in the field.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of Fipronil 5% EC (e.g., trade name: RegentSC, Devigent plus, Fipro) at a rate of 300ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately Hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Imidachloropid 17.8% SL, (e.g., trade name: Confidor, ltimo) at a rate of 60 ml per acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (Moderately Hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying og Thiomethoxam 25% WG (e.g., trade name: Actara, Anant, Renova, Evident, Spike, Click) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by WHO.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Aphis craccivora</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113356.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113357.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Groundnut Bacterial Wilt 
Authors:   G.Sudhakar, G.Murugan  and K.Bharathidasan, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use disease-free seed material.<br/>-&nbsp;Undertake crop rotation with rice, maize, sorghum and pearl millet.<br/>-&nbsp;Early sowing before 30-45 days before normal date of sowing.         <br/>-&nbsp;Follow good field sanitation practices such as sufficient irrigation, as over-irrigating can increase the risk of spreading the bacteria.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Young plants remain with green leaves which leads to sudden wilting and death.<br/>-&nbsp;In mature plants leaves turn to light green with curling at the tip. <br/>-&nbsp;Dip the root in water to notice bacterial ooze coming from the cut end.<br/>-&nbsp;Dying branches often curl to form a "shepherd's crook".  <br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are found on crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Collect and destroy infected plant parts by burning.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Pseudomonas  fluorescens</i> at a rate of 1 kg per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Bacillus subtillus</i> at a rate of 800 g per acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Always use precautionary wearing of goggles and protective clothing.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of 2-Bromo-2-Nitro Propane (e.g., trade name: Bacterimycin, Bactrinashak) (immunomodulators) at a rate of 60 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified in WHO list.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 9% streptomycin sulphate + 1% Tetracyclie hydrochloride (e.g., trade name: Plantomycin) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified in WHO list.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Ralstonia solanacearum</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113358.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113359.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Use disease-free seed material.<br/>-&nbsp;Undertake crop rotation with rice, maize, sorghum and pearl millet.<br/>-&nbsp;Early sowing before 30-45 days before normal date of sowing.         <br/>-&nbsp;Follow good field sanitation practices such as sufficient irrigation, as over-irrigating can increase the risk of spreading the bacteria.<br/> -&nbsp;Young plants remain with green leaves which leads to sudden wilting and death.<br/>-&nbsp;In mature plants leaves turn to light green with curling at the tip. <br/>-&nbsp;Dip the root in water to notice bacterial ooze coming from the cut end.<br/>-&nbsp;Dying branches often curl to form a "shepherd's crook".  <br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are found on crops.<br/> -&nbsp;Collect and destroy infected plant parts by burning.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Pseudomonas  fluorescens</i> at a rate of 1 kg per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Bacillus subtillus</i> at a rate of 800 g per acre.<br/> -&nbsp;Always use precautionary wearing of goggles and protective clothing.<br/> -&nbsp;Spraying of 2-Bromo-2-Nitro Propane (e.g., trade name: Bacterimycin, Bactrinashak) (immunomodulators) at a rate of 60 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified in WHO list.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 9% streptomycin sulphate + 1% Tetracyclie hydrochloride (e.g., trade name: Plantomycin) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified in WHO list.<br/>

Title: Groundnut leaf miner
Authors:   S.Dhanasu ammal (MSSRF) and V.R.Saminathan (TNAU)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Sowing of resistant varieties such as TMV-2.<br/>-&nbsp;Early sowing within the season to avoid high levels of young crop damage by pests.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercroping with cow pea, pearl millet at a 4:1 ratio.<br/>-&nbsp;Sow trap crops like millet, castor and soybeans in borders.<br/>-&nbsp;Straw mulching within 10 days after germination.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with maize, cotton and sorghum.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain field sanitation and don't over-irrigate the field as this can lead to increased crop damage by pests.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops on a weekly basis during the growing season.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include brown blotch with webbing on leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;In severe infestation, burnt appearance of field may be seen. <br/>-&nbsp;Instalation of 1 light trap per acre to catch adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 8-10 plants show signs of infestation out of 100 randomly monitored crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Place pheromone traps at a rate of 5 nos per acre to catch egg laying adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Collection and destruction of egg masses and early instars larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1% Azadiractin (trade name: Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of chilli, ginger, garlic extract or 5 % Vitex leaf extract at a rate of 1 litre per acre. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resuregence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides, follow product label instructions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of Spinosad 40 %SC (e.g., trade name: Comfortis, Trifexis, Natroba.) at a rate of 60 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO III (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Profenofos 50% EC (e.g., trade name: Curacron,Profex,Profos) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Aproaerema modicella</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113362.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113363.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Sowing of resistant varieties such as TMV-2.<br/>-&nbsp;Early sowing within the season to avoid high levels of young crop damage by pests.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercroping with cow pea, pearl millet at a 4:1 ratio.<br/>-&nbsp;Sow trap crops like millet, castor and soybeans in borders.<br/>-&nbsp;Straw mulching within 10 days after germination.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with maize, cotton and sorghum.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain field sanitation and don't over-irrigate the field as this can lead to increased crop damage by pests.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor crops on a weekly basis during the growing season.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include brown blotch with webbing on leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;In severe infestation, burnt appearance of field may be seen. <br/>-&nbsp;Instalation of 1 light trap per acre to catch adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 8-10 plants show signs of infestation out of 100 randomly monitored crops.<br/> -&nbsp;Place pheromone traps at a rate of 5 nos per acre to catch egg laying adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Collection and destruction of egg masses and early instars larvae.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1% Azadiractin (trade name: Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of chilli, ginger, garlic extract or 5 % Vitex leaf extract at a rate of 1 litre per acre. <br/> -&nbsp;Avoid resuregence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides, follow product label instructions.<br/> -&nbsp;Spraying of Spinosad 40 %SC (e.g., trade name: Comfortis, Trifexis, Natroba.) at a rate of 60 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO III (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Profenofos 50% EC (e.g., trade name: Curacron,Profex,Profos) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>

Title: Groundnut  thrips
Authors:   N.Srithar, ICAR, KVK.,P.Senthilkumar, MSSRF, K.Bharathidasan, MSSRF  
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Raise five rows of maize densely as border crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of resistant varieties such as kadiri 3 and ICGS 86031.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid planting rows closer than 2 m to reduce pest movement.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain weed free field and field santation.<br/>-&nbsp;Use F20:F26 mulching sheet in between rows.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops for pest activity on a weekly basis during growing season.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include white patches on the upper surface of the leaves, nectrotic patches on the lower leaf surface and leaf crinkling.<br/>-&nbsp;Pest activity and presence increases during high temperatures with low rainfall.<br/>-&nbsp;The pest is known to transmit the virus for bud necrosis, hence monitor for symptoms of bud necrosis.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 3-5 thrips are found per plant.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Removal and destruction of severly affected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Set F20:F26up blue sticky trap at a rate of 5 traps per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil (3 litres per acre) or pungam oil (6 litres per acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of neem cake at a rate of 50 kg per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Forceful water spray once in 15 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1% azadiractin (trade name: Neemole,Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of verticillium lecani at a rate of 1 litre per acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides, follow product label instructions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray Thiomethaxom 25% WG (e.g., trade name: Actara, Anant, Renova, Evident, Spike, Click) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classfied by WHO.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Imidacloprid 17.8 SL (e.g., trade name: Confidor, ltimo) at a rate of 60 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II classified.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Fipronil 5% SC (e.g., trade name: RegentSC, Devigent plus, Fipro) at a rate of 300 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II classified.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Scirtothirps dorsalis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113364.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113365.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Raise five rows of maize densely as border crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Use of resistant varieties such as kadiri 3 and ICGS 86031.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid planting rows closer than 2 m to reduce pest movement.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain weed free field and field santation.<br/>-&nbsp;Use F20:F26 mulching sheet in between rows.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor crops for pest activity on a weekly basis during growing season.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include white patches on the upper surface of the leaves, nectrotic patches on the lower leaf surface and leaf crinkling.<br/>-&nbsp;Pest activity and presence increases during high temperatures with low rainfall.<br/>-&nbsp;The pest is known to transmit the virus for bud necrosis, hence monitor for symptoms of bud necrosis.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 3-5 thrips are found per plant.<br/> -&nbsp;Removal and destruction of severly affected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Set F20:F26up blue sticky trap at a rate of 5 traps per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil (3 litres per acre) or pungam oil (6 litres per acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of neem cake at a rate of 50 kg per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Forceful water spray once in 15 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1% azadiractin (trade name: Neemole,Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of verticillium lecani at a rate of 1 litre per acre.<br/> -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides, follow product label instructions.<br/> -&nbsp;Spray Thiomethaxom 25% WG (e.g., trade name: Actara, Anant, Renova, Evident, Spike, Click) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classfied by WHO.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Imidacloprid 17.8 SL (e.g., trade name: Confidor, ltimo) at a rate of 60 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II classified.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Fipronil 5% SC (e.g., trade name: RegentSC, Devigent plus, Fipro) at a rate of 300 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II classified.<br/>

Title: Paddy black bug 
Authors:   Mr.K. Bharathidasan and  Dr. M.Ayyamperumal 
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep summer ploughing to expose pupae to local predators and reduce pest presence during the growing season.<br/>-&nbsp;Synchronous planting of the same variety in endemic locations.<br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant varieties like CO-37.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain suitable filed sanitation. <br/>-&nbsp;Liberal application of farm yard manure (10 tonnes/acre) or Green Leaf manure (3 tonnes per acre). <br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with pulses.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve and encourage natural enemies like wasps, grasshoppers, ground beetles, spiders, crickets, red ants, coccinellid beetles, ducks and toads. Avoid using broad-spectrum pesticides as these can harm natural enemies of the pest.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops on a weekly basis for pests and signs of infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include brown discoloration of leaves, wounds and lesions present on leaves. <br/>-&nbsp;Affected crops may turn reddish brown or yellow in colour. <br/>-&nbsp;Scorched leaves in severe infestation (bugburn).<br/>-&nbsp;Bugs are more active during full moon week.<br/>-&nbsp;Installation of light traps (1 per acre) to catch adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions awhen 2-3 bugs are found per 10 randomly monitored crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Metarhizium anisopliae</i> or <i>Beauveria bassiana</i> at a rate of 800 g per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Breed ducks as they feed on black bugs.<br/>-&nbsp;Draining of water and spraying of neem oil 3% (6 litres per acre) on 30, 45 and 60 days after transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 200 ml of 0.05% soap solution (a mixture of 0.5 g all-purpose detergent in 1 litre of water). <br/>-&nbsp;Instalation of fish meal trap at a rate of 5 nos per acre. <br/>-&nbsp;Flooding the field periodically to drown the bugs.<br/>-&nbsp;During early infestation, raise the water level in the field for 23 days to force the insects to move upwards (more likely to be killed by natural enemies).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence insecticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides. Follow product label instructions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of Profenophos 50% EC (e.g., trade name: Curacron, Profex, Profos) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Carbosulfan 25% EC (e.g., trade name: Marshal, Aaatank, Aayudh) at a rate of 250 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Clothianidin 50% WDG (e.g., trade name: Dentotsu, Dantop) at a rate of 60 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by WHO.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Scotinophara lurida</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113370.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113371.img?width=800&height=640

Title: Mealybug in Paddy
Authors:   Dr.Raja.Ramesh, Asst. Prof. (Agrl. Entomology), Tamil Nadu Agricultural University & Mrs. Shobana Dominic, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Early transplanting to reduce mealybug pressure.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove grassy weeds which can harbor this insect.<br/>-&nbsp;Application of raw coir pith, raw sugarcane trash and farmyard manure to reduce infestations.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy ant colonies as ants are commonly found with mealybugs.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies like small encyrtid wasps, ladybird beetles, hover flies, Chrysoperla and spiders by avoiding broad-spectrum pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Ponding of irrigation water at 5 cm depth throughout the growing period.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops on a weekly basis during growing period. <br/>-&nbsp;Symtpoms include stunted growth, yellowing and curling of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Continuous monitoring in upland rice and rainfed cultivation. <br/>-&nbsp;Initial occurance at tender shoot of crop. Mealybugs feed by sucking the sap from tender shoots.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as pests are found.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Removal and destruction of affected plants.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1% Azadiractin at a rate of 400 ml per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of fish oil resin soap (25 g per litre). <br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals, follow product label instructions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Sparaying of Buprofezin 25% SC (e.g., trade name: Applaud, Flotis, Blunt) at a rate of 300 ml/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Sparaying of  Thiamethoxam 25% WG (e.g., trade name: Tafgor, Rogor, Rogorin) at a rate of 50 g/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Brevennia rehi</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113372.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113373.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Early transplanting to reduce mealybug pressure.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove grassy weeds which can harbor this insect.<br/>-&nbsp;Application of raw coir pith, raw sugarcane trash and farmyard manure to reduce infestations.<br/>-&nbsp;Destroy ant colonies as ants are commonly found with mealybugs.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enemies like small encyrtid wasps, ladybird beetles, hover flies, Chrysoperla and spiders by avoiding broad-spectrum pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Ponding of irrigation water at 5 cm depth throughout the growing period.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor crops on a weekly basis during growing period. <br/>-&nbsp;Symtpoms include stunted growth, yellowing and curling of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Continuous monitoring in upland rice and rainfed cultivation. <br/>-&nbsp;Initial occurance at tender shoot of crop. Title: Rice whorl maggot
Authors:   S. Dhanasu ammal (MSSRF) and V.R. Saminathan (TNAU)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Growing of resistance varieties such as IR 40.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow closer planting (20X20cm).<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain weed free field throughout the season.<br/>-&nbsp;In-situ growing of azolla 10 days after planting to cover the water surface of field. <br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct sowing rather than transplanting as this can lead to reduced pressure by pests.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops regularly, notably on a weekly basis during early growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Common symptoms include white or transparent patches and yellowish blocthing with pin holes on leaves and stem.<br/>-&nbsp;Other symptoms include drooping of young leaves, shrivelled plant, stunted growth, fragile stems and yellow spots on inner leaf margin.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 1-2 eggs per hill are found and chemical control when 15-30% leaf damage is observed.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Release of <i>Trichogramma</i> eggs (2 cc per acre) at weekly intervals. Follow product label instructions.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of neem cake (75 kg/acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 1 % azadiractin (e.g., trade name: Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml per acre. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides. Follow product label instructions for safe handling.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of Cartap hydrochloride 50% SP (e.g., trade name: Padan, Kirtap, Caldan,Boreg) at a rate of 400 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Profenofos 50% EC  (e.g., trade name: Curacron, Profos, Proud, Celeron) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Fipronil 5% SC (e.g., trade name: RegentSC, Devigent plus, Fipro) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Hydrellia philippina</i>

-&nbsp;Growing of resistance varieties such as IR 40.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow closer planting (20X20cm).<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain weed free field throughout the season.<br/>-&nbsp;In-situ growing of azolla 10 days after planting to cover the water surface of field. <br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct sowing rather than transplanting as this can lead to reduced pressure by pests.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor crops regularly, notably on a weekly basis during early growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Common symptoms include white or transparent patches and yellowish blocthing with pin holes on leaves and stem.<br/>-&nbsp;Other symptoms include drooping of young leaves, shrivelled plant, stunted growth, fragile stems and yellow spots on inner leaf margin.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 1-2 eggs per hill are found and chemical control when 15-30% leaf damage is observed.<br/> -&nbsp;Release of <i>Trichogramma</i> eggs (2 cc per acre) at weekly intervals. Title: Root knot nematode on rice
Authors:   N.Srithar, ICAR, KVK, Senthilkumar and Bharathidasan, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Continuous flooding in nursery.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with marygold, castor, cowpea, soybean, sesame and onion.<br/>-&nbsp;Adapt a two month fallow period in summer in a yearly crop plan.<br/>-&nbsp;Growing of <i>Eclipta alba</i> and incorporate in the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Selection of resistant varieties such as IR 32, TKM-6, Patnai, Monohar, Sali and Udaya.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil solarization with polythene sheets for three weeks (35-60C).<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with non-host crop such as groundnut and maize.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops regularly, notably on a weekly basis during growth periods.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include hooked-like gall on roots, distorted growth of young leaves, yellowing on young plants, premature flowering and formation of panicles.<br/>-&nbsp;Other symptoms include poorly filled grains in panicles and chlorosis of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are observed on crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Basal application of neem cake (80 kg per acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i>  (1 kg per acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>Trichoderma viride</i> or <i>Trichoderma harzianum</i> (1 kg per acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil applicaion of <i>Paecilomyces lilacinus</i> (3 kg per acre).<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence pesticide.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling pesticides, follow product label instructions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seedling dip with Carbosulfon 25% EC (e.g., trade name: Marshal, Aaatank, Aayudh) at a rate of 500 ml per acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of Catrap hydrochloride 4% G (e.g., trade name: Padan, Kirtap, Caldan, Boreg) at a rate of 8 kg  per acre, 35 days after transplanting. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of Fipronil 0.05% G (e.g., trade name: Reagent, Falcon) at a rate of 6 kg per acre, 35 days after transplanting. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Meloidogyne graminicola</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113376.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113377.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title:  Groundnut Leaf Hopper or Jassids
Authors:   G.Sudhakar, MSSRF, G.Murugan MSSRF and Bharathidasan K
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Grow resistant varieties such as Girnar-2, Durga, Harithandhra, Pratap Raj Mungphali, Prutha, Abhaya, Jawahar Groundnut-3, Kadiri-7, Kadiri-8 and Kalahasti.<br/>-&nbsp;Early sowing in the month of June to July or December to January.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with sorghum, maize or pearl millet.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercropping with pearl millet. <br/>-&nbsp;Grow okra as a trap crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Conservation of natural enemies like praying mantis, dragon flies and spiders by avoiding broad-spectrum pesticides and inecticides.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor crops weekly during the growing season, especially during dry periods.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include whitening of veins with chlorotic patches in the leaf.<br/>-&nbsp;Presence of nymphs and adult pest in the underside of the lower leaf.<br/>-&nbsp;Leaf tips may become necrotic in a typical  V-shape with presence of hopper burn symptoms.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 3-5 leafhoppers are found per plant out of 10 randomly monitoried crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of 5% neem seed kernal extract at a rate of 10 liters, or 1% Azadiractin at a rate of 250 ml per acre. <br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of pongam oil at a rate of 6 litres per acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear suitable protective clothing when handling pesticides, follow product label and guidelines.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment with Imidacloprid 70% WG (e.g., trade name: Admire, Katyayani,Ad-fyre) at a rate of  2g per kg of seeds.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Imidachlorpride 17.8% SL (e.g., trade name:Confidor, ltimo) at a rate of 80 ml per acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class II.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Thiamethoxam 25% WG (e.g., trade name:Actara, Anant, Renova,Evident, Spike,Click) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by WHO.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Diafenthiuron (e.g., trade name: Pegasus, Polo, Derby) 50% WP at a rate of 250 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO class III.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Empoasca kerri</i>

Title: Rice Brown Planthopper (BPH)
Authors:   Dr.M.Kandibane, Assistant Professor (Agrl.Ento.), PAJANCOA & RI, KARAIKAL, N.Srithar, Entomologist, ICAR KVK, Karur, TN
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use resistant varieties such as PY 3, CO 43,  PTB 21 and PTB33 in endemic areas.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove weeds from field bunds.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid close planting such as 15X10cm. Provide 30 cm rogue spacing at every 2.5 metres.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enenmies such  as Ladybird beetle, Wolf spider, wasp and avoid spraying of broad spectrum insecticides  <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid continuous stagnation of rain water during rainy season.<br/>-&nbsp;Transplanting in a east-west direction.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid excessive use of nitrogenous fertilizer and follow LCC based application.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid irrigation from field to field.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Install one light trap (yellow spectrum) per acre to monitor the incidences hoppers from 8.00-10.00 pm <br/>-&nbsp;Observe for hopper burn symptoms during rainy seasons.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for circuar patches of drying.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the stem base just above the water level for hoppers presence.<br/>-&nbsp;Presences of 3-5 nymphs as considered as ETL<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 3-5 nymphs are found or as soon as adults are identified. Also consider direct actions if hopper burn is found on crops.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Dislodge the hills to remove hoppers, catch in water and remove from field.<br/>-&nbsp;Drain the stagnated water from the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Azadirachtin 0.03% (Trade Name: eg. Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml/acre after the occurrence of early symptoms.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil at a rate of 6 litres/acre.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence-causing pesticides.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Direct the spray of Pymetrozine 50% WG (Trade Name: eg. Chess, Fullfill, Apply) at a rate of 60 g/acre towards the base of the plant.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by the WHO.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Buprofezin 25 % SC (Trade Name:eg. Banzo, Blunt, Buplon) at a rate of 400 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Thiamethoxam 25 % WG (Trade Name: eg. Actara, Click, Evident) at a rate of 50 g/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by the WHO.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Nilaparvata lugens</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113562.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113563.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Use resistant varieties such as PY 3, CO 43,  PTB 21 and PTB33 in endemic areas.<br/>-&nbsp;Remove weeds from field bunds.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid close planting such as 15X10cm. Provide 30 cm rogue spacing at every 2.5 metres.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserve natural enenmies such  as Ladybird beetle, Wolf spider, wasp and avoid spraying of broad spectrum insecticides  <br/>-&nbsp;Avoid continuous stagnation of rain water during rainy season.<br/>-&nbsp;Transplanting in a east-west direction.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid excessive use of nitrogenous fertilizer and follow LCC based application.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid irrigation from field to field.<br/> -&nbsp;Install one light trap (yellow spectrum) per acre to monitor the incidences hoppers from 8.00-10.00 pm <br/>-&nbsp;Observe for hopper burn symptoms during rainy seasons.<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for circuar patches of drying.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor the stem base just above the water level for hoppers presence.<br/>-&nbsp;Presences of 3-5 nymphs as considered as ETL<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 3-5 nymphs are found or as soon as adults are identified. Also consider direct actions if hopper burn is found on crops.<br/> -&nbsp;Dislodge the hills to remove hoppers, catch in water and remove from field.<br/>-&nbsp;Drain the stagnated water from the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Azadirachtin 0.03% (Trade Name: eg. Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml/acre after the occurrence of early symptoms.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray neem oil at a rate of 6 litres/acre.<br/> -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence-causing pesticides.<br/> -&nbsp;Direct the spray of Pymetrozine 50% WG (Trade Name: eg. Chess, Fullfill, Apply) at a rate of 60 g/acre towards the base of the plant.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by the WHO.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Buprofezin 25 % SC (Trade Name:eg. Banzo, Blunt, Buplon) at a rate of 400 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Thiamethoxam 25 % WG (Trade Name: eg. Actara, Click, Evident) at a rate of 50 g/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by the WHO.<br/>

Title: Chilli Thrips
Authors:   K.Bharathidasan, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Entomology, Annamalai University, Dr.Rettinassababady.C, Professor Plant Pathology, Dr.Mathiyazhagan, Asst. Professor, Tamil Nadu Agricultural University
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Crop rotation/intercrop with Agathi (<i>Sesbania grandiflora</i>) to act as a barrier for pests.

<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid chilli cropping after sorghum or following onion. Also avoid mixed cropping with sorghum and sugarcane.

<br/>-&nbsp;Intercrop chilli with tomato. Tomato crop is recommended as a trap crop with chilli since it is not prone to thrips.<br/>-&nbsp;Planting of resistant varieties, such as Pant C1, Pant C2, Dh-7-6-6, Jwala, Musalwadi, K-3435 and IC 24343.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor for upward curling of leaf margins and mottling appearance.<br/>-&nbsp;Severe damage is leaf distortion, defoliation, stunting, flower drop and dwarfing of plant<br/>-&nbsp;Place blue sticky traps @10  no's per acre.         

<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 3 nymphs or adults are found per infested leaf.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Foliar application of  5% NSKE (Neem Seed Kernal Extract) at a rate of 1 litre per acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Pongamia oil 1.6 litre/acre (foiliar means as spraying on leaves).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of  Neem oil at a rate of 2 litres per acre (foiliar means as spraying on leaves).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar sprays with 300 ml tobacco decoction and 350 ml fish oil resin soap per acre.  <br/>-&nbsp;Release of predatory mite <i>Amblyseius swirskii</i> at a rate of 25-100 mites per m.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence causing pesticides.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment with Imidacloprid at a rate of 10 g/kg of seeds. Seedling dips with Imidacloprid 17.8 SL (Trade Name: Confidor, Atom,Imida Gold) at a rate of 1.2 ml/litre of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Imidacloprid 17.8 %SL (Trade Name: eg. Confidor, Atom,Imida Gold) at a rate of 70 ml/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Thiamethoxam 25 %WG (Trade Name: Actara, Click, Evident) at a rate of 50 g/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Thiamethoxam is not listed in the WHO guide lines.<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Abamectin 1.8% EC (Trade Name: ABC, Vertimee, Abamectin) at a rate of 100 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Abamectin is not listed in the WHO guide lines.

<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar application of Buprofezin 10 %EC (Trade Name: Banzo, Blunt,Buplon, Appland) at a rate of 250 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class III (slightly hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Scirtothrips dorsalis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113564.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113565.img?width=800&height=640

Title: Downey mildew in cucurbits
Authors:   C.Amutha, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Plant pathology, K.Bharathidasan, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Entomology,   Faculty of Agriculture, Annamalai University and  P.Senthilkumar, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Pseudomonas</i> 10 gm per kg of seed.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoid water stagnation and provide good drainage.<br/>-&nbsp;Sowing in June-July as disease intensifies during August.<br/>-&nbsp;Greenhouse cultivation in endemic areas.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding excess irrigation.<br/>-&nbsp;Effective weed control and field sanitation.<br/>-&nbsp;Wash and sterilise farming tools after use and before moving to another field location.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>Trichoderma harzianum</i> (1 kg) and <i>Pseudomonas</i> (1 kg) along with 50 kg FYM per acre.  <br/>
    -&nbsp;During the wet season, observe for purple fungal growth on the lower surface of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Common symptoms include greasy and crispy appearance of leaves, yellow-brown angular spots and purple-grey downy growths.<br/>-&nbsp;Scouting every week during July-September for downy growth at upper surface of leaves.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are observed.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spray <i>Pseudomonas</i> (250 ml) or <i>Bacillus subtilis</i> (400 ml) per acre on foliage. Apply twice in 10 days intervals.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid spraying of resurgence-causing chemicals.<br/>-&nbsp;The fungicides mentioned in this guide are strictly to be applied before flowering and fruiting.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Spraying of Azoxystrobin 11% + Tebuconazole 18.3% (Trade Name:eg. Alliance, Spectrum, Raptor) at a rate of 300 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Azoxystrobin WHO U Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use.

Tebuconazole WHO II Moderately hazardous<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Chlorothalanil 75% WP (Trade name: eg. Kavach, Jatayu, Ishaan) at a rate of 200 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO U Unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Pseudoperonospora cubensis</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113566.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113567.img?width=800&height=640
Content:

Title: Earhead bug on rice
Authors:   Dr. V. R. Saminathan (TNAU), Dr. R. Ramesh (TNAU), Dr.  R. Rajkumar (MSSRF), P. Senthilkumar (MSSRF) and G. Suthagar (MSSRF)
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Removal of alternate hosts, especially graminaceous weeds like Kuthiraivali from field.<br/>-&nbsp;Selection of late-maturing cultivars like CR 1009 and tolerant varieties like TKM 9.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor the field every 2-3 days for signs of pest infestation.<br/>-&nbsp;Observie the elongated and slender bugs on inflorescence during the flowering to milky stagea of the crop.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 1 nymph or adult per hill is observed or when 10 insects per 20 hills are identified.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Application of KKM (Killikulam is a place were Agriculture Research Station is located) 10 D. The new KKM dust formulation consists of 10% of <i>Acorus calamus</i> rhizome powder and 90% of flash at a rate of 100 kg/acre.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray azadirachtin 0.03% (Trade Name: eg. Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 1litre per acre. <br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of 10% Notchi, Ipomoea or Prosopis leaf extract at a rate of 10 litres per acre. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid resurgence-causing pesticides.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Application of Phenthoate 50% EC (Trade Name: eg. Phendal, Salvo)  at a rate of 400 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (slightly hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Application of Buprofezin 25% EC (Trade Name: eg. Banzo, Blunt, Buplon) at a rate of 350 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO Class II (slightly hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Leptocorisa acuta</i> and <i>L. oratorius</i>

Content:

Title: Early shoot borer in sugarcane
Authors:   Mrs.Sobana Domanic, MSSRF, Dr.Arivudainambi.S Department of Entomology, Annamalai University
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Selection tolerent varieties such as recommended are CO 312, CO 421, CO 661, CO 917, CO 853, CO 86010, COC 98061 and COC 96061.<br/>-&nbsp;Plough well 4 to 6 times before planting to destroy crop residue and kill pupae.<br/>-&nbsp;Early season planting during december to February is ideal to avoid the pest damage.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserving moisture by trash (coir pith, dried trashes).

mulching to a thickness of 15cm along ridges between 3-15 days after planting reduces the larval population.<br/>-&nbsp;Earthing up 30 days after planting.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Scout fields at 10 day intervals during March to May to observe dead heart, egg masses and yellowish moths.<br/>-&nbsp;Keep trash traps (5 nos/acre) to attract adults and collect egg masses.<br/>-&nbsp;Use pheromone traps at a rate of 4 per acre for monitoring from 1-3 months of planting change the septa/lure once in 30 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions when 10 dead hearts are found per 100 randomly sampled plants.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Remove infested shoots close to ground level and burn to kill larvae and pupae.<br/>-&nbsp;On observing dead heart, spray Granulosis virus (GV) at a rate of 250 ml/acre (1x107 to 109 inclusion bodies per ml) 3 times at 15 days interval.<br/>-&nbsp;On observing dead heart, release Tachinid fly parasite, <i>Sturmiopsis inferens</i> at a rate of 50 gravid females/acre twice from 30th-50th day after planting.<br/>-&nbsp;On observing dead heart, release egg parasitoid, <i>Trichogramma chilonis</i> at a rate of 2 cc/acre from 30th day onwards 4 times at an interval of 15 days.<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Neem seed kernal extract 5% at a rate of 10 kg seed/acre on 30th and 60th.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid sesurgence-causing pesticides.<br/>
    -&nbsp;On observing dead heart, use Cartap hydrochloride 4G (Trade Name: eg. Padan, Kirtap, Caldan, Boreg) at a rate of 6 kg/acre as whorl application at 30th and 60th days.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Cartap hydrochloride. WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;On observing dead heart, use Fipronil 0.3%G (Trade Name: eg. Regent Gr, Task Gr, Agadi-G) at a rate of 10 kg/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Fipronil. WHO Class II (Moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;On observing dead heart, spray Chlorantroniliprole 18.5% SC (Trade Name: eg. Coragen, Rynaxpyr, Corer) at a rate of 60 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorantroniliprole. WHO Class U (unlikely to present acute hazard in normal use).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Chilo infuscatellus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113569.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113570.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Selection tolerent varieties such as recommended are CO 312, CO 421, CO 661, CO 917, CO 853, CO 86010, COC 98061 and COC 96061.<br/>-&nbsp;Plough well 4 to 6 times before planting to destroy crop residue and kill pupae.<br/>-&nbsp;Early season planting during december to February is ideal to avoid the pest damage.<br/>-&nbsp;Conserving moisture by trash (coir pith, dried trashes).

Title: False smut in rice
Authors:   Dr.S.Mathiyazhagan, Asst. Professor, TNAU, K.Bharathidasan, Research Scholar, Dept. of Entomology, Annamalai University
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use resistant variety (ADT 39, TRY 3, PY 4 (Jawahar), Moderately resistant  (CORH4) Tolerent variety (RMD (R)1) <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain a spacing of 20 cm x 20 cm (between the rows as well as plant within a row).<br/>-&nbsp;Application of potash (5 kg/acre) at tillering stage as additional dose<br/>-&nbsp;Irrigation management to reduce humidity as disease is more prevalent under high humidity.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow alternate wetting and drying method of irrigation during pannicle iniation and grain formation stage<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with pulses (blackgram/greengram)<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitoring for fungal deposit during Rainfall and cloudy weather at  flowering and maturity periods induce the disease<br/>-&nbsp;Regular observation of panicle from milky stage to maturity stage<br/>-&nbsp;Monitoring for the individual rice grain transformed into a mass of yellow fruiting bodies to the size of 1cm.<br/>-&nbsp;Common symptoms include the development of yellow smut balls which turn black.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are found.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Wet seed treatment with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> at a rate of 10 g (talc) or 2 ml (liquid)/kg of seeds in one litre of water. <br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spray of <i>P. fluorescens</i> at a rate of 1 kg or 1 litre/acre 3 times at 10 day intervals commencing from 45 days after transplanting.  <br/>-&nbsp;Seedling root dip for 30 minutes with <i>P. fluorescens<> at a rate of 200 ml or 1kg /acre dissolved in 40 litres of water.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of<i>P.fluorescens</i> at a rateof 1 kg/acre mixed with 25 kg of decomposed FYM after 30 days of transplanting.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals. <br/>
    -&nbsp;In severe incidence spray Copper hydroxide 77 % WP (Trade Name: eg. Blue Shield DF, Kocide, Parikh) at a rate of 250 g/acre twice at boot leaf and 50 % flowering stage.  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Copper hydroxide. WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Prophylatic spray of Propiconazole 25% EC (Trade name: eg. Qnash, Zerox, Tilt, Dhan) at a rate of 200 ml/acre twice at boot leaf and 50% flowering stage. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole 25 % EC. WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Ustilaginoidea virens</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113571.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113572.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Use resistant variety (ADT 39, TRY 3, PY 4 (Jawahar), Moderately resistant  (CORH4) Tolerent variety (RMD (R)1) <br/>-&nbsp;Maintain a spacing of 20 cm x 20 cm (between the rows as well as plant within a row).<br/>-&nbsp;Application of potash (5 kg/acre) at tillering stage as additional dose<br/>-&nbsp;Irrigation management to reduce humidity as disease is more prevalent under high humidity.<br/>-&nbsp;Follow alternate wetting and drying method of irrigation during pannicle iniation and grain formation stage<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with pulses (blackgram/greengram)<br/> -&nbsp;Monitoring for fungal deposit during Rainfall and cloudy weather at  flowering and maturity periods induce the disease<br/>-&nbsp;Regular observation of panicle from milky stage to maturity stage<br/>-&nbsp;Monitoring for the individual rice grain transformed into a mass of yellow fruiting bodies to the size of 1cm.<br/>-&nbsp;Common symptoms include the development of yellow smut balls which turn black.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are found.<br/> -&nbsp;Wet seed treatment with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> at a rate of 10 g (talc) or 2 ml (liquid)/kg of seeds in one litre of water. <br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spray of <i>P. fluorescens</i> at a rate of 1 kg or 1 litre/acre 3 times at 10 day intervals commencing from 45 days after transplanting.  <br/>-&nbsp;Seedling root dip for 30 minutes with <i>P. fluorescens<> at a rate of 200 ml or 1kg /acre dissolved in 40 litres of water.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of<i>P.fluorescens</i> at a rateof 1 kg/acre mixed with 25 kg of decomposed FYM after 30 days of transplanting.<br/> -&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals. <br/> -&nbsp;In severe incidence spray Copper hydroxide 77 % WP (Trade Name: eg. Blue Shield DF, Kocide, Parikh) at a rate of 250 g/acre twice at boot leaf and 50 % flowering stage.  .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Copper hydroxide. WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Prophylatic spray of Propiconazole 25% EC (Trade name: eg. Qnash, Zerox, Tilt, Dhan) at a rate of 200 ml/acre twice at boot leaf and 50% flowering stage. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole 25 % EC. WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>

Title: Sheath rot in rice
Authors:   Dr.Mathiyazhagan, Asst. Professor, Tamil Nadu Agricultural University, Dr.Rettinassababady.C, Professor Plant Pathology, PAJANCO, K.Bharathidasan, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Entomology, Annamalai University,  and S.Dhanasu Ammal, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Use disease-free certified seeds. <br/>-&nbsp;Use resistant variety (ADT 39, TRY 3, PY 4 (Jawahar), moderately resistant  (CORH4), tolerent variety (RMD (R)1).    <br/>-&nbsp;Plant spacing of 20 cm between rows can reduce the disease. Closer planting may intensify and spread the dieases. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of potash (5 kg/acre) at tillering stage as additional dose. During tillering stage an additional dose of 5 kg of potacium per acre should be applied. <br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with pulses (blackgram/greengram).<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain field sanitation.<br/>
    -&nbsp;If temperatures of 20-280C coincide with 85% relative humidity during panicle initiation to booting stage follow intensive monitoring.<br/>-&nbsp;Regular observations of leaf sheath enclosing the panicle for grey spot with brown margin during paincle formation stage to booting stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Regular observation of white powdery growth inside the flag leaf during panicle formation stage to booting stage.<br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for the presence of plant hoppers and mealybug as they could spread the disease.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as symptoms are observed.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Wet seed treatment with <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> at a rate of 10 g (talc) or 2 ml (liquid)/kg of seeds in one litre of water before sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;Seedling root dip for 30 minutes with <i>P.fluorescens</i> at a rate of 200 ml or 1 kg /acre dissolved in 40 litres of water before transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of<i>P.fluorescens</i> at a rateof 1 kg/acre mixed with 25 kg of decomposed FYM after 30 days of transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spray of <i>P.fluorescens</i> at a rate of 1 kg or 1 litre/acre 3 times at 10 day intervals commencing from 45 days after transplanting. Repeated 55 and 65 days after transplanting.<br/>-&nbsp;Prophylactic foliar spraying of Neem Seed Kernal Extract at a rate of 5% (10 kg/acre) during tillering stage. Repeated 55 days after sowing.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Always use protective clothing when handling chemicals.<br/>
    -&nbsp;In severe incidence spray Hexaconazole 5% EC (Trade name: eg. Contaf, Force, Conquer) at a rate of 400 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Hexaconazole - WHO class III (slightely hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Propiconazole 25% EC  (Trade name: eg. Qnash, Zerox, Tilt, Dhan) at a rate of 200 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole 25 % EC - WHO class II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spray Chlorothalonil 75 % WP (Trade name: eg. Kavach, Jatayu, Ishaan) a ta rate of 400 g/acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorothalonil  - WHO Class U<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Sarocladium oryzae</i> (Formly classified as <i>Acrocylindrium oryzae</i>)
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113573.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113574.img?width=800&height=640

Closer planting may intensify and spread the dieases. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of potash (5 kg/acre) at tillering stage as additional dose. Title: Stem rot in Groundnut
Authors:   C.Amutha, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Plant pathology, K.Bharathidasan, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Entomology,   Faculty of Agriculture, Annamalai University and  P.Senthilkumar, MSSRF
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep ploughing during summer.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with cereal crops (Paddy-groundnut/Maize-Groundnut is followed in a cropping year).









<br/>-&nbsp;Effective weed control and field sanitation.<br/>-&nbsp;Polythene mulching at soil surface.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding accumulation and dumping of organic debris.<br/>-&nbsp;Deep burial of previous crops plant debris before sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;

Sowing in raised beds or in broad bed furrows<br/>
    -&nbsp;Regular scouting during the rainy season.



<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for fan shaped mycelium growth at the lower stem.<br/>-&nbsp;Leaves turn yellow followed by wilting of branches.<br/>-&nbsp;Disease is evident at 45-60 days after seedling emergence, strict monitoring for infestation during this period.<br/>-&nbsp;Yellowing of leaf and wilting of branches is considered as trigger to adopt the direct control measures.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Trichoderma viridie</i> at a rate of 4 g per kg of seeds.





<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>Trichoderma viride</i> at a rate of 2 kg per acre mixed with 20 kg of FYM.<br/>-&nbsp;Periodical collection of infested plant debris and burning.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment with Tebuconazole 2 DS (Trdae name: eg. Folicur, Torque, Mirage) at a rate of 2 ml per kg of seed.



.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Tebuconazole - WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spraying of Hexaconazole 5 % EC (Trade Name: eg. Contaf Plus, Trigger) at a rate of 250 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Hexaconazole - WHO III (slightely hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spraying of Propiconazole 25% EC (Trade name: eg. Qnash, Zerox, Tilt, Dhan) at a rate of 250 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Propiconazole-WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spraying of Chlorothalanil 75% WP (Trade name: eg. Kavach, Jatayu, Ishaan) at a rate of 300 g per acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Chlorothalanil - WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Foliar spraying of Triademefon 25% WP (Trade Name:eg Bayleton, Beeltone, Krileton) at a rate of 200 g per acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Triademefon -WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Athelia rolfsii</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113575.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113576.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Deep ploughing during summer.<br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with cereal crops (Paddy-groundnut/Maize-Groundnut is followed in a cropping year).









<br/>-&nbsp;Effective weed control and field sanitation.<br/>-&nbsp;Polythene mulching at soil surface.<br/>-&nbsp;Avoiding accumulation and dumping of organic debris.<br/>-&nbsp;Deep burial of previous crops plant debris before sowing.<br/>-&nbsp;

Sowing in raised beds or in broad bed furrows<br/> -&nbsp;Regular scouting during the rainy season.



<br/>-&nbsp;Observe for fan shaped mycelium growth at the lower stem.<br/>-&nbsp;Leaves turn yellow followed by wilting of branches.<br/>-&nbsp;Disease is evident at 45-60 days after seedling emergence, strict monitoring for infestation during this period.<br/>-&nbsp;Yellowing of leaf and wilting of branches is considered as trigger to adopt the direct control measures.<br/> -&nbsp;Seed treatment with <i>Trichoderma viridie</i> at a rate of 4 g per kg of seeds.





<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>Trichoderma viride</i> at a rate of 2 kg per acre mixed with 20 kg of FYM.<br/>-&nbsp;Periodical collection of infested plant debris and burning.<br/> -&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals.<br/> -&nbsp;Seed treatment with Tebuconazole 2 DS (Trdae name: eg. Title: Termites on sugarcane and cassava
Authors:   K.Bharathidasan, Ph.D Research Scholar, Dept. of Entomology, Annamalai University, Dr.Rettinassababady.C, Professor 

Plant Pathology, Dr.Mathiyazhagan, Asst. Professor, TNAU
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Deep ploughing with a chisel plough.<br/>-&nbsp;Flooding the field before planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Locate the termite mounds/termitarium and destroy colonies.<br/>-&nbsp;Reduction of size of field bund. Maintain the width of field bund at 30 cm.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain suitable field sanitation.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Monitor for termite mounds during dry weather periods.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include semi-circular feeding marks on the margin of the leaves, damage to canopies and drying of central shoots.<br/>-&nbsp;15% of dried central shoot is considered a trigger to action the direct control recommendations. <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for the presence of loose soil, deposits of pressed mud and movement of worker temites.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Collection and destruction of the termite affected setts from the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Pour the juice of immature papaya fruit on termite mounds (100 ml of papaya juice dissolved in 5 litres of water per mound). <br/>-&nbsp;Mixing of botanicals consist of Calatropis and Kheemp at a rate of 5 litres per acre in irrigation channels.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> at a rate of 10 g per litre or spraying of <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> 5 ml per litre of water.       <br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Metarrhizium anisopliae</i> 2 grams per litre on termite mounds.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> 5 ml per litre of water on the termite mounds and also on the infected root portions.       

<br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid spraying of resurgence causing insecticide.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Pouring of Imidacloprid 17.8%SL (Trade Name: eg. Confidor, Atom, Imida Gold) 1 ml/litre into the mounds.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Imidacloprid - WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Dip the setts in Imidacloprid 70WS (Trade Name: eg. Gaucho 70 WS, Chemida70WS) 1 ml per litre of water.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Imidacloprid - WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Sprayig of Fipronil 5% SC (Trade Name: eg. RegentSC, Devigent plus, Fipro) at a rate of 350 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Fipronil - WHO II (moderately hazardous)<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Imidacloprid 17.8%SL (Trade Name: eg.Confidor, Atom, Imida Gold) at a rate of 100 ml/acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Imidacloprid - WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Thiamethoxam 25% WG (Trade Name: eg. Actara, Click, Evident) at a rate of 50 g per acre. .&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not listed in the WHO guidelines.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Odontotermes obesus</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113577.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_113578.img?width=800&height=640
Content:
-&nbsp;Deep ploughing with a chisel plough.<br/>-&nbsp;Flooding the field before planting.<br/>-&nbsp;Locate the termite mounds/termitarium and destroy colonies.<br/>-&nbsp;Reduction of size of field bund. Maintain the width of field bund at 30 cm.<br/>-&nbsp;Maintain suitable field sanitation.<br/> -&nbsp;Monitor for termite mounds during dry weather periods.<br/>-&nbsp;Symptoms include semi-circular feeding marks on the margin of the leaves, damage to canopies and drying of central shoots.<br/>-&nbsp;15% of dried central shoot is considered a trigger to action the direct control recommendations. <br/>-&nbsp;Monitor for the presence of loose soil, deposits of pressed mud and movement of worker temites.<br/> -&nbsp;Collection and destruction of the termite affected setts from the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Pour the juice of immature papaya fruit on termite mounds (100 ml of papaya juice dissolved in 5 litres of water per mound). <br/>-&nbsp;Mixing of botanicals consist of Calatropis and Kheemp at a rate of 5 litres per acre in irrigation channels.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Pseudomonas fluorescens</i> at a rate of 10 g per litre or spraying of <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> 5 ml per litre of water.       <br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Metarrhizium anisopliae</i> 2 grams per litre on termite mounds.<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of <i>Bacillus thuringiensis</i> 5 ml per litre of water on the termite mounds and also on the infected root portions.

Title: Groundnut Whitegrub 
Authors:   Dr. M.Ayyamperumal and Mr.K. Bharathidasan
Editors: 
Sections:
    -&nbsp;Undertake deep summer ploughing. <br/>-&nbsp;Application of enriched farm yard manure (1 tonne per acre). <br/>-&nbsp;Crop rotation with sorghum, bajara or cotton.<br/>-&nbsp;Early sowing i.e. 30 days prior to normal sowing dates.<br/>-&nbsp;Trim off trees and shrubs in and around the field to reduce suitable habitat for pest and therefore pest migration into the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercrop with onion and garlic.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Symptoms include pale, wilted plants dying in patches and stunted growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Installation of 1 light trap per acre to catch and help monitor adult beetles. <br/>-&nbsp;Place five pheromone (synthetic pheromone-Anisole) traps per acre to monitor for adults.<br/>-&nbsp;Consider direct control actions as soon as the pest is found, as the effective way to protect crops is prevention.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Soil application of castor or neem cake (60 kg per acre).<br/>-&nbsp;Collection and destruction of white grub adults from host trees around the field e.g. neem and acacia.<br/>-&nbsp;Soil application of <i>Beauveria brongniartii</i> or <i>Metarhizium anisopliae</i> (Trade Name: Bio-Magic, Biomet, Metarhizium) at a rate of 800 g/acre. <br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Azadirachtin 0.03% (Trade Name: Neemole, Neemten, Azatin) at a rate of 400 ml/acre. <br/>
    -&nbsp;Avoid Resurgence causing pesticides.<br/>-&nbsp;Always wear protective clothing when handling chemicals, follow product label instructions.<br/>
    -&nbsp;Seed treatment with Imidacloprid 70% WG (e.g., trade name: Admire, DAWN 7000, Looper) at a rate of 2g/kg seed.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Cartap Hydrochloride 50% SP  (e.g., trade name: Caldan, Padan, Kirtap, Boregan)  at a rate of 350 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Fipronil 5% SC (e.g., trade name: Regent SC, Devigent plus, Fipro) at a rate of 400 ml per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;WHO II (moderately hazardous).<br/>-&nbsp;Spraying of Thiamethoxam 25% WG (e.g., trade name: Actara, Anant, Renova, Evident, Spike, Click) at a rate of 50 g per acre.&nbsp;General Restrictions:&nbsp;Not classified by the WHO.<br/>
Scientific Names: <i>Holotrichia consanguinea</i>
Images: ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_115327.img?width=800&height=640, ../../../../content/img/resize/PMDG_115328.img?width=800&height=640

30 days prior to normal sowing dates.<br/>-&nbsp;Trim off trees and shrubs in and around the field to reduce suitable habitat for pest and therefore pest migration into the field.<br/>-&nbsp;Intercrop with onion and garlic.<br/> -&nbsp;Symptoms include pale, wilted plants dying in patches and stunted growth.<br/>-&nbsp;Installation of 1 light trap per acre to catch and help monitor adult beetles.
